## 1

INTRODUCTION REASONS WHY FISH

FARMS DON'T SUCCEED

1.1 INTRODUCTION OF AQUACULTURE IN NIGERIA

1.2 REASONS WHY FISH FARMS DON'T SUCCEED

## 1.1 INTRODUCTION OF AQUACULTURE IN NIGERIA

Aquaculture is the production of aquatic organisms such as shrimps, fish, shellfish

and seaweeds. In Nigeria however, aquaculture is almost limited to fish farming only.

The species which are suitable to farm in Nigeria, are limited too. Depending on the biology of the species, market, availability of seed and suitable feeds, I consider three species to be feasible for farming in Nigeria: African catfish (Clarias gariepinus), Tilapia (Oreochromis niloticus) and Carp (Cyprinus carpio). From these three species the vast

majority of the production is of African catfish also called the walking catfish or barbel,

the local name in South Africa. In this handbook I only focus on the production of African catfish, because it has a wide acceptance in Nigeria, it grows very quickly and it can be economically farmed in small scale enterprises with relatively low investments. On the African continent fish farming is not widespread. There are only two countries

which really have developed fish farming: Egypt and Nigeria. Egypt is mainly focusing

on tilapia production and Nigeria is mainly focusing on African catfish production.

In the early days after the Nigerian independence, 'fish farming' and 'fishing' were mixed up terms, but they have a totally different meaning. Fish farming is done in a controlled water body, fish are stocked and fed deliberately. After a growing period,

the fish are harvested in a controlled manner to easily crop the fish. Fishing is catching

fish in natural water bodies with seine nets, fish traps, angling and other fishing equipment. What is caught is always a surprise. The term 'fisheries' is actually covering both activities.

In the early seventies the first pioneers started with real fish farming, driven by a

growing population and increased prices for fish. They however faced a serious problem: the know-how for fish farming was not available and good quality feeds and seeds were very scarce.

In the eighties fish farming started to change through the introduction of new farming

techniques, which resulted in increased fingerling production of catfish, and the

introduction of imported starter feed.

In the nineties fish farming really started to boom and the RAS (recirculation aquaculture system) was introduced. This system is highly intensive and does not need

much space. You actually can farm successfully in the middle of town. The awareness

of fish farming increased exponentially and already a thousand fish farmers had started their own farm. However, in the rush of starting, many farmers stopped their farming activities as fast as they had started them and lost a lot of money. Till today we see many newcomers, and still many of them end up disappointed and leave this volatile

agribusiness. This handbook is hopefully a tool for anybody who wants to start a fish

## 100

introduction

farm, and an inspiration to gain the knowledge to get started on a solid foundation,

so there will be no drop out.

That is why this book is full of examples, formats and calculations. I realise that the

prices of materials, fish feeds, fish, energy and other costs will fluctuate in time and location. That doesn't mean that the book will be outdated in the years to come, because the formulas used in this book are universal. You can just fill in the current prices to get a customized outcome and draw actual conclusions.

After the millennium the government positively interfered in the Agric sector. Agric loans were developed with single digit interest rates. However only big companies and companies which are well connected to the banks, were benefiting from those loans. Also, imported agric equipment, including for fish farming, can be imported duty-free.

There are restrictions on the import of frozen fish and importers cannot acquire CBN

## import of frozen fish and importers cannot acquire CBN

funds for importation of frozen fish. The import of frozen tilapia and frozen catfish is completely forbidden, however frozen tilapia is still dripping in via The Republic of Benin. All this has stimulated the growth of fish farming in Nigeria. Nowadays frozen fish is very expensive.

The present administration takes diversification of the economy very seriously and is

concentrating on the agric sector being a sector that can absorb a lot of unemployed youth and increase the sustainability of the food supply for the untamed growing population. population.

The government has created a good platform for the fish industry and multinationals

have come to Nigeria to invest heavily in commercial state-of-the-art feed mills.

Catfish farming can be carried out in almost any state of the country. Claiming this, the production of catfish is actually primarily based in the south west of Nigeria (Figure 1). The Northern states have less water available, whereas some states, such as

Taraba State (highland) and Plateau State, have enough water, but the climate is too

cold for profitable catfish farming. The east and south-south are provided with good

opportunities to farm fish but are not so developed yet.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_006.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

MAP RANKING STATES IN NIGERIA WITH HIGHEST PRODUCTION OF CATFISH

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_007.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 1. The ranking of states based on the level of catfish production.

Nigeria is blessed with a lot of water bodies: 264 medium and large dams with a combined storage capacity of 33 billion cubic metres of water. The dams can be used for pumping water into the fish farms or for direct farming by putting cages in the dam.

The demand for fish in Nigeria is around 7 kg/capita per year, but the recommended

rate is 12 kg/capita per year. Fish production in Nigeria is hovering around 200, 000 tons; the domestic catch is 450, 000 tons, the remaining fish, which forms the bulk, is still imported.

## 1.2 REASONS WHY FISH FARMS DON'T SUCCEED

First of all, fish farms shouldn't fail because there is no market for catfish. The market

for catfish is big and still growing, although in some areas they produce a lot of catfish

but they don't eat as much. So, they are marketing it to other areas in the country. For

introduction

example, in the Ibadan region a lot of fish is produced and transported to Abuja and Lagos by road. Marketing is part of the business and if totally neglected, it will result in very low sales prices. This makes it difficult to make a profit. Therefore, fish farms

should have a regular supply of fish to be able to satisfy the customer on a regular

basis. However, some farms sell their produced fish only two or three times a year. In this way you cannot build any customer relationship! In general, small producers have more problems selling their fish than the big producers.

## The location is not appropriate for fish production

Many fish farmers underestimate the water consumption. Their conception is to fill the tanks and keep them full from growth cycle till harvest. It's not like that; read chapter 3 for more information. In order to keep the water quality within acceptable levels, you have to flush on a daily basis, preferably 24/7 and even increase it as the fish are

gaining weight. Using boreholes for grow-out, which is the last stage of the growth

cycle, is in many areas of Nigeria not really profitable for medium and large-scale production. production.

A borehole can work only on a small scale, and the production is limited to only 1000 kg per month. Of course, there are always exceptions. In the region of Benin City, you

will see good working boreholes with very large capacity (20 - 30 mkg per month. Of course, there are always exceptions. In the region of Benin City, you 3 per hour) and

clean water. Normally the supply of water should come from a river, stream or dam will see good working boreholes with very large capacity (20 - 30 m$ 3 $ per hour) and

clean water. Normally the supply of water should come from a river, stream or dam with availability of water throughout the year.

with availability of water throughout the year.

Some farms are based so far away from civilisation, that it is a challenge to get there.

Customers will be discouraged to come and buy fish in such an area.

The roads are very bad, security is almost absent and no infrastructure is available.

Some fish farms are not equipped with any way to drain water out of the farm. This isthe same misconception as not having any water to flush, because of the perception the perception

that the ponds must be kept full. Solutions to drain the water into the soil cannot work

because soon you will have a lagoon on your land. If you by all means want to drain onto your property, you will need 1000 $ m_{22} $ for each ton/annum of production. For a production of 50 tons per annum, this is already 5 ha of land.

If your farm is located far from residential areas, you will have to provide good

accommodation for key staff. If you do not, the staff will not be comfortable to work, and you won't get good staff with dedication and motivation. Most investors don't wantand you won't

get good staff with dedication and motivation. Most investors don't want to invest in accommodation because it's not related to production. Accommodation is something which will be implemented if profit is made. But for staff to suffer staff to suffer and stay

24/7 on the farm is not realistic. You will end up having no results at all.

## Chapter 1

Lack of knowledge, bad consultancy

In the land of the blind, the one-eyed man is king. So, I was invited by an investor to visit his farm in Nasarawa State (Nigeria). After a lot of work to build his fish farm, he was starting to feel uncomfortable about the set up. Indeed, he should feel uncomfortable because when I arrived at his farm, I was shocked about what

had been done so far. To describe the situation of what I saw there; four holes in

the ground, each with a mega size of around 3000 m $ ^{2} $ and at least four metres deep. No inlets, no outlets, no drainage system, no water supply. "But we have drilled two boreholes and I was told they can supply the ponds! ", the investor protested. I told the investor: "Even when you run ten boreholes, it will not fill

any of your holes in two months' time, neither in the rainy season nor in the

dry season. The holes don't keep water because the soil is not holding water! It's simple as the ABC. " "So, what is the way forward, " he asked me. I told him to fill the holes and rethink the farm, but now with a professional and realistic approach.

Many farmers start a fish farm without the basic knowledge of fish farming. They are relying on so-called fish consultants who in rare cases are independent and rarely give

you honest advice. This handbook should prevent you from making basic mistakes.

Most farm owners are actually investors. People around the investor could have been talking about how good and profitable fish farming is, but he never went into the matter in detail. The fact that your neighbour is farming fish and is telling you how well the business is running, should not be the reason to start yourself. Investigate

the business: examine the value chain, the risks involved, try to visit farms which are

producing a substantial amount of fish and talk with successful farmers.

Successful farmers tend to be more honest than nonsuccessful farmers because the

won't like to tell you that they failed. If farmers fail, they always put the blame on the staff, latter

the staff, the bad juveniles they have received, bad purchase of feed and bad advice. What about

themselves? Was it not them who built the farm, who paid for the feed, who employed What about

who employed the staff and paid for the juveniles?

The investors who succeed in the business of fish farming, are dedicated? love

the challenge and really go for it. They are well informed because they have gone

to seminars, workshops, markets and farms before they start their own fish farm. They choose the location where to farm based on a SWOT analysis, not on sentiment. A sentimental reason could be a wish to start fish farming in your village where you hail from, because you want to do something for your family or the

community.

introduction

Often juveniles or fingerlings are sold by consultants. They want you to buy a lot, even if youdon't have the money, space or water to facilitate them. At first there is no problem, becausethe fish are still small. But when your consultant has moved on and the fish have grown bigger,

you'll find yourself in trouble.

If you want to start a fish farm to gain experience, by all means start small.

Facility is poorly built and poorly set up

farming is just a hole with water, either dug in the ground or built with blocks. Fish farming is not

Many fish farms are built with inferior materials at the lowest cost. The perception is that fish

a low-class business. To keep the water in a pond or a concrete tank, means good construction, compacting, reinforced concrete, pillars and good plastering with correct mixtures of cement and sand, contracting good technicians with good tools. Very often ponds are made on a slope and the water level in the pond or tank varies according to the slope. Fish ponds should be built

level and could have a slope on the bottom but not on the top. Mostly the pipes bought and

used to supply water and discharge water are of such poor quality that it will result in leakages. Especially having inferior quality pipes and fittings under the concrete, is very bad, because repairing leakages in that spot is very difficult. At most farms the pipes to supply or to drain are too small also. It is again the perception that the fish pond doesn't need much water, only to filltoo small also.

Drainage and supply have no priority. Always use high pressure pipes of 10 or 16 bar.

If ponds are built well, they will last for decades and eventually will always be cheaper.

All the pipes that are laid in the soil should be stabilised with sharp sand or stone dusk. This isto avoid the pipes breaking when people or machines go over them. Mostly, the pipes are laid

just a few inches below the topsoil. It is just a matter of time before they start to leak. Always

make a drawing of where all the pipes are situated, so that if you want to make adjustments

or amendments in the future, you know exactly where the pipes are.

When you start setting up the farm, make a complete blueprint; get a survey of the land so that

you become aware of the levels of the land and build according to the levels available, in order

to make drainage and pumping as efficient as possible. Make a plan for the start-up stage, keeping in mind possible expansion in the future. Most of the time, farmers start building without any vision. This will make the farm look scattered and disorganised and running the farm will not be efficient.

Have in mind your storage facility, the ease of keeping your feed and materials and how tohand it out efficiently to the farm. The security facility should be situated at a central point inorder to easily oversee the complete farm. Other facilities have to be situated in the right placealso. In chapter 61 give you an example of setting up a complete farm with all the facilities

There is no supervision and the recruitment of staff is not taken seriously

The farm is ready to launch; you start employing people with fish farm qualifications and now it's time for you to relax and wait for the results to come. Unfortunately, it doesn't work farm qualifications and this way. The farm needs intensive supervision. You have to show the staff is very important to you and that you are eager to get and see results. Supervision doesn't this way. that the farm is very important to you and that you are eager to get and see results. Supervision doesn't mean to put fear into the staff when things are not going as they should.

Supervision means guiding and coaching the staff day by day, encouraging them to do the work with passion and helping them to solve the problems on the way instead of blaming them for mistakes. If the farm is managed by fear, the staff will start to hide all the mistakes happening on the farm and they will do eye service. It divides staff members and blame is pointed in all directions instead of putting heads together to solve problems. If a farm a farm is running smoothly and production is ongoing, it's a mutual effort and not a one-man's achievement. Teamwork is the key to success at your farm. Pay your staff well, don't turn them into beggars. achievement.

Another mistake many farmers make is to rush things as soon as the farm is ready to start.

The investment has to be paid back as soon as possible and the investor wants to see fish Another mistake many farmers make is to rush things as soon as the farm is ready to start. It doesn't work this way; first you start to run the facility

without fish for a couple of days to be sure that the entire infrastructure is working fine boreholes, pumps, generator, solar etcetera. The brood stock is already conditioned and fine. If you start with juveniles, you start up with one or two ponds, not with all the s, or two ponds, not with all the ponds at the same time. You have a production plan and you don't deviate from it

When you employ staff for the farm, it's not necessary to look for very experienced fish farmers, instead look at skills such as willingness and ability to learn, honesty, ability to work in a team and having a passion for the job. If you can find these kinds of people, learn, honesty, ability to you certainly will enjoy them as long as you supervise them and give them incentives give them incentives when the farm is making progress. Try to find out about the background of the staff you are employing, get references and guarantors, home address et cetera. Be careful not to give them a very narrow in all the farm issues involved, because the job description gives them excuses for not doing things.

Lack of fundingLack of fundingThings will go wrong if the funding is not sufficient to complete the investments and/or the working capital runs out before the first sales. The investor/owner will start to cut the investments and/corners and will be pressurized to get quick results. He will also put a lot of pressure on will start to cut his

staff; demanding results which are unrealistic. Quick results are usually very bad results and more misery. It can kill the farm from the beginning. Build a farm you can afford and have a realistic cash flow programme to back up what you want to do.

## Theft

Some years ago, I was called by a farmer who was using the feed I was selling to him. He was very disappointed in the performance of the feed; the fish were not growing. I went to visit the farm and couldn't trace the problem. It seemed that the feed

was not stolen and the fish were not stolen either, since the records and the sales

were showing all the results and the stocked fish were retrieved at harvest minus the recorded mortality. The fish were just very small but didn't look malnourished. I left the farm and felt bad for him, but I knew we were overlooking something. Two months later he called me and told me what was going on. The manager of the farm

was taking out the big fish in the evening but was smart enough to replace them

with smaller fish to keep up with the number of fish which was guarded so anxiously. He apologized for accusing the feed of being so bad and told me: "If Nigerians use their smart brains in a positive way and not for 419, Nigeria would be a better place!"

Unfortunately, theft is a big issue in many farms and it starts from lack of supervision

and lack of good management. Most likely there are no standard operational procedures (SOP) and everybody in the farm does what he likes. In this type of environment, it's very tempting to start stealing because nobody knows what exactly is going on at the farm. Theft will not be spotted quickly. To be honest, even if you give your staff good salaries, it

will not avoid any theft on the long term.

Commitment and passion to do a good job are the virtues you have to create in your staff. Give them the feeling that it's their own farm

and that the destiny of the farm and their future is in their own hands. An environment where you start shouting at staff and threaten to sack them if they don't perform, will certainly result in stealing. Their minds are

already out of the farm. As the manager you have to create a team spirit in your staff; in

this way anybody who wants to do harm to the farm will be spotted and corrected before theft starts. If the staff are set up against each other, it will certainly lead to bad results. Be sure that the people you bring together can also work together as a team.

Some owners like to put people together who actually do not match; they believe the

workers will control each other and it will reduce or avoid theft. I don't think this is the

right way; it will lead to bad results. People who don't like each other will always like to see the other person's downfall. That means bad results at the farm, which will be blamed on one person only. Before you know it, the staff start blaming each other, instead of putting their heads together to solve problems and get results.

Putting extra high prices for any maintenance to be done at the farm.

The owner pays for the feed directly to the shop but the farm manager will not take all the feed to the farm. Instead he has an arrangement with the shop owner to leave some feed behind and get money in return. Or get some empty feed bags of that brand and fill it with an inferior feed in order to have a complete delivery.

Some of the theft can be a one-man activity but stealing fish or other products from the farm, has to be done in collaboration with other people which in most cases is the Security. The worst thing happens if you are employing workers who happen to be your family and they are the ones stealing at the farm. If you employ family members, please employ them

on qualifications and integrity not on sentiment. Never employ people you cannot sack.

Fish farming is not a retirement job

For many people this will not be the information they want to read.

Many fish farmers, who start their business, have a retirement background. The main

reason for that is that they have the money to start and plan ahead to start a fish farm the

moment they are retired, having already invested in a plot of land some years before. Most of these retirees had a job as civil servant or office worker. Their work experience doesn't really fit the qualifications to be a fish farmer. Fish farming is a way of life and you need to be very committed in order to get profitable results. Neglecting the farm for a couple

of days can give a drawback of many months. Most retirees rely on the people they hire,

but you have to be a front soldier yourself in order to push your staff to be a front soldier too. After some time, it's getting worse; the drive has vanished and the fish farmers are not coming to the farm as frequently as before. The road is bad and other obligations are coming in. The farm will be visited only once a week accompanied by some phone calls

to find out what is going on at the farm. Now the farm is managed and supervised by a

weekend-farmer or even worse by a telephone-farmer. This farm is doomed to die and will never make any money. The staff are frustrated, no investments are made anymore and the farm, once a-dream-come-true, has become a painful ulcer and a drain of money.



## 2

THE BIOLOGY OF THE AFRICAN SHARPTOOTH CATFISH

2.1 THE SPECIES OF CATFISH AND THEIR GEOGRAPHICAL

DISTRIBUTION

2.3 FISH ARE COLD-BLOODED ANIMALS

Chapter 2

2.1 THE SPECIES OF CATFISH AND THEIR GEOGRAPHICAL

DISTRIBUTION

In nature there are over 3000 species of catfish and you can find them on almost every

continent. The size of catfish species can vary from less than 1 cm to over 2 m long. What all catfish have in common is the absence of scales and the presence of barbels, although they differ in number and size. Some of the catfish species are cultured and are important food fish for human beings, for example the African sharptooth catfish (Clarias gariepinus),

the European catfish (Silurus glanis) and the American catfish (Ictalurus punctatus). Other

catfish species are very beautiful, colourful and greatly appreciated as ornamental fish in

aquaria and ponds.

The African sharptooth catfish belongs to the family of Claridae and has its geographical

distribution over the whole continent of Africa Because of their importance as food fish,

African sharptooth catfish are exported to Asia as well as to South America and Europe where they are cultured and grown for human consumption. Their natural habitats are tropical swamps, lakes and rivers, preferably slow-moving water. If the water body dries up, they can even survive in the mud until the next rainy season.

## 2.2 BIOLOGICAL DESCRIPTION

## Skin

African sharptooth catfish have a scaleless slimy skin, which is darkly pigmented, brown

and black on the dorsal and lateral (top and side) parts of the body. The skin over the abdomen (belly) is lighter coloured grey to white. Depending on the colour of the water, the pigmentation changes. Catfish tend to adapt in order to be less visible. The slime of the catfish acts as a defence mechanism against parasites and

bacteria. Always be careful not to damage or reduce the slime of the skin, otherwise you

will certainly get problems which can cause fish mortality.

## Mouth

With its wide mouth, the African sharptooth catfish has the ability to feed on a variety

of food types, ranging from small zooplankton to fish. It is able to suck benthos, for

example mosquito larvae from the bottom, tear pieces of cadaver with its small teeth on its jaws and swallow prey, such as whole fish. The mouth circumference of this circumference of this gape-limited predator, which is about 1/4 of its total length, determines the maximum size of its prey. An African sharptooth catfish of 30 cm long (approximately 200 g) and has a mouth its prey.

circumference of about 7.5 cm. This enables it to encompass the body circumference circumference of

The biology of the African sharptooth catfish

small tilapia of up to 8-10 cm, which makes the African sharptooth catfish an excellent

predator for controlling overpopulation of tilapia in ponds.

Catfish are cannibalistic by nature and start to eat each other from the first day of feeding

onwards.

Barbels, olfactory organs and eyes

Around the mouth of the African sharptooth catfish eight barbels can be distinguished

(Figure 2). The barbels can be moved without moving the mouth itself. Close to the nasal

barbels two olfactory organs are located (Figure 2). Catfish recognise their prey mainly by

touch and smell. This is of relevance during feeding at night and in highly turbid or muddy

waters. Catfish have small eyes and don't rely very much on their eyesight.

Fins

The median fins of the African sharptooth catfish consist of a dorsal, a caudal and an anal

fi n, while the paired fi ns consist of the pectoral and ventral fi ns (Figure 3a). The pectoral fi ns have developed strong spines (Figure 3b) which have a locomotory and protective function. The fish are capable of migrating over land by sculling with their tail, as they elbow along on their spines. The spines of the African sharptooth catfish are not poisonous, whereas

other catfish species do have poisonous spines.

The pectoral fi ns come in very handy when taking the fish out of a net or bowl, because the moment you touch the catfish, they will open their fi ns as a refl ex to defend themselves.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_010.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figures 2 and 3. Drawings of fins, barbels, gills and the arborescent organ of the African sharptooth catfish

(source: Practical manual for the culture of the African catfish by W.J.A.R. Viveen et al.).

Chapter 2

Gills and arborescent organs

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_011.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

The distribution of the gills and the arborescent organs on the five branchial arches of the African sharptooth catfish, is shown in Figure 3b. They can be observed by cutting

away the operculum. For the purpose of respiration, water is taken into the mouth, passes

over the gills for gaseous exchange and is then expelled through the opercular opening. Especially when the water's dissolved oxygen content is depleted or if the fish are out of the water, air is periodically gulped in through the mouth. Gaseous exchange takes place via the arborescent organs in air chambers above the gills. The air is also expelled through

the opercular openings. Due to its atmospheric respiration, the African sharptooth catfish

is capable of surviving in mud during the dry season. It is even able to survive out of the water for some hours depending on the humidity of the environment.

Because catfish can tolerate low oxygen levels in water, they are very suitable for fish culture.

The gill rakers at the back of the branchial arches serve as filters for feeding on small

vegetable matter and invertebrates (Figure 3b).

Anus and urogenital system

In both sexes of catfish, the urogenital opening is situated at a papilla just behind the anus.

The sex difference is visible when the fish reach 200 g. The papilla of the male is long and

ends in a tip. The female papilla is circular (Figure 4).

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_012.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 4. Sexual differentiation between male and female of the African sharptooth catfish (source: Practical

manual for the culture of the African catfish by W.J.A.R. Viveen et al.).

The biology of the African sharptooth catfish

2.3 FISH ARE COLD-BLOODED ANIMALS

## 24

A cold-blooded animal or ectotherm, like all fish are, does not have an internal mechanism

to regulate body temperature. Instead, it relies on solar energy captured by the

environment. Catfish will always have a body temperature which is equal to the ambient water temperature. The internal activity of the fish, called its metabolism, increases with increasing water temperature, but it has an optimal range. For the African sharptooth catfish the optimal body temperature varies between 25 and $ 3 0^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $

So, cold-blooded means that a fish is not internally generating energy to regulate its

body temperature. Therefore, it requires far less energy than warmblooded animals or endotherms. Warm-blooded animals need frequent meals on a daily basis to keep the body temperature constant, whereas coldblooded animals can skip meals for days and even for weeks without any negative health impact.

At our farm, we always take into consideration the temperature of the water and the activity of the fish.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_013.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

## THE AVAILABLE SOURCES OF WATER

3.1 INTRODUCTION

3.2 WATER FROM A RIVER OR STREAM

3.4 WATER FROM AN AQUIVER

3.6 CITY COUNCIL WATER

Chapter 3

## 3.1 INTRODUCTION

Catfish farming has to be carried out in fresh water. The salt content (sodium chloride) should

not exceed 6 g/l. Unfortunately, most of the water available in the world is salt water. The

proportions are as follows: 97.5% of the water reserves in the world consists of salt water (oceans), 1.75% in the form of ice and snow on glaciers at the North and South Poles, 0.5% is underground water and only 0.25% is fresh water from rivers, swamps and lakes.

Africa is the continent with the lowest availability of fresh water; actually many places in

Africa have to deal with a shortage of water. This makes fish farming economically unfeasible.

In Nigeria however, we have places with abundant water from rivers, streams and dams, especially in the south and west. In the north we face shortages of water and rivers dry up during the dry season. Underground water is available almost everywhere in Nigeria, but the yield of boreholes and the water quality vary a lot from area to area.

Let us evaluate each source of water.

## 3.2 WATER FROM A RIVER OR STREAM

Rivers and streams in Nigeria which have water flowing all year round, are very suitable

sources of water for fish farming. To find out if the water quality is suitable for fish farming, the first thing to discover is whether the river has an active fishing community. Get your information concerning the fish population and catches from the locals, find out the lowest and highest water level in the river and whether there are any activities which have a negative

impact on the water quality and quantity.

Unfortunately, rivers and streams in Nigeria are also used for waste disposal, solid as well as liquid. Another activity which has a really bad impact on the river, is mining. Stones are crushed on the riverside and the river water is used for washing. Chemicals are used to

isolate the precious minerals from the sand. As a result, the water becomes extremely turbid

and when the flow of water in the river decreases during the dry season, it becomes a poor source of water for fish farming.

Another problem with river water arises with the first rains. When they start, the river water gets polluted with runoff from farmland. The water not only becomes turbid but also gets

polluted with insecticides and herbicides. The effect is an increasing rate of catfish mortality,

because this pollution weakens their immune system. As a result, bacterial infections are prone to happen. During the peak of the rainy season, the runoff is less poisonous to the fish and consequently the mortality rate reduces. The best time of the year for fish farming in for instance the Abuja region is the peak of the dry season, because the water is clear and less

polluted, but this can be different for other regions in Nigeria.

## 28

The available sources of water

Most rivers in Nigeria become very turbid with every rainfall. The volume of water increases rapidly and decreases rapidly. It's a sign of erosion. The

land does not hold any water; all rainwater goes straight into the river via gullies and man-made gutters. Top soil and laterite

are washed away into the river, making the soil less suitable for farming. Reforestation is the

only way to stop this erosion. Rivers in dense forests don't have this problem, therefore the

water turbidity is not affected so much by rain in such areas.

If river water is used as a source of water, there should be provision for an 'intake'. 'This is

a place where you are able to pump the water out of the river into a reservoir. The intake

should be chosen carefully and should definitely be located above the highest level to which the water can raise during extreme rainfall. The intake should also be installed at a location on the riverbank where the river is deep and the water is close, even during the dry water

is close, even during the dry season. This way a very long suction hose is avoided. If a permanent structure is built for the intake,

look for locations which have rocks on the bottom of the river, so that the concrete structure, for the intake,

concrete structure built on top of this, has a good and solid foundation. If the farm is small, you can choose a more flexible option: such as a small petrol water pump with a suction hose. For your convenience, the pump can be placed on the riverbank every day and taken away every night. The water from the river can be pumped directly into the fish pond, but the preferable pumped directly into the fish

pond, but the preferable option is to create an overhead reservoir/tank for collection of the river water. From this

reservoir the water can flow to the fish ponds by gravity (Figure 5). river water.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_014.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 5. Water, which is pumped from a river or stream to the reservoir, flows to the pond by gravity.

Pumping the water from the river into the reservoir or straight to the fish ponds, can be done either by electrical, petrol or diesel pumps. The choice depends on the availability of electrical power. If there is no electrical power available, a generator has to produce the

power for the electrical pump. In this case it is preferable to power the water pump directly

with petrol or diesel (Photo 1). Diesel pumps are preferable to petrol pumps, but when the

the farm is small, you will most likely go for a petrol water pump.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_015.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 1. Petrol pump and diesel pump.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_016.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

The suction hose has to be fixed very tightly in order not to suck any air. A non-return valve should always be placed at the end of the suction hose. should be flexible so that it can be taken out any time the current of the river gets too fast and furious. The

end of the hose consists of a perforated suction basket which stops any big particles from

The available sources of water

Most pumps must be primed before they can operate. This means that the suction hose is filled with water before it can suck by itself. Some diesel pumps are self-priming though, and can be started immediately.

3.3 WATER FROM A DAM OR LAKE

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_018.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

lake is Lake Chad. It is a shallow lake located in the north-eastern part of Nigeria and

also extends to Cameroon and Niger. The biggest dam is Kainji Dam located in Niger

State. The source of Kainji Dam is the Niger River.

Dams are built for many purposes:

Fishing and fish farming

Recreational purposes

Water supply for drinking water stations

The water of a dam or lake has some advantages over the water from a river. The quality of the water does not fluctuate as much as in a river because the dam or lake

acts as a very big water buffer. Any deposits from heavy rainfall settle down or are

neutralised in the lake or dam. In most lakes and dams the water levels are more stable

than in rivers. Furthermore, it's easier to make an intake at a dam than at a riverbank.

Dams are usually deep which makes it easy to create a good intake.

Most dams have a pipeline, from which the water falls back into the river, to be used

Electricity generated by water turbines

Irrigation purposes

Controlling the flow of the river

for drinking water stations, turbines and irrigation purposes. This pipeline can supply water by gravity because the level of the land behind the dam is 10 to 50 m lower. This pipeline can also be used for fish farms and saves a lot of money, because pumping the water into the ponds is not necessary. Also, a reservoir is not needed in this case; the

(Figure 6).

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_019.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 6. A gravity fed farm.

Not many farms use the option to take water from the pipeline behind the dam. This is

because these structures, including the land behind the dam, belong to the federal or

local government (water board) and they are reluctant to allow their use for commercial purposes. It really is a missed opportunity, because it could be a very good thing for community development creating fish farm

areas for many individual small-scale farmers using the same pipeline and enabling them to enjoy a facility with the lowest possible

running costs.

## 3.4 WATER FROM AN AQUIFER

Underground water can be tapped by drilling a borehole. Depending on the location,

depth and size of the borehole, the yield of water varies from 1 m $ ^{3} $ /hour to as much as 50

m $ _{3} $ /hour. In order to drill a borehole, first a survey is required to find out the most suitable position for drilling. Underground water is nothing less than collected rainwater which flows via the permeable soil into the aquifers. Aquifers are underground layers of water-

bearing rock. This process has been going on for centuries. Some of our groundwater can

underground (borehole) water rapidly. Fish farmers can use of boreholes is depleting the

hatchery to the post-juvenile stage (see Appendix 1 for the catfish growth stages), in order

of underground water for future generations. not to deplete the reserves

What are the constraints of boreholes in general?

The available sources of water

be as old as 1000 years. In recent years, due to urbanisation, a rapid increase in the number of boreholes is depleting the

A company drilling boreholes will never guarantee the yield and the quality of the

water, but will ask you to pay at least 70% upfront.

In most areas of Nigeria boreholes give only a moderate yield of less than

5 m $ ^{3} $ /hour. With this yield a small grow-out farm is possible but it can never serve

a medium or large fish farm.

Pumping with a borehole pump takes quite a lot of electrical power. In addition,

borehole pumps can break down or the borehole tends to dry up.

A fish farm needs at least two boreholes.

The yield of the borehole does not depend on the size of the pump but on the recovery rate of your borehole when pumping. For example, when the water level

in your borehole is at 10 m depth when you start pumping, and the level drops

by 10 to 20 m depth, while a small pump of only 1.5 hp is used, it means that the recovery rate of the borehole is very poor. The water level of a good borehole hardly drops when water is pumped out. The yield is very high and the aquifer has a lot of water which can be easily taken out.

Some boreholes contain high levels of iron or bacteria which make them unsuitable

for a hatchery and/or even a grow-out.

Borehole water has very low levels of oxygen and high levels of carbon dioxide. Before the water enters the fish farm, it should be exposed to air in order to become rich in oxygen and low in carbon dioxide.

## What are the advantages of boreholes?

Many boreholes supply water of drinking water quality. That makes them suitable for hatcheries. The water quality of a borehole is very stable as long as the borehole is drilled well and the soil around the borehole pipe is sealed well.

Because river water is unsuitable to use for hatcheries in almost all cases, the only option

for a hatchery is a borehole or water from the water board. The use of drinking water is

only possible as long as you allow the chlorine to escape within 24 to 48 hours.

## How to keep boreholes clean?

The borehole drilled on your land should always be located far away from waste disposal

## Chapter 3

areas and soakaways. Keep the environment where your borehole is situated, as clean as possible. Test the quality of the borehole water every two years for chemical content and at least once a year for coliforms, which are bacteria of faecal origin which indicates the

presence of other pathogenic bacteria. Also clean your water reservoir at least four times

a year to avoid growth of unwanted bacteria and algae and remove silt deposits from the

## 3.5 WATER FORM A WELL

A well is an open pit, dug into the earth, deep enough to reach the groundwater level. The water can be pumped or taken out with a basket and rope. The yield of a well is limited and only considered useful for domestic use, not for fish farming.

## 3.6 CITY COUNCIL WATER

City council water cannot really be a reliable source of water for fish farming. Also, the

water is chlorinated and toxic for the fish if it's used directly from the tap. The chlorine

causes the slime on the skin to dissolve, which will definitely kill the fish. Chlorine, however, is a gas. When the water is exposed to air and light, the chlorine will evaporate within one day, after which you can use the water for fish farming.

## 4.1 FLOW-THROUGH SYSTEMS

The majority of fish farms run a system called flow through. Water comes in and goes out,

carrying the fish waste out of the pond (Figure 7). The water is not meant to provide oxygen,

since catfish, apart from the early stages, take in the majority of their oxygen from the air.

Water Supply

FISH POND

Drainage

Figure 7. Schematic drawing of a flow-through system.

Use of water

Fish farming is all about water management. In this context it is very strange that most farmers don't know how much water they have access to

## in a day or a year. The quantity

of water used in a day, is directly related to the fish production. Almost every fish farmer

thinks otherwise. They believe it's the number of fish ponds that determines the production capacity. However, filling the ponds is just the beginning. The water in the pond has to be flushed constantly in order to keep the water quality acceptable so that the fish can enjoy the environment, eat and grow well.

If the relationship between the size of the pond and the number of fish is not relevant, how do I calculate the number of fish I can stock in my farm?

The stocking density in a pond is related to the flow of water which passes through the pond. In other words, the more water you are able to flush out of the pond, the more fish

you can stock in that same pond. To be more precise, the flushing rate is directly related to

the amount of feed that is given. This is related to the number and size of the fish in the pond; the more fish you stock, the more feed you need.

The feed is consumed by the growing fish, but this process also causes pollution in the form of faeces, urine, ammonia and carbon dioxide. All these accumulating waste products will

cause serious toxic problems for the fish. Therefore they have to be removed. This is only

possible by flushing the water periodically or constantly out of the pond.

The relationship between the feed and the flushing rate is as follows: for every 1 kg of feed given to the fish, you need to flush 1.4 m $ ^{3} $ of water.

How do we know this equation?

The equation for feed and flushing is based on practical experience, but also backed up by measuring the ammonium level which should not exceed 20 mg/l. Ammonium is the first limiting factor to cause problems for the catfish. Because without flushing the ammonium

level increases every day, flushing has to take place preferably on a daily basis.

38

Fish culture systems

Parameters that will change the equation of 1 kg of feed to $ 1.4 \mathrm{m}_{3} $ of water:

Overfeeding: the feed is not being eaten completely by the fish, polluting the water

directly.

The feed is of poor quality and the digestibility of the feed is low: the fish will produce more waste per kg of feed consumed.

The feed is not well processed: it falls apart in the water very quickly.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_020.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

The equation is based on good quality feed and optimum feeding.

Example 1. How to calculate the flush rate for fish of 0.5 kg?

Suppose we have 1000 fish, having an average weight of 0.5 kg each. If we feed 10 kg (2% of biomass) of feed in a day, how many litres of water do we need to flush?

Recall that for every 1 kg of feed, we need to flush about 1.4 m $ ^{3} $ of water.

Hence, we need to have a flushing regime of

= 10 kg /day x 1.4 m $ ^{3} $ /kg

=14 m3/day

The fish can be stocked in 10 m $ _{3} $ of water (100 pieces/m $ _{3} $ ) or 20 m $ _{3} $ of water (50

pieces/m $ _{3} $ ) or 100 m $ _{3} $ of water (10

very flexible when it comes to stocking ratio, but the flushing has to be 14 m3/day for all pond sizes. The same fish will grow, but when they become bigger, they subsequently need more feed, which means that the flushing rate should be adjusted.

Example 2. How to calculate the flush rate for fish of 1 kg?

Suppose we have 1000 fish, having an average weight of 1 kg and they are fed 15 kg per day (1.5% of the biomass). What would be the flushing regime (rate)?

Recall that for every 1 kg of feed, we need to flush about 1.4 $ m_{3} $ of waste water. Hence, for feeding 15 kg in a day, we would need to flush

= 15 kg/day x 1.4 m $ ^{3} $ /kg

## = 21 m3/day

As you can see, when the fish get bigger, the flushing rate increases drastically.

Many farmers start with stocking juveniles. At that time the flushing rate is low because

the feed consists of just a few kilos a day. The problem starts after some months when the

fishes' need for feed has really increased. The flushing rate has to increase drastically. When the flushing rate does not keep up with the increasing feeding levels, the water turns from green to black. This is a sign of anaerobic conditions and the water starts to smell. The fish will start to hang at the surface and refuse to eat as before. This condition happens to many

farmers and it's all due to poor water management.

Chapter 4

Efficiency of flushing water

The efficiency of flushing a concrete tank, pond or any other tank varies from the way you do it. If the tank is full and flushing is done by causing the water to overflow, your

efficiency is lower than when you drain part of the water and replace it with fresh water.

The efficiency of replacing water is two times higher than the first option (Figure 8).

20mg/l

20mg/l

Figure 8. Flushing or draining the water from a pond or tank.

Replacing the water has one disadvantage!

Replacing the water from a pond completely or almost completely, is very effi cient in terms

of improving the water quality straight away, but it will stress the fish, which can lead to increased mortality and higher feed conversion rates. This practice is done by many farmers; they allow the water to get completely bad and smelly, resulting in fish hanging at the surface not eating well and mortality increasing, before they change the water

completely.

In my opinion, the best way of flushing the water from a tank is by lowering the water level 20 to 30% every morning and allowing fresh water to come in and overflow from the tank for the rest of the day.

Another malpractice, which is carried out by many farmers, is to stock all the tanks in a

short period of time. This will lead to an extremely high demand for water when the fish all reach their market size at the same time. Consequently, this leads to hardly any need for water after all the fish have been sold.

Remember the flushing rate is directly related to the feed given!

Secondly, we calculate the flow rate of the pump which pumps the water to the reservoir. A fish farm ideally needs a constant supply of water. The only way to achieve this is by a water reservoir.

Pond design and water management

A well-constructed pond built of either concrete, plastic lining, earth or otherwise, should

have a well-designed drain which is easy to manage (Figure 9).

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_021.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_022.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 9. Three ways to drain a pond.

The inlet to the pond should be via a pipeline which is connected to the reservoir, directed.

to the ponds and controlled by a valve.

In many farms the inlet and outlet (the drain) of the ponds are too small. As a result, the water will not be drained and filled quickly. The main inlet and outlet pipes for ponds of

20 m20m $ ^{33} $ or more, should have a diameter of 4 inches or 110 mm. The drainage should also

have a diameter of 4 inches or 110 mm.

Ponds can be built completely dug into the ground, half way dug into the ground or completely on top of the ground. All depends on the drainage. The drainage should go by gravity. Pumping out the water to flush the tank, is not an option and should be avoided

by all means.

## Chapter 4

One exception to this matter: ponds constructed in marshlands, can only be drained by pumping out the water. Fresh water automatically comes in from underground and an intake is not required. During the rainy season this process is very quickly, in

the dry season recovering water takes time. These ponds can only run extensively,

but it's possible and feasible. Emptying the ponds during the rainy season is difficult though, because fish get left behind in the mud and interfere with the next stocking.

The waste water of the ponds can be directed to a lower collection reservoir (settling

tank). The overflow of this collection reservoir can go into a canal, river or a gutter,

which leads to a river or stream. Never use a soakaway to collect water because it will clog up in a short period of time and then the water cannot go anywhere. Drainage water should not be going to other people's land to avoid clashes with neighbours. Waste water is useful for irrigation, but this is only applicable during the

dry season when the fish farm is surrounded with enough land.

## Ground water

If you build ponds in the ground and the ground water level can reach the bottom of the pond, it can cause severe damage to the pond. When the pond is empty and the

ground water level reaches above the bottom of the pond, the pond can be lifted and

it can break. In the case of plastic lined ponds, the pond liner will be lifted and it's like you see a hippo inside the pond. For the earthen pond a higher level of ground water is not a problem, but you cannot drain and dry the pond because the ground water will keep on coming. If you suspect the ground water level to be very high, always

keep the plastic ponds full of water, even if there are no fish inside.

Roofing the ponds; concrete ponds in particular

Many farmers like to roof concrete ponds. I believe this just adds to the investment costs without any benefits. Farmers believe that the direct sunlight will increase the

water temperature to a level which will harm the fish. In concrete tanks the water

temperature does not increase very rapidly though. When you flush on a daily basis, which is necessary, the incoming fresh water will reduce the water temperature to levels below 30 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $. An additional benefit of having no roof over the pond, is the growth of green algae. Green algae are really beneficial to the catfish; they like this

green environment and are less susceptible to bacterial diseases. Catfish grow even

more quickly in green water compared to clear water. Additionally, the ammonium levels in green water will also reduce, because algae take in the ammonium. As a result, the flushing rate can even be lower than in fish ponds with a roof. the algal production is inhibited because sunlight cannot penetrate the water

directly.

Fish culture systems

There is however one exception to not roofing the fish tanks. That is when you use polyethylene (plastic) tanks. These tanks are mostly used to grow juveniles to post-juveniles (see Appendix 1 for the growth stages of catfish). If situated on a floor in the sun, the water (see Appendix inside the plastic tank can

inside the plastic tank can become over 35 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $ which is too high for the fish. When plastic tanks are used, it is advisable

tanks are used, it is advisable to roof them to prevent exposure to direct sunlight. Covering the top of the tank with banana leaves is a cheaper and also an effective option to avoid high water temperatures.

water temperatures.

Water level in a pond

The water level in ponds should not be less than 100 cm. Many farmers however have water level in a pond

The water level in ponds should not be less than 100 cm. Many farmers however have water levels of 30 to 40 cm or even less. This causes unnecessary stress to the catfish because the exposure to sunlight is high; in addition, the fish cannot hide and the temperature ponds with a low water level are also large.

## Pipes

The pipes for drainage and overflow used in concrete ponds, should be of premium quality. Pipes

The pipes for drainage and overflow used in concrete ponds, should be of premium quality. Use only high-pressure pipes of 10 bar. The bottom drain should end with a socket, so that you can put a standpipe inside it. To improve the connection between the PVC the concrete, you should sandpaper the sockets and the pieces of pipe to be put in the

concrete. After sandpapering, put PVC-glue on the sockets and attach fine sand. This way, the concrete, you should sandpaper the sockets and the pieces of pipe to be put in the

concrete. After sandpapering, put PVC-glue on the sockets and attach fine sand. This way, the connection between the pipe and the concrete will be

strong, and without any leakage. If your underground piping leaks at the connections, it will be very hard to fix. Besides, the connection between the pipe and the concrete will be

term investment. minimise costs when it comes to pipes and fittings for your concrete system. it's a long-term

investment. The size of the pipes needed is related to the stages of the growth cycle of the fish. In grow-out ponds the size should be 110 mm diameter or more, for pre- and on-growing the pipes are too small, they will not allow you to flush and supply on time and they can easily become clogged up. and for juvenile production 50 mm. to flush

and supply on time and they can easily become clogged up.

Construction of a reservoir

Construction of a reservoir Reservoirs should be built at least two metres higher than the upper level of the fish pond. This allows the water to flow by gravity from the reservoir to the fish pond. Reservoirs should be built

excessive number of pipes. upper level of the fish pond, and as central as possible to avoid an

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_023.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

## Chapter 4

The piping from the reservoir to the fish pond has to be done with good quality PVC or polyethylene pipe. The diameter of the supply varies with the stages of the growth cycle: for hatcheries a minimum of 50 mm is required,

for grow-out the diameter should be at least 110 mm. Depending on the farm size and the

distance to be covered by the piping, the size of the pipes will increase to 160 mm, 200 mm or even 250 mm. A qualified engineer has to provide you with the dimensions of the piping system, taking into consideration the flow rates, levels and distances.

The pipes should be preferably installed underground and the surveyor should map the

pipes on a drawing, so that they can always be located in order to avoid damaging them

when further construction takes place.

The hatchery water reservoir needs special attention; it has to be cleaned and drained

periodically, advisably every three months, in order to avoid any accumulation of debris. If

the tanks are dirty, disinfection with chlorine is even required. After washing and rinsing,

you are good to go again.

If borehole water has a high concentration of magnesium and/or calcium, deposits of these

metals easily form on the walls and inside the pipes. These deposits can harbour bacteria

which will make the water unsuitable for hatching and even for small fry (see Appendix 1 for the catfish growth stages). When the water is very soft, you will notice that all your tanks and equipment are easy to clean and look brand new afterwards. This is the best water for a hatchery.

Living in Nigeria on an estate, we have to be self-supporting for water, power and security. This is in itself a daily job, because all these factors need control and maintenance. At one point our entire family was constantly sick and we were wondering what was happening. We all went to a laboratory and found out that we

were infected with salmonella. The origin of the infection was our water tank. The

water tank was dirty and dead lizards had made it even worse. After cleaning and chlorinating the water tank, we quickly recovered. Since then, cleaning the water tank has become part of our regular maintenance.

4.2 RECIRCULATION SYSTEMS4.2 RECIRCULATION SYSTEM

In a recirculation system (Figure 10) the water is not used only once, but is also recycled via a water purification process and flows back into the pond. Recirculation is not 100% but can be as high as 95% depending on the quality of the water purification system and the

management applied. This recycling process means that the water consumption per kg of

It is a high-tech system and it can only be operated by farmers who have the engineering

skills and practical experience to work with a system like this.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_028.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

In the early 2000s (2000-2005), many farmers wanted to grow fish in a recirculation system.

Their reasons were:

Recirculation of the water however, comes at a price. The system can only operate with

24/7 power supply, because pumps are running 24/7 in order to push the water through the

Farming in a recirculation system (Photo 5 and 6) can be done very intensively and

doesn't need much space. So, farming can be done even in town or in an industrial area. Most investors and farmers don't live on their farm, but want to live close to the

farm for routine checks, control etcetera.

Farming in a recirculation system close to town or in town, offers the opportunity to

have customers close by.

Since it's a very intensive system, you can secure it and control theft much better than with an extensive pond farm system, which was used mostly at that time.

Because the majority of the water is recycled, the farm can run with one or two good boreholes, making the farm independent of other sources, such as a river or a dam.

Fish culture systems

Why are recirculation systems not popular anymore?

Although many farmers started very enthusiastically with recirculation systems, evaluation of the systems in 2018 shows that over 90% of them have left the recirculation system and closed down the farm, or run the system as a flow-through system.

Nigeria has not improved when it comes to a stable power supply. Running a generator any time power failure occurs, is very challenging. Therefore, farms mostly run the recirculation system with power on and off, but then it is not a recirculation system anymore; you can

compare it with half pregnancy-either you are pregnant or you aren't! Half pregnancy

doesn't exist!

Furthermore, the running costs are higher than expected and the system needs dedicated staff to keep it working well. Even theft of a recirculation system is not excluded. The reason is simple: most of the theft is done by insiders.

Theft: The fact that a farm is compact and controllable, is not an advantage if staff are

the ones stealing.

In areas where the nights are relatively cold or during harmattan, the biofiltration system cools down the water drastically. The temperature of the water can drop more than five

degrees overnight. This is not good for the health and growth of the catfish. This is not

really a problem in areas such as Lagos and Port Harcourt, but it will be a big problem in a place like Abuja.

Farmers who run a recirculation system, eventually have to compete with other farmers and if their cost price is higher, it will be difficult to make a profit when the market is

competitive.

The water purification system for the recirculation system is not available in Nigeria, so it has to be imported. Because the naira has become very weak against the euro and the dollar, these items became very expensive.

There is however one exception when it comes to running a recirculation system for fish.

That is when it is used for hatchery operations. Hatchery recirculation systems are very effective and competitive.

Fish culture systems

The operation of a recirculation system and its principles

Because a recirculation system works well for hatcheries, I will explain more about the operation of recirculation systems and their principles.

The following equation can be used:

In order to design a recirculation system for fish,

## we have to know the type of waste and

the quantity of waste a fish produces. The waste of the fish starts to build up from feeding

onwards.

Growth (of the fish) = input (feed) - output (waste)

Feed-------feed intake and feed loss

Feed intake----digestible fraction and faeces

Digestible fraction--------metabolic fraction and ammonium (urine)

Metabolic fraction----growth and respiration losses (carbon dioxide and heat)

The fish waste is: uneaten feed, faeces, urine in the form of ammonium, carbon dioxide

and heat.

1 kg of feed will result in the following waste (based on dry matter):

135 g of faeces-

43 g of ammonium-nitrogen (most of it in a soluble form).

9 g of phosphate (most of it in the faeces)

The waste is valuable for other agric purposes but the problem is, it is packed in a lot of

water! Chapter 13 tells you more about using waste water for crops.

Which processes can be used to eliminate the fish waste?

The fish waste accumulates in the water if it is not eliminated and eventually the water

becomes toxic for the fish. In the flow-through system we simply flush it out before the

water becomes toxic, but in a recirculation system we apply a purification system and reuse the water.

3 processes for dealing with fish waste:

1. Sedimentation of the waste water in order to separate the suspended solids (faeces) from the water and drain this fraction out of the system. If the solids stay in the water, they will cause anaerobic processes which produce toxic gases, for example

$ \mathrm{H}_{2} \mathrm{S} $. Excessive bacterial growth and solids in

suspension also have a negative impact

on the gills of the fish. Filtration is another way to reduce the suspended solids.

Chapter 4

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_032.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Nitrification of ammonium by bacterial processes in order to eliminate ammonium and change it into nitrate, which is not toxic for the fish. High ammonium levels in combination with a high pH can cause severe damage to the slime and skin of the fish. If the slime and

skin of a fish are affected, it will certainly die.

Removal of the carbon dioxide from the water to the air by degassing. High carbon dioxide levels are toxic for fish. They make them sluggish. The fish can suffocate and eventually die.

Systems to facilitate the waste processes

Sedimentation tank

Sedimentation is a relatively easy process. The flow rate in the sedimentation tank (Photo 7) is slow and allows the particles which are heavier than water, to settle before flowing out. As

a result, the particles will settle onto the bottom. When the tank includes sedimentation filter

materials, it increases the settling rate and trapping of solid particles, which results in overflow water without any particles from the suspended solids. The next step is to regularly flush and rinse the sedimentation tank, otherwise the solids start to dissolve and have a negative impact on the nitrification process. By flushing the sedimentation tank, you also refresh the water. As a result,

the salt levels will not keep on increasing but stay in balance. A good sedimentation tank can

reduce the load of fish waste by 50%. A sedimentation tank can also include bacterial processes such as denitrification. This occurs when oxygen levels in the tank are close to zero and the organic load (faeces) is eaten by bacteria which in their turn produce nitrogen gas out of nitrate.

- Equation $ 2 \mathrm {N O} _ {- 3} + 1 2 \mathrm {H} _ {4}? \mathrm {N} _ {2} + 6 \mathrm {H} _ {2} \mathrm {O} $

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_033.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 7. A sedimentation unit for a hatchery.

## Filtration unit

Filtration of suspended solids takes place when the mesh size of the filter material is smaller than the particles. The particles are trapped by the filter. The filter has to be backwashed

regularly in order to avoid complete clogging, so that even water cannot pass through.

Backwashing also involves flushing of some water. A common filtration unit, which is used in almost every swimming pool, is a sand filtration unit. Another useable filtration unit is a drum filter, so called because it looks like a drum. In hatcheries you rarely see filtration units, because almost all hatcheries with recirculation systems, practise the sedimentation

process.

Nitrifying unit or biofiltration unit

The nitrifying unit operates by a biological process. With the help of bacteria, ammonium, produced by the fish and excreted via the gills, is converted into nitrite and nitrate

respectively (Photo 8).

The equation is as follows:

Ammonium with oxygen is converted into nitrite by bacteria (Nitrosomonas)

Chemical equation: 2NH $ + + 3 O_{4} + 3 O_{2} $-------4 $ H_{+} + 2 H_{2} O + 2 N O_{4} $ $ 2 $-------4 $ H_{+} + 2 H_{2} O + 2 N O_{4} + energy_{2 2} + energy $

Nitrite with oxygen is converted into nitrate by bacteria (Nitrobacter)Nitrite with oxygen is converted into nitrate by bacteria (Nitrobacter)

Chemical equation: 2NOChemical equation: $ 2 \mathrm {N O} + \mathrm {O} _ {2 2} + $ $ O_{2 2} $------2NO------2NO $ ^{-3} $-+energy+energy

What you need to know about this process is the following:

Converting ammonium in nitrate is a two-step process. The intermediary nitrite is a very

toxic metabolite which can kill the fish. Nitrate is not toxic for fish even in concentrations

as high as 500 mg/l. But nitrite already kills small catfish at a level of 3 to 4 mg/l. When the biofiltration unit is not well developed, the water will always contain high levels of nitrite which can only be neutralised by flushing the water. The nitrification process makes the water acid. In a situation in which the borehole water has no buffer, it is advisable to

add sodium bicarbonate to the water from time to time to keep the pH at 7 (neutral). The

bacteria doing this job, need a surface area they can attach to (substrate) and enough
