Fish culture systems

What you should know about filter media:

- The material from which the filter media is made (Photo 9), has to be non-toxic for fish.

The surface area has to be large (about 200 m²/m³), but should be open enough for self-

cleaning. Excess bacteria on the media should be washed out with the water that

flows through it. For example, a stone bed is a good medium in the beginning, but when bacteria start to grow on it, it will clog completely, which will be very difficult to clean.

Air and water have to pass through the media easily so that exchange of carbon

dioxide and oxygen can take place efficiently.

The biofilters can be set up as a dry filter system; the water is pumped through the filter as a rain shower. Or, the biofilter unit is a submergible filter and the oxygen is supplied by an air

pump.

Extra note on nitrite intoxication

Small fish like fry are extremely sensitive to high nitrite levels. The first signs of intoxication are sluggish behaviour and hanging at the surface of the water. Their appetite reduces and after some hours or a day the first mortality is recorded. If not properly addressed, most of the fry

die within 48 hours. Concentrations already start to be toxic at 2 to 3 mg/l. When you have

a recirculation system for a catfish hatchery, you need to use a test kit to test the nitrite level in the water regularly.

When the catfish are bigger and the nitrite level suddenly rises, the fingerlings or juveniles can die very quickly too. This is accompanied by a very specific sign. The blood of the fish gets

brownish. This is because of the reaction between the blood and the nitrite. The haemoglobin

This also explains the toxicity of nitrite, because it makes the transport of oxygen in the blood almost impossible and the fish will suffocate.

2 remedies are possible:

in the blood binds to the nitrite which results in the blood turning brown.

1. Changing the water with clean borehole water in order to reduce the concentration of nitrite drastically.

Adding 3 kg of sodium chloride (industrial salt) per $ \mathrm{m_{3}} $ of water to neutralise the nitrite

and reduce its binding capacity to haemoglobin.

You can also add the salt after flushing. Combining the remedies makes them even more effective. Safe levels of nitrite for catfish are below 1.5 mg/ 1. Check every day and adjust on a daily basis if necessary. Industrial salt should always be available as standard material in a

hatchery!

Chapter 4

Degassing unit in order to remove carbon dioxide

When the fish metabolise, they produce carbon dioxide. This gas will partly be dissolved in the water which causes a problem at high concentrations. Carbon dioxide tends to make the

fish sluggish which reduces their ability to eat. Compare it to a poorly ventilated room which

you are in. The only thing you want to do is sleep. The carbon dioxide is easily removed with a properly functioning biofiltration unit. In the biofiltration unit oxygen will diffuse into the water and carbon dioxide will diffuse into the air. When the water has passed this unit, it is in a good condition for the fish and will go straight to the fish tank.

No special unit is needed, because a properly functioning biofiltration unit will automatically

take care of degassing the water.

UV-filtration unit (UV = ultraviolet)

The UV-filtration unit reduces the level of pathogenic bacteria in the water. A UV-light provides

ultraviolet rays which kill bacteria by changing their DNA (Photo 10). However, UV-light is

dangerous for your eyes, so never look at UV-light when it is on UV-rays only work when the water is transparent, allowing them to pass through, and if the flow rate of the water is in line with the capacity of the UV-light. The filtration unit should be cleaned and its functioning should be checked

after every cycle. In hatcheries it can be especially helpful to keep a healthy

environment for the catfish fry. The UV-system should be configured in such a way that, after

the water has gone through the sedimentation system, it is free from particles when it passes

through the UV-filtration unit.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_036.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 10. AUV-filtration unit.

Starting up a recirculation system

A brand-new recirculation system has no bacteria inside the filter. The good thing is that bacteria will move in spontaneously the moment you run the system and fish

release their waste products. These are food for the bacteria. It takes about six weeks to

develop a fully-grown bacterial mass on the filter media. During this period, the levels of ammonium become high in the first two weeks. Thereafter high levels of nitrite levels arise for about three weeks. In this period, you have to flush a lot of water in order not to poison your fish. Also start with small fish or fry so that the load of waste is small and

the bacterial mass can grow alongside the fish.

You can also buy nitrifying bacteria in a bottle and add them to the system. This start-up will be faster. Another method is to start up the filter without fish by just adding a little feed or urea into the system and allowing it to run for some weeks. The third method consists of putting a spare filter media in a tank submerged in the water aerated and fed

with some fish feed or urea. The filter media, when covered with bacteria, are slimy and

can be used in a system to speed up the nitrifying process.

The water in a good recirculation system will become brownish. This is the effect of recirculation of the water combined with some ingredients in the feed, such as blood

meal, because they are not completely decomposed by the bacteria. This process is not

harmful for the fish; as a matter of fact, catfish like to swim in this tea coloured water. It

reduces stress and helps to prevent diseases.

If the water in the recirculation system is foaming, it is a sign of pollution by dissolved

proteins in the water. This is not really a problem, but it shows that the water purification

system can barely cope with the pollution. If there is excessive bacterial growth on the filter media, it is a sign that the system is overloaded. It can also be a sign of overfeeding.

the system is overloaded. It can also be a sign of overfeeding. Uneaten feed has to be decomposed by bacteria which are different from the nitrifying bacteria. As a matter of fact, they will occupy all the space and nitrification doesn't take

place any more. This process, called mineralisation, consumes a lot of oxygen and produces take place any more.

produces excess bacterial sludge. This process will be enhanced when the sedimentation filter is

overloaded and not cleaned regularly. filter is overloaded and not cleaned regularly.

Medication and recirculation systems

In a recirculation system you can medicate the fish, but depending on the medicine or

chemicals you use, this can affect the performance of the biofilter.

Treatment with chemicals, such as formalin and potassium permanganate, will kill some of the bioflora on the filter media. After treatment, extra flushing is required to keep the levels of ammonium and nitrite low. Normally the bacterial mass will return within

a week.

Chapter 4

Other medicines, such as antibiotics, usually have no effect at all on the bioflora of the media. They specifically kill the pathogens and not the bacteria in the filter.

Salt, widely used to suppress bacterial growth and parasites, has no effect on the bioflora

of the media.

When the fish are given medicines via a bath treatment (see chapter 9 on fish diseases), it's advisable to treat the complete system and not only the culture tank. Apply the chemical in

the fish tank, but keep the pump running. By doing it this way, you avoid the fish getting

stressed. If a chemical like formalin is used, you have to increase the flushing rate in order

to remove the formalin after some hours.

The effectiveness of the medicines usually reduces with time, because they are not stable

in a water solution and the filter breaks them down too. Especially oxytetracycline which

breaks down rapidly. The water will turn dark brown within twelve hours after applying it.

Don't bother to flush it out, since the catfish like this dark tea coloured water.

Maintenance of a recirculation system

A recirculation system requires maintenance. The major maintenance consists of keeping

the components clean. When the pump gets dirty, the yield of the pump reduces gradually. It's important to clean the impeller on a monthly basis or every time the system is emptied after a growth cycle. If the system uses UV-light, the quartz glass should also be cleaned after every cycle, and checked if the UV-light still works. Ultraviolet radiation kills pathogens

and keeps the water transparent, but if the quartz glass of the UV-light is dirty, the radiation

is not optimal and will not do anything. Also, the UV-light reduces in efficiency and should be replaced on a yearly basis, even if it's still radiating UV-rays. Ultraviolet light can harm the eyes, if the eyes are directly exposed to it. So, be very careful not to look at the UV-light directly. After every growth cycle, the pipes of the recirculation system should be cleaned

inside and outside. Therefore, the pipes should have some fittings which can be easily

disconnected. Some parts inside the tank shouldn't be glued at all. Pipe brushes with a long pole can be helpful.

Any time you empty the system, the cleaning should start immediately because if the dirt dries up on the surfaces of the tank and other components, it becomes very hard to get

rid of. The filter media should be cleaned as well. A high pressure cleaner works very well

for this purpose. After cleaning, you can start another growth cycle by putting a new set of fish in the tank. If you want to do another spawning in the cleaned system, it's also advisable to disinfect with chlorine or hydrogen peroxide. After thoroughly rinsing, the system is ready for another spawning. Because the filter media will not have any bacteria

yet, keep in mind that the recirculation system has to start up afresh.

The disinfection procedure is discussed in chapter 8 on reproduction because in hatcheries disinfection is very important in order to get continuously good results.

Power supply for a recirculation system in a hatchery

The fish farm has to be run with constant light. Constant light means 24/7, without any interval of more than ten minutes.

Recirculation systems for hatchery operations do not really consume a lot of power when they are designed well. For example, a unit which can produce 120, 000 fingerlings in a

year or 40, 000 juveniles in a year, can run on a power consumption of 100 watts per hour.

The 100 watts are for the pump and the UV-light only. The consumption on a yearly basis is 900 kWh a year. The commercial rate for 1 kWh is approximately 25 and if the PHCN (Power Holding Company of Nigeria) provides power constantly, it will not be more than

22, 500 per year to run one system.

With the current prices of fingerlings at N 15/piece and N 25/piece the output is respectively N 1, 800, 000 and N 1, 000, 000. In percentage, the electricity bill is not more than 2% of

the sales price.

However, in Nigeria we cannot rely on a constant power supply. Therefore, fish farms need

a back-up with alternative sources of power, which increase the price of running a system

on electricity.

What are the alternative sources of power?

## Generator

Battery pack with inverter

Battery pack with inverter and solar panels

The cost of running a generator is almost three times higher than getting the electricity

from the PHCN. It is not only the diesel or petrol consumption, but also the maintenance needed to keep the generator working all the time, which adds seriously to the cost of producing electricity.

I believe that in order to run a hatchery with recirculation systems, you need all the sources

In a normal situation when PHCN-power is available for four to five hours a day and solar power from an average sunny day is coming in, the generator will still run for two to three hours, mainly during the night and early morning. Don't be deceived, when they offer you a

standalone system for solar, and promise you will always have power from the solar system;

The borehole system should be switched on during the hours the sun is shining brightly and the

The borehole can have a solar driven pump installed. When the output of the pump is high

enough to get enough water during the day time to also supply for the night, then it is a good

option. The capacity of the reservoir has to be calculated and should be big enough to store water for 16 hours consumption. When there is not enough sunlight available complications and shortage of water can occur because the pump will only work on DC and not on AC. So, a generator or electricity from the PHCN

cannot be used to power it, because they provide a generator or electricity from the PHCN

AC. In this case, it's advisable to have two boreholes available one on solar power and one on

conventional power as a standby for the worst-case scenario.

About solar power in generalAbout solar power in general

Solar systems that have been installed well (Photos 11 and 12), are relatively maintenance free

and reliable. The shelf life of the various components varies from twenty years for the solar

panel, ten years for the inverter to five years on average for the battery pack. The shelf life of the battery pack depends on how it is used and where it is placed; batteries should be installed in a ventilated cool, dry area. The inverter too should not be placed in the hatchery building, where it is hot and humid, but in a well-ventilated room. It is always advisable to place the where it is

hot and humid, but in a well-ventilated room. It is always advisable to place the

inverter and the battery as close together as possible.

The solar panels should be put on the roof, with more than 5 cm space between the roof and the panels, in order not to accumulate heat. If the panels are too close to the roof, they get very hot. As a result, the cables can melt and the efficiency and life span of the solar panels decrease. In many cases the solar panels are first of all placed on scaffolding and not straight

onto the roof.

Buy your solar system from a company with a proven track record. It is also advisable to buy it from a dealer who is close to your site, so that after sales service can be offered in time and when needed.

Always connect earth to the solar system and put an arrester on the roof, so that

lightning will not affect the installation. The inverter is very vulnerable to power

surges.

Buy maintenance-free deep cycle batteries. These batteries differ from normal car

batteries in the property that they can be drained completely without being spoiled.

The number of batteries should be enough to store the energy that is needed to

overcome the period in the evening, night and early morning. The size of the battery is expressed in Ah. When the battery is 12 volts, the capacity of the battery expressed in Ah can be multiplied with the voltage (V) to yield the capacity in watts (W).

Example 5. How to calculate the required solar system capacity? Suppose you have 16 batteries of 200 Ah and the voltage is 12 V. Formula: P = V x A. Total capacity in watts: 16 x 200 x 12 = 38, 400 W or 38.4

kWh.

Assume the consumption of the farm is 1.5 kWh, you can run this farm on battery for circa 20 hours (30 kWh), because it is not advisable to run the battery

totally flat. Normally the inverter will shut down when the battery drops below

20% capacity.

Assume you have a solar system and the farm takes 1.5 kWh 24/7.

The total consumption in a day is 1.5 kWh x 24=36 kWh. The solar system

works approximately 8 hours on full capacity and should be able to produce 12

kWh in this time, in the meantime being able to store 24 kWh in the batteries.

So, the capacity of the solar system should be approximately 5 kW per hour in order to take care of the farm 24/7.

Depending on the farm's power requirement, you need to have the appropriate size

of inverters, the correct number of batteries and the correct number of solar panels.

The golden rule is that the current through the wires should not exceed 100 A. If the current gets too high, it will burn the cable, which will be dangerous and expensive to replace. So, the cables would be thick. The only solution is to put the batteries in series (Figure 13). This will increase the voltage of the output, but not the amperage. That's

why you will see the inverters using a higher voltage, when the capacity increases.

Capacity of inventer: 1000 W = 83 A x 12 inventer: 2000 W = 83 A x 24 VCapacity of 4000 W =83 A x 48 V

the bottom of the pond or lake. The difference is clear. When the water is very deep, the

only way to put cages in the water is by allowing them to float at the surface with floating devices. The net will hang in the water with some weights on the edges, in order to create a cage where the fish can swim freely. If the level of the water is less than 1.2 m, you can also push sticks into the bottom of the pond or lake and attach the net along-side. These cages

are also called pen cages. Traditionally they have no bottom net, only side nets. I consider

this type of cage unsuitable for catfish, because the fish can dig in the mud and escape. In any situation the net should be enclosed on all sides except for the top. On Photo 13 you can see a module of 10 floating cages of 6 x 6 x 2 m (length x width x height).

Fish culture systems

4.3 CAGE SYSTEMS

Catfish can also be farmed in net cages floating in the water, or net cages attached to

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_044.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 13. A cage farm in a stone pitch reservoir.

Floating cages

How to avoid a floating cage drifting away?

There are two ways to get the cages fixed:

1. Anchors on the bottom of the pond, which are connected to the cages with rope.

2. The cages are connected to the shore with rope.

## Chapter 4

The first connection is the most difficult one, because the anchoring has to be done according to the size and number of the cages, the weather conditions and the current of the water in the dam or the lake. The best place for cages is where the optimal water

exchange occurs and the water is very deep. In the case of a dam, the best place for putting

cages is where the river bed was situated originally. This is the deepest place in the dam anyway. If the dam has fluctuating water levels, anchoring has to be adjustable. Anchors are more efficient at holding the cage structure in place if the bottom is soft and the anchor can dig itself into the soil. An alternative is to use concrete blocks. If the anchoring

is too light, the cages will start drifting away from the initial place. In a worst-case scenario,

you will end up losing the whole farm. Calculating the size or weight of the anchoring

system can only be done by engineers with experience in the field of cage farming.

If the cages are situated not far from the shore, it is possible to hold the cages in position

with ropes which lead to the shore and are hooked onto trees or concrete pillars. The cages

can be accessed by a jetty. This construction makes it easy to harvest and feed the fish,

because the cages are situated close by the shore.

Feeding floating feed in a cage?

Floating feed is advisable when cages are used. Sinking feed which is not directly eaten, will

just sink through the bottom of the net. This is an immediate loss. Floating feed however, can drift away through the sides of the cages, if no proper care is taken. Therefore, each net requires a feed collar. This is a small mesh size net with a width of 40 cm which is attached to the complete periphery of the cage at the surface of the water. This way the

feed cannot drift away to open water (Figure 14).

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_045.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 14. A feed collar to avoid floating feed to drift away.

Fish culture systems

Size of fish and stocking density in floating cage

Catfish should not be stocked in cages when they are very small. Their size should be at least 30 g. The juveniles first have to grow in ponds or concrete tanks to a weight of 30 g,

then they are graded and transported to the cages. Small juveniles stocked in a cage, need

a very small mesh size in order not to escape. But when they grow, the small mesh size will not allow good water exchange through the cage. Dirt will also clog the small mesh size net and eventually the net gets very heavy and difficult to handle. The diameter of the net mesh should be 1.5 to 2 cm. Furthermore, juveniles tend to get affected by bacterial

diseases in cages when they are too small. In addition, the net should not have a depth

of more than 2 m, because if the catfish start swimming up and down through the water column, they will use a lot of energy; thus the feed conversion rate will not be optimal. Densities can be as high as 100 pieces per m³.

## Cage design and construction

If the nets or cages are placed in open water, for example a lake or dam, it should be clear that any damage to the nets or cages results in immediate loss of fish, without a chance of recovering them. Net quality is therefore of utmost importance; it should be thick enough, UV-resistant, well maintained and kept in a clean environment, because rats

like to sleep and nest in it and make gaps. The specifications of nets are given in weight

per $ m_{2} $ thickness of the thread and mesh size. The nets should be knotless, so that they will not damage the bodies of the fish during the harvest. Any time a net is placed in the cage, it has to be thoroughly checked for gaps. Nets are made of several materials, either nylon or polyethylene is most commonly used.

Nets are vulnerable at their corners, especially when weights are put there which are not

supported by a rope but instead are hanging on the net itself. In rough weather conditions

nets can be shaken and tear apart after a period of time, resulting in large gaps.

If nets are placed in a big pond and the pond can be drained, escaped catfish are only a

temporary loss, because they can always be caught again.

Cages can be built in any size. It depends on how many fish you want to sell in a year and your marketing strategy. A good size for example is a cage of 6 x 6 x 2 m, especially when galvanised pipes are used, because they have a length of 6 m. Stocking this cage with

100 pieces per m $ _{3} $ results in about 7000 pieces. Growing them to 1.5 kg average, you can

expect a harvest of 10, 000 kg per growth cycle.

Cages in Nigeria are often built with galvanised pipes; two lines of galvanised pipes are welded together approximately 45 cm apart. In between these pipes, plastic drums are placed to create a floating platform. The nets can be hanged into the inner square of

square of 6 x 6 m. The outer square is around 6.4 x 6.4 m. The plastic drums m (length x width). The plastic drums are

## Chapter 4

usually 200 l. Check them thoroughly for leakages and seal the covers carefully, so that water cannot enter. For a cage of 6 x 6 m, use two drums on each side, making it eight drums altogether. The drums are lashed with rope between the galvanised pipes. Use good

quality marine rope which is UV-resistant. The rope which you buy on the side of the road

will not last longer than ten months.

Also, other options for making cages are available; there is one Nigerian company that produces floating elements of good quality plastic which can be mounted together. The

nets can be placed inside them. It is more expensive, but more durable.

If you want to start a megaproject in cage farming, you can also contact overseas companies. They can give you turnkey solutions, including the anchoring system, predator nets, harvesting devices, ponton boats etcetera. Off course, buying from these companies

comes at a price.

Cage farming of catfish is feasible, although currently you mainly see cage farms producing tilapia in Ogun and Oyo State at the dams.

## Predators

Putting cages in a natural environment, attracts a lot of fish-eating birds and if not taken care of, this will certainly lead to severe losses. The most common birds are the kingfisher, the heron, the hammerhead bird and the cormorant. Within days of stocking, they will spot your site and immediately start to hunt; even when you have not seen any of those

birds when building the project. The evidence apart from seeing them on the cages, are

the faeces, feathers and wounded fish. A bird net to protect your fish on top of the cage is obligatory.

Less obvious are the predators in the water, for instance monitor lizards, when cages are close to shore, crocodiles and tiger fish. If they enter the cages, they have already damaged

the nets. The loss mainly consists of fish that have escaped through the gaps in the nets,

because more fish escape than the predators actually eat. To overcome this problem, you can put an extra strong net around the net in which the fish are contained. This net is called a predator net, which is a very strong coarse 3 to 5 cm diameter netting. The net cannot be damaged by crocodiles or any other animal with sharp teeth. An extra advantage is that

fish which escape from the first net, will still be trapped in the second net as long as they

are big enough. Between the first net and the predator net a population of young wild fish can grow and eventually not escape the predator net anymore because of their bigger size by then. These fish are attracted and grow in this environment because of the faeces of the catfish, uneaten feed and the benthos living on the nets.

68

## Applying for a license

When you start a cage farm in a dam, you have to apply for a license from the water authorities of the federal government who are in charge of the dam. After you have been

Fish culture systems

handed over the necessary documents, you will usually get a license for a certain area of

water defined by coordinates, where you can start your operations. The security of the operations is not the responsibility of the government, but has to be provided for by you. In order to get a good consensus with the people who live around the dam, you should visit them, explain your activities and tell them about the benefits of your presence. Employ

people (ex-fishermen) from the communities around the lake. Mark the area, which is

meant for the cage farm with floater balls, so that people know that this is a no-go area

for them.

The security of the farm can be a big problem, especially if the operations of the farm are small and cannot pay off for the expenses made to secure the place. Most cage farms in

Nigeria have a respectable size and, apart from having cages on the water, they also have

land-based activities, such as hatcheries, nursery ponds and accommodations.

Harvesting catfish from floating cagesHarvesting catfish from floating cages

Harvesting the catfish from the cages, is not so easy especially if the construction aside

from the cage is small and cheaply built with small planks. In principle harvesting consists

of just lifting the net and crowding the fish together in one corner,

scooping them up with of just lifting the net and crowding the fish together in one corner, scooping them up with a basket or catcher and carrying them to the shore or to the boat, depending on whether the cage farm is situated at the shore with a jetty or is a standalone cage in open water. If the nets have weights in the corners, they should be hung on a rope and taken out before

the net is lifted. A long bamboo stick is helpful to lift the net to one side in order to reduce

the volume of the net gradually, while shifting the bamboo stick from left to right. When the nets are crowded enough, you can start to catch the fish. When you want to take a break from catching the fish, you lower the net so that the fish are able to swim freely again and are not exposed to the sun.

Maintenance of floating cages

Maintenance of the nets is required to make sure they don't contain any gaps. After each growth cycle you can dry the net and clean it, if excessive algae or other debris are attached. The shelf life of a net depends on the quality, but after five to seven years the

nets should be replaced for new ones. Losing a batch of fish because the net has gaps.

costs more than replacing the net for a new one. Nets outside the water should be hung

and dried in a dry area not exposed to sunlight and free from rodents.

Security of floating cages

As already mentioned before, when the area you are farming consists of a cage in open

everyone too. The night however needs special attention.

The place is dark and open. In order to secure the place, you can work with solar lights,

sensitivity cameras and security guards on the water or on the jetty. Apart from theft of fish, the nets can be vandalised, which brings you even more losses when the fish escape. In my opinion, cage farming in open water is a business for well organised companies with good structures on the ground and on a scale, which allows good investments and

Water quality in dams and lakesWater quality in dams and lakes

The water quality of dams fluctuates with the seasons. During the rainy season the levels of nutrients reduce but the suspended solid level increases, which makes the water more

spending money on security operations.

turbid. The water temperature also varies with the seasons. It is lowest during harmattan

and highest during the dry season. The fluctuations are not that drastic for the fish and both in dry and rainy seasons there is usually no

problem with the water quality. There both in dry and rainy seasons there is usually no is however one exception, which happens occasionally, once a year. The water from the bottom of the dam flows upwards, which results in mixing of water layers from the bottom

and the surface of the dam. This normally doesn't happen. This process causes bad odours

from hydrogen sulphide and methane gases and depletion of oxygen at the surface of the water for some days. Tilapia especially are sensitive to this situation and it can cause increased mortality. Usually after some days the mixing process stabilises; at that point even the natural fish in the water show signs of intoxication, although they have the opportunity

to swim away.

4.4 EXTENSIVE POND CULTURES

can be used to build one. materials which

The difference between the flow-through system usually concrete tanks, and the pond system, is the size at which they operate and their stocking density.

Ponds: 1000-5000 $ m_{2} $, stocking density 5-10 pieces/$ m_{2} $ preferably earth pond.

Tanks: 50-100 $ m_{2} $, stocking density 50-100 pieces/$ m_{2} $ preferably concrete tank.

Ponds, especially earthen ponds which consists of clay, tend to be large sized with a surface area of 1000 msurface area of $ 1 0 0 0 \mathrm{m}_{2 2} $ or more. They are located in rural areas where land is abundant,

and a sufficient water source is able to keep the ponds filled even during the dry season.

Flushing is restricted to keep the ponds filled, because the release of nutrients by the fish is neutralized by the algae in the water and the binding activity of the soil. In other words, the ponds, if run extensively, can take care of the waste. Therefore, only at the end of the

growth cycle, extra flushing is advisable.

Due to evaporation and seepage, the water consumption can be as high as 100-200 as 100-200 m $ ^{33} $ per hectare per day during the dry season. Catfish do well in this natural environment. The mortality rate is usually low, but the level of predation by birds, monitor lizards and other

animals is higher than in intensive systems. Feed conversion rates tend to be slightly higher

in earthen ponds too, because of the increased ability of the fish to swim around, which takes more energy. Hybrid catfish do very well in extensive earthen ponds and appear to adapt more to this natural environment than the pure Clarias gariepinus strain.

## 4.5 BACKYARD FARMING

Backyard farming is not really an alternative farming system, but it's worth emphasizing the principle and the advantages. Each of the farming systems mentioned before, can be used,

but in almost all cases the backyard farm that works with these systems, uses the concrete

pond for the flow-through system.

Backyard farms are small-scale farms situated in the garden of a house. The business is run by the family members, security, staff etcetera. The beauty of the backyard farm is

the combination of interest; the water and electricity supplies support the house as well

as the fish farm. The security and people are already there and they can easily take care of a small-scale fish farm. So, you don't have extra costs, apart from buying feed and fingerlings. The size of the farm is small and you wish to sell the fish to retail not all at once. This is very possible if you live in a residential area. You can even add value to the fish by

smoking them. This way sales can be done any time you want, because the fish have been

preserved. A backyard farm is also very good as a starting point for learning the ins and outs of fish farming. These provide for a basis for setting up a farm later on in a larger and more professional way in a designated area where there is enough water and land.

The waste water of a backyard farm can be a problem, if there isn't a good drainage

system in the residential area. The water, in particular the water with solid waste, can be used in the garden, but the majority of the water will have to go out of the compound into the gutters. If the waste water remains around the compound, it will start to smell and attract mosquitoes and rodents, and your neighbours will start complaining!

income should not depend on it when you

are a newcomer in the business.

There is nothing wrong with thinking big, but start small. As a matter of fact, many entrepreneurs who start big, fail and turn away disappointed and broke from the business of fish farming.

Chapter 5

5.1 INTRODUCTION

A fish pond is defined as a water body which has an inlet and an outlet in order to manage

the pond when it comes to draining, flushing and harvesting. If a pond does not have

those features, it is not a fish pond in my opinion. In any case, a fish pond is not just a hole

Building a pond and the choice of materials depend on many factors:

Financial capacity

5.2 EARTHEN POND

If the soil holds water, which occurs when the soil consists of a minimum of 30% of clay,

you have the possibility of constructing an earthen pond (Photo 14). It is important that the dykes of the pond are well constructed and well compacted; they should not contain any stones or other materials, because they make the dyke permeable and weak. Usually the dykes of a pond have a slope of 30-45 degrees and a depth of 1.5 m. The water level

should be 1.2 m which provides for a freeboard of 0.3 m. Small ponds of 100-300 $ m_{2} $ can

be excavated manually, but bigger ponds require machines for excavating and compacting. The top soil should not be mixed with the lower soil layers and should be placed back on the dykes and roads. Grass should be planted on top of the dykes in order to avoid erosion. Constructing an earthen pond should be done by experienced people. A surveyor has to be

involved in order to get the levels correct. An earthen pond is, as I stated in the introduction

of this chapter, definitely not just a hole in the ground. This book is not meant to be a manual for constructing an earthen pond, but it offers you an idea of the requirements for such a construction.

Many farmers use bags filled with soil to make dykes; I do not believe this is a durable

solution. The bags certainly do not seal the dyke but they avoid erosion and reduce the

## seepage.

Earthen ponds are usually operated extensively. The stock of fish varies from 5 to 20 pieces

per $ m_{2} $. Earthen ponds need a lot of space and a lot of water due to evaporation and

Choice of materials for fish farms, sizes, shapes and numbers

seepage. During the dry season evaporation can go up to 2 cm per day, which means 20

m of water has to be added daily into a 1000 m2 pond to keep the water level constant. Because in an earthen pond the soil and the water interact, the catfish really like this kind

of pond. Their nick name is mud fish for a reason; they especially like the bottom of the

pond. The only challenge of an earthen pond can be harvesting the fish, if the bottom he fish, if the bottom of the pond is very muddy and the pond cannot be drained completely. Any fish left, will seriously interfere with the next stock of juveniles. The soil can be disinfected with lime after every drain or harvest and dried during the dry season. After some years, you will

have to take out the excessive sludge. This sludge is perfect for improving the quality of any

soil for farming crops, because it increases the organic matter in the soil.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_047.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 14. An earthen pond.

5.3 PLASTIC LINED POND

If you are interested in building a natural pond but the soil does not hold water, you

can dig a pond in the same shape as an earthen pond and put a plastic lining in (Photo 15). For a plastic lined pond, it is important that the surface of the soil is smooth and does not contain any sharp objects which can puncture the lining. Also, the lining should be 1 mm thick and UV-resistant. UV-resistant means that sunlight doesn't spoil

the lining and eventually cause it to crack after some time. The standard UV-resistant

lining is not available in Nigeria, so it has to be imported. If the pond is big, the lining will be delivered in pieces and will have to be welded together. This is a job for a specialist with a special welding machine. If the welding is not carried out well, after

some months or years the lining will just fall apart due to the detrimental effects of the

wind and other weather conditions.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_048.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 15. A plastic lined pond.

If you want a natural looking pond, but the soil is not suitable and plastic lining is not

available, you still have another alternative which is a stone pitched pond (Photo 16). In my opinion, stone pitching should only be carried out in such a way that the soil is well stabilized and erosion will not be a factor, otherwise it will undermine the stone pitching after some period of time. Stone pitched walls should be 12 cm thick and only be built

by experienced masons in this field of expertise. Stone pitched ponds are not completely

sealed, but that is not a problem because flushing and adding water is part of the water management anyway. The slope of the dykes is the same as for earthen and plastic liner ponds, which is 30-45 degrees.

Choice of materials for fish farms, sizes, shapes and numbers

A farm I visited, complained about unrecorded losses of fish from its stone pitched ponds. There were actually so many lost that the farm was not making any profit. Theft is always an excuse, but sometimes theft is not the reason and you have to

look further into it. I found out that monitor lizards can be a serious threat if the

environment is conducive for them. After one year, stone pitched ponds which are not built very strongly, will show openings between the stones or even worse, stones will fall out. This environment is ideal for monitor lizards to hide in. They dig a hole behind the stone pitching where they have shelter. In early morning and evening

those lizards will be hunting your fish and you will actually have a lizard farm instead

of a fish farm!

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_049.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

## 5.5 CONCRETE TANKS: FULL CONCRETE BLOCKS OR COMBINED

In all situations it's possible to build tanks of concrete or blocks. This type of pond can be seen everywhere at small and large farms in remote or urban areas (Photo 17). If constructed well, they last forever and are easy to maintain. These ponds have vertical walls and harvesting the fish is slightly easier too.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_050.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Chapter 5

The photo gallery in Appendix 4 shows you how to build a complete farm with reinforced blocks. In Appendix 5 a detailed bill of quantity for a full concrete tank versus a tank with reinforced blocks is offered.

The density of stocking depends on the flow rate of the water but can be as high as 100 pieces per $ m_{2} $. Because of the costs of a concrete pond, the strategy is to farm as intensively as possible.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_051.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

## 5.6 PLASTIC TANK

In Nigeria, there are manufacturers that produce ready-to-use plastic tanks for fish culture (Photo 18). They are available in different sizes and usually have a circular shape. The

volumes of the tanks vary from 500 to 50001. The tanks have a disadvantage though.

Because the bottoms are not flat, harvesting fish from these tanks is difficult. To overcome this problem, you can put a layer of concrete on the bottom to cover and level it. This also makes the tanks very strong. The outlet should be positioned right at the bottom so that the tank can be drained till the last drop.

Choice of materials for fish farms, sizes, shapes and numbers

Plastic tanks are very good for the pre on-growing stage. At these stages the fish weigh between and 50 g, which is between the hatchery and the grow-out stage (see Appendix 1 for the growth stages of catfish). For small scale farmers these tanks can also be used for grow-out. Appendix 1).

Plastic tanks are circular because this shape makes them strong and most cost-effective, compared to square or rectangular tanks.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_052.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Fibreglass or polyester tanks are not very common in Nigeria. But there is an industry that produces boats using the same material. On request a company is able to produce fish tanks too. As long as the tanks are made correctly, they are very durable and suitable for fish farming. The sizes are in the same range as for the plastic tanks between 500 to 1000 fish farming.

1, and can be rectangular or circular (Photo 19).

## 5.8 SHAPE OF THE POND

You want to build a pond which is efficient and as cheap as possible. This can be expressed

as costs of material per $ m_{3} $ of the tank. More interesting to know is that with tanks of the

same volume a rectangular shape is more expensive than the square one and a square tank is more expensive than a circular one. In addition, bigger sized tanks will be cheaper than smaller sized tank per unit of volume.

Compare the following tank sizes with the same volume:

20 x 5 x 1 m rectangular tank: 100 m $ ^{3} $ (length x width x height)

10 x 10 x 1 m square tank: 100 $ \mathrm{m_{3}} $ (length x width x height)

Diameter 11.2 circular tank: 100 mDiameter 11.2 circular tank: 100 m $ _{33} $ $ ((\pi r^{\wedge}\pi r_{2} x height)_{2} x height) $

Comparing the costs of building a tank is done by calculating the surface area of each tank, because the more material you use, the more expensive the tank will be, whether it is built in plastic, concrete, blocks or stone pitching.

Choice of materials for fish farms, sizes, shapes and numbers

20 x 5 x 1 m rectangular tank: 150 m $ \mathrm{m_{2}} $ 10 x 10 x 1 m square tank: 140 $ \mathrm{m_{2}} $ 11.2 diameter circular tank: 135 $ \mathrm{m_{2}} $

The rectangular tank has 15 m $ ^{2} $ more material and is therefore 11% more expensive than a circular tank.

The advantages and disadvantages of circular, rectangular and squaretanks

## Circular tanks

Advantages

Relatively cheap in material costs.

Strong.

Self-cleaning and no corners where waste or dead fish can accumulate.

Disadvantages

More difficult to harvest the fish.

Setting up a farm consumes a lot of space because the tanks have no mutual walls; have no mutual walls; tanks stand on their own. all tanks stand on their own.

## Rectangular and square tanks

Advantages

- Efficient in setting up the farm with little spacing or no spacing at all between the tanks.

- Easy to harvest compared to circular tanks because the fish can be concentrated into the corners.

Disadvantages

- More expensive in material costs.

- Accumulation of dead fish and waste in the corners if the flow rate is insufficient.

I estimate that in Nigeria 50% of fish production is done in earthen ponds, 40% in concrete

ponds, 5% in plastic lined ponds and the remaining 5% in the other alternatives such as plastic

tanks, fibreglass tanks etcetera.

Most farmers prefer rectangular tanks. This is a good choice, but for small tanks you often see

Chapter 5

In Appendix 5 you can find a bill of quantity (BOQ) for a 10 x 5 x 1.3 m pond made out of reinforced blocks or full concrete with early 2019 prices.

## 5.9 POND SIZE AND NUMBER

When you are ready to start building ponds, you probably have already chosen the shape of the pond and the material you want to use, but you have not yet decided how big the

ponds should be. How big should a pond be? For the on-growing stage of the growth

cycle, the pond should be of a size which enables the stocked fish to be sold within a week when harvest is due. You also have to determine the number

of sales days you want to have in a year. The more times you want to sell the more ponds you need to build. It is advisable to have regular sales, for example on a weekly basis. This allows you to build a

customer base with regular customers.

Example 6. How to calculate the number of ponds you need?

Suppose your production is 100 tons a year and you want to sell on a weekly basis.

This means 52 sales moments or days in a year. Let's assume the growth cycle of the

fish is 175 days; in this case the fish remain in the pond from stocking till harvest

during 175 days. This means you can do 2 cycles in a year. Each pond has 2 harvests in a year. So, for sales on a weekly basis, you need 52/2=26 ponds! This means you stock on a weekly basis and you harvest on a weekly basis. If you want to sell on a monthly basis, you need 12/2=6 ponds.

Many new farmers are tempted to stock all the ponds at once. This will not work atall. You will get a serious problem when the fish are ready for harvest. There are four

Your working capital to grow all the fish at once, is very high.

reasons:

You have to sell all the fish in a short period of time.

Customers cannot buy regularly but only a couple of times a year.

Your need for water is very high just before the sales whereas it drops

to almost zero after the sales.

When the ponds are too big and the sales from one pond are spread over a longer period, let's say three weeks, the result will be bad. The fish from the first sales will be bigger than the fish sold after three weeks. Because during these three weeks feed will be given

periodically, the fish will be severely stressed so that they eat without growing.

84Appendixes 2 and 3 show how the maximum working capital increases with only two sales in a year compared to twelve sales in a year.

Another problem I notice is that many fish farms operate with different sizes of ponds. To

manage this is very difficult, because all the ponds will have a different number of fish and the feeding regime has to be adapted for each single tank. Also, the sales quantities are not regular, they depend on the size of the pond that is harvested. If you want a smooth and easy operation, you need to build all the ponds the same size.

## 6

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_054.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

## HOW TO SET UP A FISH FARM

Chapter 6

Setting up a fish farm is not the goal, but just a tool in order to start farming fish. I have seen investors who love to build a farm, but when it comes to farming, they are nowhere to be seen. The joy is over!

When you have found the best location and have acquired the land, it's time to start. The first step to take, is making a survey of the land including all the levels of the land, where there is water and the distances involved.

With this survey you can start making the design and put all the facilities into place (Figure

15). The design can also be used to make an investment plan, a production plan and a profitability and cash flow projection. You will find more about in chapter 12 on the economics of fish farming.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_055.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

A fish farm needs the following facilities:

## Fence or wall

Fish farming is a capital-intensive business. When the ponds are not protected, you will certainly get theft problems. It is not only birds with feathers which can take your fish,

also birds without feathers can do that! A fence or a wall can be constructed with blocks

How to set up a fish farm

or it can be a wire fence. Both will serve the purpose. When the area is very swampy, it's advisable to make a fence out of wire. It is wise to build the enclosure before starting any other job.

## Fish pondsFish ponds

The fish ponds are usually located between the lowest and highest level of the land. The storage reservoir is normally situated at the highest level and the drainage at the lowest level. If the land does not have many differences of level, you must create levels and slopes,

level. If the land does not have many differences of level, you must create levels and slopes,

in order to have the correct flow of water. The ponds should be easily accessible by car,

tractor or at least a wheelbarrow for a small farm in order to provide the feed and transport the fish when they are due to harvest. Most investors start by building ponds but instead they should first start with the roads and water infrastructure. Fish don't grow in a don't grow in a concrete pond; they grow in water. Without water the ponds are useless

## Power house

If PHCN-electricity is available, the generator house should be located close to where the PHCN-power comes into the farm. Since it is important that this spot is supervised, it should not be situated far away from the security house. Normally you will see the power

house, security house and gate house located close together or close to the gate.

Gate house or security house

The gate house is the place where goods, services and people coming in or coming out, are recorded. It is very important for security to check the inflow and outflow, and be aware

of what is going on. Another aspect of the gate house involves biosecurity. Don't allow

people to enter the farm with contaminated materials. People should be directed to the person they want to see. They should not start walking around the farm unattended.

In bigger farms, it's advisable to give visitors a pass which clearly shows they are a visitor. Thus, the gate house plays an important part in keeping the environment safe and theft-

proof!

Accommodation for the staff

Most investors do not give too much attention to accommodations for the staff. They come with costs and do not benefit the production. However, the farm will always have some key

staff walking around during the night. If they are not comfortable, this will certainly affect

their performance. So, if your ambition is to develop a big farm, you should also take in consideration that staff accommodation is a serious matter. Water, light, security, a bed, a kitchen, a shower and a toilet are the basics for workers staying 24/7 at the farm. Many investors have in mind to provide all those things when they start making money; but the

sad story is, this way the money will never come!

Hatchery-, pre- and on-growing pondsHatchery-, pre- and on-growing ponds

Depending on what you want to do and the size of the farm you wish to have, a hatchery and an outdoor facility to grow fingerlings and juveniles (Photo 24) to the stage of post-juveniles stage of post juveniles

prior to stocking the outgrow facility, are important. See Appendix 1 for the growth stages of

the fish.

Farms with the ambition to produce over 50 tons of fish each year, should consider having their own hatchery, but they will certainly need a facility to grow juveniles and fingerlings to post-

juveniles. Farms that rely on supplies from other hatcheries for stocking fish, can become very

disappointed in terms of quality and regular supply of the fish. This will result in periods without stocking and inevitably no supply after five to six months. A farm depending on an erratic supply of fingerlings cannot

Water storage facility and boreholes

Water is the lifeline of the farm. After building a fence or wall, this should actually be the second action to be taken. When you have drilled a borehole and made the water storage facility and installed the supply line, this will also supply your needs when you build the remaining structures, because for building you need water! A survey of the land in order to get a good spot for drilling

a borehole does not guarantee a steady supply for water and a good yield. The proof of the

pudding is in the eating! After drilling and putting the borehole pump into place, you will find

out the real capacity of it. This will help you to decide how many tanks you can build.

Intake from a river or dam

The intake is actually the heart of your farm; it is the supply line of water. The dimensions of the

intake should be determined by the water needs of the farm. A river or dam contains normally more than enough water to supply the farm. Officially when you start a farm and you take more than 250 m $ ^{a} $ of water in a day, you need a license from the river basins development authorities,

which operate at state level. A license can only be issued if you make an environmental

assessment report. When you start small, you will get away with pumping water from a river or

dam, but if you want to start a big farm, sooner or later this organisation will catch up with you.

It is better to face the music before starting to dance!

Materials and feed storage

Storage facilities for materials and feed can be built with concrete blocks, but I prefer 20- or

40-foot containers (Photo 20). These containers are well protected against rodents and can be closed and easily protected from theft. You need to roof the container in order to keep the heat out. This is important when stocking feed. Usually you make a base to put the container on, so that flooding or rainwater will not disturb it. Storage of feed should be done in a strategic

location for easy access.

graders, catchers, baskets, scales, drag nets etcetera. All these materials should be kept in a dry place. As far as the nets are concerned, it is important to store them in a rodent free area. Rats and

How to set up a fish farm

mice especially like to make nests in nets, which leads to large holes if they are not taken

good care of. When you leave your harvesting equipment close to the ponds, you make a tempting environment for theft. After use, harvesting equipment should be locked up at all times.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_056.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 20. Feed or materials storage, made from 40-foot containers.

## Administration block

When the farm is relatively small, all those facilities mentioned above, can be combined in a multifunctional building.

and petty cash can be received. In the administration block you can find a cashier, an

accountant, a marketing or sales manager, the staff manager and the store keeper. But if the farm is small it will be just one person doing everything. So, a small farm needs a general manager who understands all the disciplines and is able to handle them.

## Point of sale

When the farm is small, you will most likely want to sell your fish close to the ponds, because that is where the fish are harvested. But this is not an ideal situation, because a point of sale

near the ponds will disturb the fish in the other ponds. Also, for biosecurity reasons it is not

advisable to allow buyers to come near to the ponds with their dirty baskets.

Selling fish in all situations, should be carried out under shade conditions with no exposure to sun, with access to clean cold water supplied by a hose from a tanker or storage tank, and a

smooth floor that will not damage the skin of the fish when they accidentally fall out of the

basket (Photo 21). The simplest way is to put a plastic lining on the floor where you weigh the fish and sell them. Ideally, there should be drainage to allow excess water to flow out.

If you want to make a point of sale at your farm, it should be close to the gate and the administration block with easy access for customers. Consequently, the fish harvested from

the ponds, should be transported to the point of sale.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_057.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 21. A point of sale at a fish farm.

## Internal roads and drainage system

To fast track operations, you will need internal roads and drainage (Photos 22 and 23). The easiest way to make a road is with gravel and capstone. On the blueprint of the farm it should be clear where roads are needed. The levels on the land will show you where the gutters and drainage

systems are needed in order to release excess water either from the farm or from the rain.

Neglecting roads and drainage will result in a muddy, dirty place, which makes operatingsmoothly difficult.

## Chapter 7

Some years ago, I went to a big farm. I was asked to analyse the farm, since the proft they were making was not encouraging at all. They wanted to know what actually was going on. So, I investigated the farm by moving around with all the

staff for a couple of days without interfering in their behaviour and handling. Feed

is a crucial aspect in the economics of fish farming, since it is by far the highest cost factor. I noticed that the people dealing with feed, were not experienced. Actually, neither the farm's supervisor nor any of the senior staff were involved in the feeding. They left the feeding to IT-students, day laborers and low-rated workers without

supervision. So, the feeding was carried out badly without any vision and any idea

of how to grow fish. The senior workers remained in the office, equipped with air conditioning and gossiping the entire day. Feeding fish is the main

job of the day and should always be supervised by the most experienced staff. At feeding time, you interact with your fish. This provides information on how the fish are doing in relation

to their health and growth. Never allow feeding to be carried out by inexperienced

and unmotivated workers!

## 7.1 THE GROWTH CURVE OF CATFISH

The growth curve of most animals has an S-shape; catfish are no exception. Figure 16 shows a slow growth in the first two months: from 0.002 g as a fry to 5 g as a juvenile (see Appendix 1 for catfish growth stages). From this stage the growth accelerates till they reach 1 kg in a period of four months. From 1 kg onwards, the growth rate

declines, reaching to almost zero when the maximum end weight of 3 to 4 kg is

## reached.

Catfish actually never stop growing. Depending on environmental factors and feed, they keep on growing, but only very slowly after a certain point. Brood stock which is

well fed and taken care of, can reach up to 8 kg in two years!

The growth curve of catfish depends on the feed quality, the quality of the environment, the genetics of the catfish strain and the water temperature. The growth curve shown in Figure 16 is based on an ambient temperature of 25-27 $ ^{\circ} $ C and a high-quality extruded feed with a protein content of at least 45% at the beginning of the growth

curve and 40% once they reach the adult size.

The growth curve shows an average of the total population of the fish. If the individual growth of the catfish is used, the growth curve will show an enormous variation.

The range of growth is shown in Figures 17 and 18 and is based on the Gaussian

distribution. The chart in Figure 17 shows an ideal range of growth. The chart in Figure 18

shows the range of growth in a batch of fish with a lot of growth variation. This implies

that the farmer is less skilful in reaching his target of 1.5 kg.

Figure 16. The growth curve for the African catfish.

## Feed and feeding

As fish farmers, we are not necessarily interested in individual growth rate figures, we

want to know the average growth rate. When a farmer tells you that fish can reach 1 kg in

three months, he is most likely talking about a shooter that has reached this weight at the expense of other fish. When it comes to selecting brood stock, it can be useful to select the fast-growing fish, but not the shooters. They are cannibals.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_062.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_063.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Grading fish before stocking them has been done badly: the runts and shooters

were not taken out.

Disease problems have occurred during the growth cycle.

Feeding has been carried out erratically.

The genetics of the stocked fish originated from different batches and were of

poor quality.

This results in a poor survival rate and reduced profit.

How to minimize the growth range?

You can minimize the growth range of the fish by grading them very uniformly, before

final stocking into the grow-out pond. The juveniles should all be from the same mother and father (full siblings! ) The moment you have stocked juveniles from different genetic backgrounds, there will be growth variation resulting in cannibalism, feed competition and higher feed conversion rates.

Chapter 7

7.3 FEED QUALITY

A definition of a good quality fish feed is a feed that meets all the nutritional requirements.

of the fish. So, the first thing you have to do is find out what they are. Luckily this has been of the fish. Luckily this has been

done in many studies and experiments at scientific and practical level. It is important to know, that a catfish is basically carnivorous, which makes the requirements for protein, in particular animal protein, relatively high. The digestive system is short and any ingredient which is not easily digestible, will be less beneficial for their growth.

So, making a good quality catfish feed, is easy in principle. The challenge however, is to at a competitive price! Prices of fish feed ingredients change almost on a daily basis; so, the formula for the feed is not static but a continuous process of adjusting it to the low-cost formulation, without reducing the quality of the

feed. Prices of ingredients are changing constantly due to demand and availability. The

availability changes when the harvest of important ingredients, such as soya, goes up or down. The availability of fish meal depends on climate factors; it is a product which is harvested from natural resources and limited available. Therefore, it is subject to large price fluctuations. fluctuations.

Some ingredients contain essential nutritional factors. Without these ingredients the fish feed will not be complete. This will result in fish developing problems like ceasing growth and/or getting sick. For example, the essential amino acids in proteins cannot be replaced by any other amino acid. The same is true for vitamins and minerals. If the feed doesn't

provide the basic requirements for these nutrients, the fish will certainly become sick and

die.

Fish feed can be seen as a chain of ingredients which meet the requirements of the fish. If

which meet the requirements of the fish. If one link in the chain is not sufficient, the chain will be as weak as the weakest link.

Making your own feed is not something you can do overnight!

Besides the feed formula, the appearance of the feed influences the quality and performance of the feed too. of the feed too.

## Uniformity

Feed is produced in different sizes. Depending on the size of the fish, the feed size will

be bigger or smaller. The range of feed is shown in Appendix 6. High quality feed has be bigger or smaller. High quality feed has uniform particle sizes which all have the same appearance. Also, you cannot distinguish the ingredients inside the particles, such as corn, because they have been ground finely. Well ground feed is more stable in water and is easier to digest.

## Water stability

The feed is given to the fish in the water and, if it is not eaten immediately, it can disintegrate and is wasted. Starter feeds, especially those which do not float, should be water stable for

some time. The choice of ingredients and the machines used to produce the pellets, make

feed water stable.

## Palatability

The feed should be tasty for the fish. This can be achieved with ingredients such as blood meal

and fish oil. Special products can be added to the formula in order to improve the taste even

more. As a result, the fish will eat more feed more quickly and the growth rate will improve.

The feed should be dust free. Feed factories have a special machine to separate the dust from

the feed particles. The dust is reclaimed in the process, so it's not wasted. However, if the feed

does contain dust, it only pollutes the water and it doesn't benefit the fish at all. If the feed is not up thorough handling in bags, for example carrying and piling up, it can cause a lot of dust. dust.

## Floating

If the feed can float, it will allow you to have a good view of the feeding behaviour of the catfish. You will immediately notice when the fish have had enough. This way overfeeding can be easily avoided. Floating feed usually is produced with extruder pelletizing machines. Another advantage of feed from this kind of machine, is that it is more digestible because it Another advantage of feed

has been processed under high temperatures.

## Expiry date

The expiry date of purchased feedshould not be within three months. Feedmillers can achieve months. Feed millers can achieve this by drying the feed to at least 90% dry weight and adding antifungal additives.

7.4 IS IT ADVISABLE TO MAKE YOU OWN FEED?

Many fish farmers think about making their own feed. They believe it is something is something they

can do easily alongside farming the fish. In their opinion it is also very profitable because it

reduces the production costs of the fish. All this is based on assumptions and gossip from other farmers. It's an idea born out of ignorance, because if you know all the ins and outs of feed milling, you will certainly think twice before starting a feed mill yourself.

Starting your own feed mill should only be considered if there is no alternative. Don't be a jack

of all trades and master of none!

Nowadays Nigeria has at least four professional feed millers with the professional equipment, purchased from overseas and owned by multinationals based in Europe and the USA. Their scale of production is massive (2000-4000 tons per month) and efficient. They have good

connections for purchasing raw materials at competitive prices and laboratory facilities

to check the quality of the raw materials. They use software to change the feed formula based on the low-cost formulation without minimizing quality. Because quality control is carried out during the entire production process, the feed always has a consistent quality. The prices for feed are very competitive, because feed millers need this scale of production

in order to survive. Net profit margins are less than 10%. They employ a lot of marketers

and have a wide distribution network. Before starting your own feed mill at farm level, you have to ask yourself: "Can I compete with companies like this? And, is it not better to have a good agreement with a feed mill to purchase from them instead of producing it myself?

Let's have a look at a professional feed mill and list all the stages which feed ingredients go through, before they become fish feed (Figure 20).

- Warehouse for stocking ingredients such as soya, corn, fish meal, concentrate,

pre-mixes etcetera. Intake of feed ingredients; from a bunker to the hammer mill.

From the hammer mill to the mixer.

From the mixer to the extruder or pelletizing machine, where the ingredients aretransformed into pre-feed.

From the extruder to a dryer, where the pre-feed is dried.

From the dryer to a screener to get rid of dust?

From the screener to a coating machine where the feed possibly is coated withfish oil or soya oil.

From the coating machine to the weighing and packaging machine.

## From the packaging machine to a warehouse for fish feed where it is ready to be

sold.

Additional equipment and facilities

- Boiler to produce steam for extruding the feed or pelletizing the feed

- Laboratory for quality control

<div align="center">
