84

Oct The water temperature is considered to be optimal for hatching and rearing fry when it is

29 to 31 °C. The periods in December, January and February are considered too cold for successful spawning, if measures to heat the water during the night are not taken, especially for Abuja and Jos, because the

harmattan in these regions has a serious impact on the temperature from evening till dawn. Lagos has the best climate for a catfish hatchery. The

nights are not too cold and the fluctuations in temperature are less than in the middle belt

or the highlands, such as Jos. When the water temperature is 25 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $ or below, the hatching of eggs and even the absorption of the yolk sacs will be significantly delayed. Also, the fry start eating only after 2.5 to 3 days instead of after 2 days. Their behaviour will be sluggish and the fry will not be as strong 30 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C}.

Chapter 8

The height of a hatchery building should be less than 4 m and it should not be furnished with a ceiling. The roof should be dark coloured so that it will absorb heat and the water will at least be heated during the daytime. Minimise ventilation, especially during the night.

The building should be air tight. During harmattan the humidity is very low. This causes

a lot of evaporation and as a result the water cools down even more. When the building is airtight, you increase the level of humidity which will result in less evaporation and the water will cool down less.

If maintaining the temperature of the water above 27 $ ^{\circ} $ C is a serious problem for you, you

have the option to add extra heating. Glowing charcoal can be used to heat the air. Be sure the charcoal has stopped fuming before putting it in the hatchery room. Heating the water with an electric heater is another option to increase the water temperature, but make sure that the heater cannot be in direct contact with the fish and that it does not touch any

walls. If you use electrical heaters in the water always turn them off before you put your

hands in the water. Some heaters have a built-in thermostat, others are just heating the water till you turn them off.

Solar heaters are another option for heating the water, and as a matter of fact they work very well, because Nigeria has a high level of sunshine. If you make one yourself, the

biggest challenge you will face is deciding which material to use for exchanging the heat. If

you choose PE or U-PVC and the water is not going through the exchanger, the material will melt and the pipes will start leaking. Metal exchangers, for instance those made of copper, cannot be used since they poison the water. The only pipe material I believe is suitable, is stainless steel. Stainless steel is non-toxic, transfers heat very well and is resistant to high

temperatures. The principle is simple: wooden casing, an absorber, an exchanger and a

transparent plate of glass or Perspex are all that is needed.

## 8.4 SPAWNING PROCEDURES

## Natural spawning

Before explaining the artificial procedure for spawning catfish used at fish farms, it is good to know how African catfish spawn in their natural habitat. The African catfish has a spawning cycle and produces offspring only during a couple of months each year. The

period is initiated by the start of the rainy season when rivers, dams and lakes are flooded.

For Nigeria, it starts in March, at the time when the water temperature reaches its highest levels of the year. The female and male catfish will have their highest GSI (gonadosomatic index). This means that during this time, the weight of the tes and ovary occupies the largest percentage of their bodyweight, which is 1% for the males and 10% for the

females. High water temperature is also beneficial for the growth of fry and for the increase

## 124

Reproduction of the African catfish

of their natural food supply. During the rainy season, the flooded areas contain increased levels of organic material, which enhances the growth of zooplankton, the natural food for the freshly hatched catfish fry.

Catfish mating usually starts in the evening or in the early morning and takes place on the

shoreline of a lake, river or dam. Both sexes are close to each other, vigorously swimming and releasing the sperm and eggs in abundance. The sticky fertilised eggs stick to the bottom and to underwater plants. Catfish don't have parental care, so the hatched fry are on their own from day one.

In captivity catfish rarely spawn because the last step of egg maturation and ovulation do not happen, so the eggs are not released. Although, on rare occasions, spawning does happen. It is initiated when gravid brood stock is transferred from an environment with dirty water to one with cleaner water. It's annoying when this

happens, because if the dirty water to one with cleaner water. It's annoying when this

females do release their eggs, you cannot use them for a couple of months, and the eggs

released in the fish pond cannot be collected. The change of water quality actually imitates

a rainstorm; the reduced level of dissolved chemicals boosts the brooders.

Artificial reproduction of catfish is carried out by injecting a hormone into the female. It is a

standard procedure and it is temperature related. The hormone is a gonadotropin releasing

hormone and can be a pituitary gland or a synthetic product such as Ovapitine, Ovaline or Ovaprim. This hormone induces the final step of ripening of the eggs, called vitellogenesis. In this final step the eggs are provided with a yolk and absorb water.

The time between injecting this hormone and stripping the female, takes around 10 hours,

but can be less if the water temperature is higher than 26 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $, and more if the temperature

is less than 25 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C}.

The best time of stripping has been found by trial and error. As a farmer you will get to know the best time for stripping from your experience of previous spawnings. The release of the first eggs in the tank, where you have isolated the female brood stock, is a good sign.

If you try to strip the eggs out of the belly too early, it will be difficult. The eggs look

somewhat dry and you will have a pile of eggs in the egg collection tray instead of evenly

spread layers of eggs.

Step by step procedure for artificial reproduction

Preparing the system/tank: disinfection of the incubator

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_078.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

In order to get continuously good results with catfish hatching, it is important to clean and disinfect the system in which you put your fertilised eggs. This system is called 'the incubator'. Most farmers use the flowthrough system for incubating the eggs, but some

use small recirculation systems. The latter are more difficult to disinfect, in particular the

Chapter 8

filtration unit since more components are involved, and the disinfection procedure is

different.

## Flow-through system

Most farmers use white plastic tanks to incubate the eggs and get good results. However, after each spawning and transferring the fry, you immediately have to clean the tanks thoroughly with a brush and apply either calcium hypochlorite, which is also used in swimming pools, or hydrogen peroxide as a disinfectant. The

first disinfectant comes as a swimming pools, or hydrogen peroxide as a disinfectant. The

white powder while the latter is a liquid of 35% industrial hydrogen peroxide.

Apply this to all the surfaces of the tank in a 1% solution of calcium hypochlorite or a 3% solution of hydrogen peroxide. This can be carried out with a rag or by spraying it with a knapsack sprayer. Allow the disinfectant to remain on the surface for at least one hour. Follow the same procedure for the hatching nets or hatching trays, the filter and the PVC-

materials. Use the same rag or brush to dispose of the disinfectant with abundant clean

water. Fill the tank with water 12 hours before putting in the fertilised eggs.

Recirculation system

Hatcheries using recirculation technology also have to be disinfected completely after each

spawning. So, after the fry are transferred, all the components of the recirculation system,

such as the sedimentation tank and the biofilter unit have to be thoroughly cleaned with a brush and/or a high-pressure cleaner. The best thing to do is to take small components outside and clean them with a high-pressure cleaner while the tank and sedimentation tank are cleaned inside with a brush. After all the components of the system have been cleaned,

put them back and fill the tank completely with water and allow it to circulate. Add the

disinfectant, either calcium hypochlorite at 30 g/m $ _{3} $ or 1 l/m $ _{3} $ of a 35% hydrogen peroxide solution for 12 hours. Flush, rinse and fill the system again, and allow the water to circulate for another 12 hours before putting in the water for starting up another spawning.

Notes.

Calcium hypochlorite and hydrogen peroxide are both strongly oxidizing chemicals, which attack any organic matter including all living organism. The substances change the composition of proteins and enzymes in living cells which will result in dysfunction and death.

Always use personal protection if you weigh out and apply these chemicals, because

they are also harmful for human beings!

If your water is very soft (German hardness of less than 4), you are lucky because systems and tanks filled with soft water will not get dirty rapidly and are very easy to clean. As a matter of fact, spawning in soft water is more successful and the

growth of fungus on dead white eggs occurs less frequently.

Reproduction of the African catfish

Selection of females and males prior to injection

You have drained a brood stock tank to select female and male catfish for reproduction.

You can identify a gravid female that is ready for injection by her swollen red papilla. It

should be possible to strip out some eggs with little force and you will see that the eggs

have a migrated nucleus, which means that the core of the cell is situated at the periphery of the egg. The eggs have a diameter of approximately 1 mm. I prefer to select the female catfish in the early afternoon and inject them with the hormone in the evening. In the same way, the male catfish, which should be at least 300 days old, are selected. The

maturation of the male is difficult to discover from the outside. Only dissection will show

you if the tes are well developed with milky milt. Each female and male catfish should be put into separate tanks located in a quiet environment. The water temperature should be maintained at around 26 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $ both day and night. A very suitable isolation tank is the white rubber 1000 l tank, used to transport chemicals and sold afterwards in many in many places

brooders. in Nigeria. Allow the fish to have at least 3001 and again don't stress the brooders.

in Nigeria. Allow the fish to have at least 300 l and again don't stress the

Injection of the female

Just recently, I noticed that in some farms the female fish get infected after injection.

The location where the needle is inserted, swells up and results in a wound. The fish

can easily die from it, which is a big loss for a hatchery, especially if the female has

been giving you good spawning results. When I was doing the hatchery and the spawning operations myself, I never experienced this infection and I wondered why! So, I asked the hatchery manager, whether he was using new needles with each spawning. He told me: "Yes the needle is still sharp! " So, I asked him: "If a doctor

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_079.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

uses a needle, which he has just recently used with the comment 'the needle is still

sharp', you will buy that idea? " He said: "No way, I don't want to die of HIV or any other disease. " Please, use a new needle every time for each

spawning. The cost of a new needle is just 20, don't be penny wise and pound foolish!

At around 8.00 pm inject the hormone into the female catfish; the dosage is 0.5 ml for each

kg of fish. Use a 5-ml syringe and a needle with the specification 23Gxkg specification $ 2 3 \mathrm {G x} 1 _ {1 1 / 4} ^ Needle and syringe. are both readily available at a good pharmacy. The hormone can be bought from companies which sell fish feed, drugs etcetera.

Never insert the needle in the middle of the fish towards the central spine. It can start bleeding

heavily, because the central vein is located in this area. Insert the needle at an angle of 45

degrees away from the head in the thickest part of the muscle. The hormone is viscous and the syringe should be pressed gradually in order to empty it inside the muscles of the fish. After gently withdrawing the needle, you massage the spot where the needle entered for some seconds, before putting the fish back in the isolation tank. This procedure is easy to carry

out without using force on the female. She remains calm as long as you handle her gently.

## Chapter 8

Males are not injected, but kept in the isolation tank ready to use for the next morning. After injection, the females become a bit restless and can start to jump. Ensure that the fish do not jump out of their holding tanks to keep them safe. The female fish often change

colour and gain weight, because of the water absorption during the egg ripening process.

## Collection of the eggs

In the morning, the female fish will be ready for stripping. Take the female out, but if anaesthesia is available, you should first tranquilize her. MSS-222 (tricaine methanesulfonate)

is an anaesthetic for fish, including catfish. It is added to the tank at a ratio of 2 g/101.

After some minutes the female fish will stop breathing and turn on her side. Take the fish out, gently supporting the entire body, and wash off the water, containing the anaesthetic, with clean water. Place the fish on a smooth table and cover it with a clean wet towel; the

towel should not leak any water but also should not dry the skin of the fish, because this will

damage its slime. The stripping can now proceed. The female is stripped until the eggs are

not flowing out anymore. When blood is coming out with the eggs, it is a sign the ovaries are getting empty. Afterwards the female is put back into the tank she was isolated from, but not before its water has been refreshed. Then the eggs are weighed.

Collect the eggs on an egg collecting tray, preferably made from glass or ceramic plate.

## to the tray surface easily. If you don't

have anaesthesia, you have to apply a bit force to stop the female from moving her tail and wasting or dirtying the eggs on the collecting tray. Most of the time the female will remain relatively calm. The eggs should be stripped as cleanly as possible; without slime, water or faeces (Photo 29).

In the afternoon the female must be taken out from her tank again to strip the remainder of

the eggs which should be discharged. After stripping the ovary should be completely empty,

A smooth surface does not allow the eggs to stick

otherwise the eggs left behind, will start to rot which causes serious problems for the fish.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_080.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Reproduction of the African catfish

## Collection of milt (sperm)

There are two ways to collect the sperm from the male; either by sacrificing the male via dissecting the tes out of the belly, or by keeping the male alive, and collect the

sperm by taking a part of the tes out or sucking the sperm out of the tes with a

a syringe during surgery.

Sacrificing the male is the most usual method and it is relatively simple. The best and easiest way to kill the male is by hammering him on the head. It seems cruel, but if you do it with force, the fish will die almost instantly. Clean the belly with a towel and

make an incision from the anus upwards with a clean surgical blade. Open the cavity

and look for the tes which are located deep inside the cavity, close to the spinal

to the spinal cord. Use the surgical blade to cut the tes out of the tissue which is holding them in place in such a way that you keep the tes complete. There should be no leakage of sperm from the tes. Collect the tes in a small dry cup and cover it with tissue

paper. Then put it aside in a safe place where it cannot fall or come into contact with

water.

Note. Sperm of fish is inactive as long as it has not been in contact with water. The moment the sperm cells in the sperm come into contact with water, the energy locked

inside activates them to start surging for eggs. This will last for only about 60 seconds.

Afterwards the sperm is not fertile anymore! Also, eggs which have been in contact with water for a few minutes, are not fertilizable, because the micropyle, the opening where the sperm has to enter the egg, will have closed. Some fish species have a special attractant on the chorion, the outer membrane of the egg, which directs the

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_081.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

sperm cells into the micropyle of the egg. So, it is important to collect eggs and sperm

in a clean cup or bowl without any contact with water!

Note. Dilution of sperm in a physiological salt solution of 0.9% sodium chloride in water to enhance mixing of sperm and eggs before adding water to trigger the fertilisation, is

also possible. Be sure the solution is fresh and has a temperature of 28 $ ^{\circ} $ C.

## More about milt

Sperm or milt can be preserved in a fridge at 4 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $ for one day, but it's advisable to use the milt directly after it has been taken out of the male. Sperm can even be frozen and remain

viable for many years. This process is called cryopreservation. This technique consists of remain

using special chemical solutions which are added to the sperm, and liquid nitrogen to keep consists of and liquid nitrogen to keep the milt as cold as $ - 1 7 3 $ $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $

in a special container. For Nigeria the milt as cold as -173 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} this technique is not feasible at farm level, but in aquatic research institutes it could be interesting to use this method for improving the genetics of the catfish.

## Chapter 8

Sperm quality can be tested under a microscope; put a small drop of sperm on a glass slide and look at it with the 100-x magnification. If there are plenty of sperm cells in the milt, you will see millions of little grey balls which you can activate with a little drop of water.

The sperm cells should swim actively for some seconds. This is the sign that the sperm is

fertile and is able to fertilise the eggs.

Fertilisation process

The eggs are divided between different bowls with no more than 200 g in each bowl.

Fertilise 200 g of eggs at a time with at least 7 to 8 drops good quality white milky sperm.

More sperm will not increase the fertilisation rate, but it will not cause any harm. Make small incisions in the tes and by a little squeezing, the sperm will come out and must be directly put onto the eggs. Without water nothing will happen, but immediately after the sperm is put onto the dry eggs, you have to activate the sperm by putting water in the

bowl. For 200 g of eggs half a litre of water is enough. Stir the solution gently for about

three minutes, so that the sperm can be optimally mixed with the eggs and fertilise them. The water you use to activate the sperm, should come from the tank which you use to put the fertilised eggs in.

Afterwards, spread the eggs over a mosquito net. Most eggs will stick to the net, but

some will go through it and stick to the bottom of the tank. 200 g of fertilised eggs need

a surface of 0.25 $ m_{2} $ to be spread onto. It should be a single layer of eggs on the net, so that the bad unfertilised eggs on which fungus will start growing, do not infect the good fertilised ones.

## Incubation time till hatching

The incubation time till hatching is about 24 hours, but it can vary a lot, depending on the water temperature. The best temperature for incubation and hatching is 30 $ ^{\circ} $ C. The acceptable range lies between 27 and 31 $ ^{\circ} $ C. Below 25 $ ^{\circ} $ C the hatching will take too long and will give poor results. A low temperature makes the fry weak and less active. They will

stay where they have been hatched and will not swim to the corners of the tank. They will

just drop onto the bottom and get infected with fungus or bacteria.

After the fertilisation procedure, it takes about 10 to 12 hours before you can check if the eggs are actually fertilised. The nucleus grows into a roundshaped line at the periphery of

the yolk sac, forming the tail of the embryo. At that moment you can distinguish the eggs

which have not and which have been fertilised. The unfertilized eggs become white while the fertilised ones are still greenish, shining and the development of the embryo is visible.

Usually, the hatching rate differs from the fertilisation rate. If the eggs are strong, the

hatching and fertilisation rate will be close, but normally the hatching rate will be not more

Reproduction of the African catfish

than 50% of the fertilization rate. When most of the eggs have hatched and dropped out of the mosquito nets, you must remove the nets from the water. If you wait too long, the water will get whitish and fungus will develop, which has a negative impact

on the yolk sac of the fry.

Clean and rinse the nets straight away!

Note. Don't mix the eggs of different females in one bowl or in one incubation tank

and use one testis for each bowl of eggs. The offspring from the hatching should be

full siblings, so that the genetic variation in the fry is as low as possible and the growth

will be as uniform as possible.

One day I visited a farm in Mali. They have a well-equipped catfish hatchery and

## clarias: selecting the brood stock, preparing

and we prepared for a spawning of Hetero-clarias: selecting the brood stock, we prepared for a spawning of Hetero-

preparing the incubator by cleaning, disinfecting and rinsing, checking all the materials needed for the actual spawning, such as anaesthesia, bowls, hatching trays, surgical blade and hormones. Another check was carried out on the availability trays, syringe, of starter feed, salt and Artemia, also called 'brine shrimps', which are a good

a good starter feed for fry. Well, in the evening we wanted to inject two females; one

one Heterobranchus and one Clarias female. We checked in the fridge before and knew that we had at least three bottles of Ovaprim still in their packaging, so we thought there was no problem. How surprised we were, when we found out later that all the bottles of Ovaprim were used and almost empty! So, we had to empty! So, we had to

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_082.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

postpone the hatching procedure. The next day we started looking for the bottles with the

hormone! with the hormone!

I notice in many farms that empty packages are never disposed of but put back into the fridge, cupboard or any place where you usually can fnd them. This provides a false sense of security and it's annoying too. I asked the farm manager why asked the farm manager

those empty packages of hormones, artemia, starter feed, antibiotic etcetera are why all

never disposed in the dustbin? The answer was clear: if the boss asks about these etcetera materials, the staff can show that they have used them by showing him the empty packages. I suggested having a separate cupboard for this, so that you can at least keep a clean record of your real stocks!

Chapter 8

## What may cause unsuccessful hatching?

In most cases unsuccessful hatching has multiple causes from a variety of angles and therefore not easy to spot and to correct, but I try to list the issues which usually go wrong:

Brood stocks are of inferior quality because they have not been given good feed and/or have been underfed and/or are less than 12 months old.

The female does not release her eggs. There are multiple reasons for this: the incubation temperature of the water of the holding tank is too low (less than 24

°C), wrong dosage or expired hormones, badly handled and stressed brood stock

or the female is just not yet mature.

The collection of stripped eggs contains a lot of white eggs; this is a sign of regression of the eggs or off-season spawning. In nature catfish only spawn during the rainy season, so the dry season is not the period catfish have their best eggs!

The eggs look good but turn white within eight hours. Most likely the disinfection

of the tank has been carried out but it has not been rinsed well afterwards; traces

of chlorine can kill the eggs within a short period of time.

The eggs delay hatching if the temperature of the water is 25 $ ^{\circ} $ C or below. The

incubation time between fertilisation and hatching can become up to 30 hours

or more. The yolk sac-fry will be sluggish and are not likely to swim to the corner

of the tank. They stay at the spot on the bottom of the tank where they dropped down. Then, the fry can get easily infected with bacteria or fungus. This will reduce the initial survival rates and it will also cause reduction of the number of fry during the first two weeks of growing.

The water quality also plays an important part in successful hatching; preferably

the pH is around 7, the German hardness not higher than 7 and the iron content is less than 0.2 mg/l. Spawning of catfish eggs proceeds best in soft water. Another problem with hard water is the much more rapid and severe growth of fungus which infects a lot of hatchlings

The storage tank is very dirty and causes a lot of bacterial influx into the system.

The storage tank of a hatchery should be cleaned at least every three months. When you have hard water, containing a high level of calcium and magnesium, the storage tank gets dirty very quickly. The limescale (calcium) deposits on the walls of the tank and pipes are a breeding ground for bacteria and will have a very

negative effect on results for freshly hatched eggs and fry.

Oxygen levels are too low because water is not flowing through the tank constantly. If you use the flow-through system, it's advisable to have an aerator in the tank to support the oxygen level in the incubator and during the growth stage of the fry.

## Yolk sac absorption till first feeding

Reproduction of the African catfish

The yolk sac-fry are not yet developed into a fish. The mouth has not been formed and the digestive system has not been completely developed. Over the course of two days

at a temperature of 28 to 30 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $, they absorb their yolk sac and change into swimming

fry able to eat. In this period the fry avoid light and move away from it, which is called 'negative phototaxis'. In the tank you will see them clustering in dark corners. It is important that the tank for the fry has no drain where they can hide in. The fry will certainly die here, since the oxygen level will be too low for them. In this period, the

fry also start to show pigmentation; they turn from greenish to brownish. When the

fry swim and cluster into corners, it's a good opportunity to clean the bottom of dead eggs, fungal and bacterial growth etcetera. This can be done by sucking this waste out with a small 4-5 mm hose. After two days the fry are ready to start eating; they come out of the corners and swim up the water column, searching for food. They will

be swimming everywhere, not in schools just erratically; that's why they are called

'swim-up-fry'.

8.5 FEEDING FRY

First feeding

In the olden days "What to feed the swim up-fry? " was one of the most crucial questions. Feed from the factory was rarely available and starter feed was not even developed at that time. So, farmers breeding catfish used natural plankton, egg yolks

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_083.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Artemia salina cysts became available and they appeared to be a very good starter feed for catfish. Till today you can use Artemia salina to start feeding the fry at their initial stage, but this is not common in Nigeria because of the low availability and high price (Photos 30 and 31). In Appendix 8 you will find the recipe for making starter feed

from Artemia cysts. An alternative is encapsulated Artemia cysts, which are available in

shops specializing in fish feed products.

At present several feed factories produce or import good starter feed. They are expensive (N 9000/kg in 2018), but when you calculate it, it is preferable to use good

starter feed instead of inferior products, as long as you get improved survival rates and

good healthy growth. Appendix 6 shows a list of starter feeds with specifications.

Live Artemia have a big advantage over dry starter feed because they are very much appreciated by the catfish fry and they stay alive in the water for at least 30 minutes.

Live Artemia don't pollute the water like dry feed does. Overfeeding of Artemia is not

## Chapter 8

a big problem, whereas overfeeding dry feed causes excessive bacterial growth, which means trouble for the catfish fry. The feeding frequency of catfish fry should therefore be every three to four hours and in small quantities at the time.

You can see their stomachs getting bigger after feeding and if you give them orange

feed, their bellies will turn orange too. When the fry are satiated, they become less active in the water column and rest at the bottom of the tank. After some hours, they are normally already in search of feed again and swim up. So, if they do not come up after some hours, there is a problem. The water temperature plays an important part

in the response and growth of the fry. Preferably the water temperature should be 30

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_084.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 30. Hatching Artemia, to make starter feed for catfish swim up-fry.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_085.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 31. Harvesting Artemia, starter feed for catfish swim up-fry.

The economics of the use of so-called 'expensive' starter feedsThe economics of the use of so-called 'expensive' starter feeds

Many farmers don't want to spend money on the best starter feed; they believe they can never make a profit if starter feed is expensive, and therefore use alternatives. But it is

important to achieve good growth and good survival. In that case, an expensive feed will

pay for itself and it will actually become a cheap feed!

Example 12. What is the feed cost to produce a fingerling of 0.6 g? Suppose the starter feed for the first week is N 14, 000 per kg (particle size 0.1 mm)and the second week you use a starter feed of N 11, 000/kg (particle size 0.2 mm).

After these two sizes you can use an ordinary starter feed for catfish as long as the

size is between 0.2-0.3 mm. This feed costs about N 1000/kg.

FCR = 0.6 which means 0.6 kg of feed is needed to produce 1 kg of fingerling.

0.1 mm is used for fry? ro? 2 mg to 25 mg in week 1 (growth 23 mg).

0.2 mm is used for fry? ro? 25 mg to 80 mg in week 2 (growth 55 mg).

0.2-0.3 mm and 0.5 mm is used for fry? ro? 80 mg to 600 mg in week in week

3, 4 and 5 (growth 520 mg).

Feed needed for 1 fish of 0.6 g:

0.1 mm: 23 mg x 0.6 = 14 mg of feed

0.2 mm: 55 mg x 0.6=33 mg of feed

0.2-0.3 mm: 520 mg x 0.6=312 mg of feed

0.1 mm: 0.014 x N 14, 0/g = N 0.2/piece

Cost of feed per size for 1 fingerling:

0.2 mm: 0.033 x N 11, 0/g = N 0.36/piece

0.2-0.3mm: 0.312x N 1, 0/g= N 0.312/piece Total cost for 1 fish of 0.6 g = N 1.0/piece

Not all fry will make it to fingerling and therefore you should multiply N 1.0 with 2.

The cost to produce 1 fingerling will still be 42, 0 or less a piece!

8.6 GRADING ACCORDING TO SIZE

Catfish are carnivorous and cannibalism is normal if the situation is favorable for it. To

avoid cannibalism in the early growth stages, you need to grade the fish according to size. If the fish are of the same size, cannibalism will be reduced. Cannibalism can already start

from the first day the fry are eating. It will be especially enhanced in less optimal situations,

such as having weak fry or dead fry in the tank. The fry will not all develop at the same speed. Some fry will still be eating their yolk sac while others are already looking for food. If the first feed is too early, you already create a difference in size from the start! Normally when the fry are healthy and feeding is optimal, not too less, not too much, cannibalism

will not be a big problem, since they all grow at the same pace. That's why I always

## 136

Reproduction of the African catfish

recommend growing batches of full siblings and not a mixture of many different genetics,

which enhances different growth rates.

During the first two months till the juvenile stage the fish have to be graded at least two

to three times. Grading can be carried out in different ways. You can decide to take out the shooters only and leave the rest of the batch to grow on. Or, you take out the shooters and grade the remaining fish into two different sizes. Shooters are at least three times bigger than the average size. They really eat other fish and sometimes you can see those shooters

vomiting complete catfish when you start grading. They take a bite from the head and

swallow their prey whole. A shooter of 12 g can eat a fish of 4 g! If you see many head injuries in a group of fish, it's an indication that there are many shooters inside. Shooters usually don't eat dry feed, but start hunting any time they are hungry. They even fight each other and can die as a result.

I don't consider shooters good brood stock, although they grow much more quickly than

the others. But this is not a result of genetics but of the excellent food they get. If shooters are not taken out in time, cannibalism will reduce your fish population up to 50% in two weeks' time!

Grading can be carried out in different ways. Apart from a grading table you can also use

an adjustable grader or net grader (Photos 32 and 33).

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_086.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 32. A table grader for post-juveniles.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_087.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 33. An adjustable grader and a net grader for fry, fingerlings and juveniles.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_088.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

8.7 SELLING FINGERLINGS AND JUVENILES

Health status of the fish

The fingerlings and juveniles you sell your customers should be in a perfect condition and

well fed. Some hatcheries stop feeding their fish well, as soon as they receive a booking and get paid a deposit or full payment. After all, the fish

have already been sold. The customer has just to collect them and the fish are already at their selling size. If this period takes time, the fingerlings or juveniles become weak and lean; actually, what you have been taking care of for

two months, you spoil in a matter of days, just because you don't want to buy another bag of

starter feed. Discuss with your customer that the price of the fish depends on their size. If the fish are not collected by the customer in time, which happens a lot, and the fish become bigger, the price will be adjusted. If the fish have been sick, be sure that the sickness is completely over before you sell, because otherwise the transport and stress of a new environment can

trigger the sickness to return. Your customer doesn't know how to handle this problem and will

certainly encounter severe losses; another customer who will not buy from you again!

## Grading

If you have a hatchery and you sell your product to customers, then it's an obligation to grade

Reproduction of the African catfish

the fish very well. Most grow-out farmers don't have the means to grade and stock fingerlings

and juveniles in a big pond with the projection to keep them in this pond till harvest!

In any group of fish, you will have runts: fish which don't grow at all. When the fish have for example an average weight of 10 g, the runts are only 2 g. In Nigeria farmers

reluctant to throw these little fish away and still keep them or worse, stock them with

other fish from a different batch. Fish which don't grow, are a liability. You have to get rid of them as quickly as possible. Don't waste feed on them and don't sell them to spoil your

name!

## Counting or weighing method

Counting the fish one by one is an accurate way to collect the number of fish a customer wants to buy, but when it takes too long or if the number of fish is over 10, 000 pieces, it is not the right method. Most farmers believe

counting the fish is the best and most accurate way, but by counting the fish many things can still go wrong. Usually they use the grading

table for counting. The table is smooth and the fish are put on top of it. They count till

one hundred and put a stone aside; later on, they count the stones to estimate the overall

number of counted fish.

I personally prefer the average weight method. Because the shooters should have been

taken out, you take the average weight of the fish after grading from each tank. At least

300 pieces are counted and weighed on a scale with an accuracy of 1 g. The average weight will be the total weight divided by the number of fish. If you know the average weight, then you divide the total weight of the fish by the average weight to obtain the number of fish you want to sell. This method doesn't stress the fish as much as counting

fish counters can be used to but are very expensive.

Example 13Example 13.. How to collect 5000 pieces by the average weight method?

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_089.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

You weighed 315 fish and you got a total of 500 g.

The average weight is 500/315=1.59 g.

Now, you want to sell 5000 pieces, so the total weight you want to sell is: 5000 x

1.59 g = 7, 950 g or 8 kg. So, you weigh 8 kg of fish for your customer. Usually you

give the customer 2 to 3% extra to be sure he gets the number he wants.

In this case you weigh out for the customer an extra of 0.16 to 0.24 kg.

The problem with the average weight method is the water attached to the fish. The

smaller the fish to be sold, the bigger this problem will get, because the amount of water attached to the fish, provides false information about the average weight and the total number of fish. But, the smaller the fish, the more damage you will face when using the one by one counting method.

## Chapter 8

Packaging and transport

Some years ago, I was invited to evaluate a fish farm in Ogun State close to Ijebu Ode.

As I was already staying in Abeokuta, it was a convenient journey, because the general

manager of the fish farm picked me up from there. On our way to the farm, he explained

about his plans. He wanted to upgrade his hatchery, because he faced some challenges buying the fingerlings and just recently had lost a lot of fish due to transportation. I asked him what happened and he told me the story. The fish he always buys originate from a farmer friend and their quality is good. Since the trip between the farms is short, they

quickly weigh the fish and put them in those 50- 1 plastic bags with oxygen in very high

minutes. But not this time around. A serious road accident had happened and the car with fish was trapped in a go-slow for three hours before it could move again. By that time, the fish were already dying. He lost 90% of them. The financial loss of approximately 200, 000

was now gradually deducted from his salary!

Usually, customers come to pick up the fish. They are responsible for the containers to put the fish in. When the fish are small, less than 0.5 g, they can also be transported in plastic bags with extra oxygen. These bags are the responsibility of the supplier, which is the hatchery.

densities. It has always gone well previously because the trip takes just 30

First of all, the fish should not be given any feed at least 12 hours before transport. After

counting or weighing, the fish are put in a bag or container. But how many fish you This question is not easy to answer because it depends on the weight of the fish, the distance, the transport time, the weather conditions and the condition of the roads. See Photos 34 and 35 about transport and packaging materials for fish transportation.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_090.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 34. A 50-l transport KEG for juveniles.

140

Reproduction of the African catfish

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_091.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 35. A transport 500-l insulated tank for juveniles or brood stock.

The transport time is actually more important than the distance. If the trip takes usually two hours, you have to prepare for safe transport for the fish for at least five hours!

If it is a hot day and you put the tanks or bags in a car without AC, you will risk the water temperature rising to more than 30 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $. As a result, the oxygen level of the water

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_092.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

will go down and the fishes' rate of metabolism will increase. You create a big risk of

getting very weak fish and mortality, either on arrival or when you put the fish in their new environment. If it is going to be a long trip, the best time to travel is in the evening and at night, if security allows you to do so. If the road is bumpy, the fish will get stressed and you will lose water on the way bit by bit.

Farmers usually stock between 500 to 1000 pieces of juveniles in the black containers showed on Photo 34. In the white plastic bags around 500 pieces of fingerlings are usually showed on Photo 34. The bags are filled 1/3 with water and 2/3 with pure oxygen. So, not with air! stocked. The supplier should always warn the farmer, who buys the fish that the transport of the fish

is the farmer's responsibility and dead fish on arrival cannot be compensated. If the supplier fish is supplier

transports the fish, it is his responsibility.

The farmer who buys the fish, should have his pond well prepared, so that when he arrives, the stocking of the juveniles or fingerlings will be fast and go smoothly. Don't start and go smoothly.

counting the fish again, they are already stressed enough!

Chapter 8

## After sales service

If you want farmers to be loyal to your farm, you must not only sell good quality fish but also offer after sales service. Inquire about the progress and growth of the fish and support

the farmers with tips. Grow-out farms don't have the expertise hatcheries do, so you can

certainly give them good tips and advice. The farmer's success will also be your success and if the farmer makes money with the sales of the table-sized fish, he will certainly come back to you for more fingerlings. Don't try to sell farmers quantities of fish they cannot accommodate, because it just suits you to get rid of your juveniles. You will force your

customer to sell his immature fish for a low price, because in this case the money for feed

usually runs out before the end of the growth cycle.

## 8.8 HATCHERY SYSTEMS

I believe the combination of flow-through and recirculation systems is the best way forward for continuous supply of fingerlings and juveniles. The initial growth stages of at least the first three weeks, should be kept inside a building with constant water supply. Afterwards, the fry and fingerlings

I believe a green water environment is good for growing catfish in their first growth stages

can be stocked outside in plastic tanks with periodic

## 8.9 GREEN WATER

flushing, creating a green water environment.

because of the following reasons:

The algae in the water consume the waste of the fish and reduce the flushing rate without you having to deal with bad smelling water.

The catfish feel secure because birds or other predators cannot spot them easily.

It creates a favorable environment in which good bacteria have an advantage over the pathogenic ones.

It creates a flora of organisms (natural food) which are beneficial to the growth of catfish fry.

Green algae produce oxygen during the day but during the night they consume

it and the oxygen level reduces. So, catfish need to have developed the labyrinth organ in order to breath oxygen from the air! I believe pathogenic organisms relying on oxygen, such as Aeromonas species, causing fin rot and elimination of the barbels, and Flexibacter columnaris, also called saddleback disease, are at a

disadvantage in green water because they cannot flourish during the night.

The catfish are usually healthy and don't suffer from bacterial diseases as much as in a clear water environment.

Sick fish can even get over their illness without any treatment.

In order to keep a green water environment, you should never flush all the water at once, but in parts on a daily basis in such a way that the water is not getting too green, but also not getting to clear. The transparency of the water should be about 3 to 4 cm.

## 8.10 HYBRIDIZATION8.10 HYBRIDIZATION OF CATFISH

In biology, a hybrid is the result of combining the qualities of two organisms of different breeds, varieties, species or genera through sexual reproduction. Since Clarias

gariepinus belongs to the genus Clarias and Heterobranchus longifilis (Photos 36 and gariepinus (Photo 36)

(Photo 37) belongs to the genus Heterobranchus, this type of hybridization is called an intergeneric hybridization. In

nature hybridization between two species doesn't occur, intergeneric hybridization. In because they are reproductively isolated by morphological differences and different mating behavior. But when we proceed with an artificial reproduction of these species

in the same way that we produce pure Clarias gariepinus, it results in viable hybrids

called 'Hetero-clarias'.

The Hetero-clarias hybrid shows characteristics of both parental species both in behavior and morphological appearance. Heterobranchus longifilis is the biggest

the back and very long whiskers. The meat has 30% more fat than Clarias has and is whiter in colour while Clarias meat is pinkish. You find both characteristics in Heteroclarias.

The Hetero-clarias is not quite fertile and will not spend much energy on gonads. This

affects the somatic growth and the FCR positively. However, its growth rate shows a lot of variation, so grading during the early stages of the growth cycle is very important to suppress cannibalism. The fish are hardy and do well in natural environments such as earthen ponds. Heterobranchus longifilis doesn't mature quickly compared to Clarias

gariepinus. It takes close to three years in captivity. The most common cross breed

consists of a Heterobranchus male with a Clarias female.

In the Netherlands one company specializes in producing the Heteroclarias hybrid because of the white meat. They even branded the fish with the name 'Claresse'.

## 8.11 DISCUSSION

Hatchery operations are not easy to manage and many farmers who start up hatcheries,

face problems with the continuity of getting good results. So, at the end of the day, end of the day growout

farmers buying fish from these hatcheries, cannot rely on them, causing disruption in on them, causing disruption in the production and profits completely. Therefore, many grow-out farmers start their own hatchery operations out of frustration.

Why is a hatchery so difficult to manage? Because running a successful hatchery depends

on so many factors. When things go wrong, most of the time it is a multiple problem instead of a standalone one. What I have noticed in most cases is that the problem came down to lack of commitment of the hatchery manager and insufficient knowledge. They get results now and then, so in principle the facility works. But, if they get a good spawning and a

good survival rate, they cannot repeat the results because they don't know why things

## 144

Reproduction of the African catfish

has triggered me to stay involved in hatchery operations because it's a very challenging

are going wrong or going well. Lacking good operational procedures causes problems for

repeating good results.

Hatcheries in Nigeria are not located in a controlled environment like in Europe, that's why

you should adapt the procedures with the seasons. Running a hatchery is not only hard work, but also a way of life and an art form. You need to be naturally talented and have an eye for problems before they occur. As a young man I started hatchery operations in 1984 and till today I have not completely mastered the art of running a hatchery. That 'till today'

profession and never boring. Also, this work makes me a humble person and one who respects the law of God. I always say to my fellow farmers: "We don't make anything in a hatchery, we only support the law of nature created by God.

Chapter 9

## 9.1 INTRODUCTION

When I was studying at the University of Wageningen, I did an experiment with African

catfish. I had to produce the fish for the experiment myself. This was my frst step in

becoming a fish farmer. The spawning was successful. I obtained about 40, 000 fry to grow to the juvenile stage. At this stage the fish were stocked for the experiment. I needed only 2000 pieces. At the fngerling stage, I stocked the fish in two fow-through systems with crystal clear water and high oxygen levels. I believed this was the best water

to grow my catfish, not knowing that this water actually stressed them and allowed

virulent bacteria, such as Flexibacter columnaris, to develop very rapidly. The bacteria killed over 90% of my fish before my supervisor was aware of it. He quickly applied antibiotics which resulted in just enough fish to stock for my experiment. Actually, I learned more from growing these fish than from my experiment. My way of looking at

fish has never been the same since! A song which relates to this experience is from The

Beatles: 'Yesterday, all my troubles seem so far away!

Fish diseases are the nightmare for every fish farmer. They can arise any time, even when you don't expect it. In most cases the losses are not severe when proper attention is paid, in other

words diseases are manageable. But when not taken care of, a batch of fish or even worse

a farm can be totally destroyed by diseases. They can even lead to bankruptcy of a fish farm. The life of fish is very dynamic, so many factors play a part in the outbreak of diseases. There are three major factors (Figure 23):

Environment

Catfish as? host

Pathogens

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_096.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

As you can see in Figure 23, one factor can compensate another factor. For example, As you can see in the drawing if the environment is not optimal for the fish, but there is no pathogen present, it will not be likely that the fish will get a disease. Or, the pathogens are present,

present, but the condition of the fish is very good; the fish will resist the pathogen and will not get

sick. The moment you abuse all three factors to a certain extent, the fish will certainly and will not get sick. You also will understand from Figure 23 that you treat the fish with medicine and they recover, it is actually a short-term remedy and not a sustainable solution. If you don't improve the three factors mentioned above, recurrence of the

disease will be inevitable recurrence of the disease will be inevitable.

Fish live in water and at a fish farm they cannot escape from the water you provide for

them, so it's your responsibility to give them water of a good quality. I believe that poor water quality is the number one reason fish develop diseases. I have seen cases where fish wanted to jump out of the water because of the poor water quality. Fish swimming towards or away from the inlet, are also signs that the water quality is bad.

Chemicals and factors causing a bad environment for the fish

The most common pollutants which cause a stressful environment for the fish are thewaste products of the fish themselves and chemicals released by human activity.

Ammonia-nitrogen

Ammonia-nitrogen is a waste product produced by the fish and excreted through the gills. It is equivalent to the urine of mammals but more toxic; the levels of ammonia-nitrogen in the water should therefore be low.

Ammonia-nitrogen is actually a combination of ammonium and ammonia (NH $ ^{+4} $ and

NH $ _{3-3} $: total ammonia-nitrogen or TAN), but only the ammonia is very toxic to the fish.

The concentration of ammonia and ammonium in the water is present in a ratio, whichdepends on the pH of the water (Figure 24). When the pH is high, the percentage of ammonia is high and it starts to increase rapidly above a pH of 8. When the pH is low, the percentage of ammonium will be high, which is not a problem for the fish. But

when the pH skyrockets, you have an emergency situation.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_097.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_098.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 24. The link between ammonia and ammonium and the pH of the water. (source: Cornell Composting) water.

Levels of ammonia start to be toxic in the range of 0.1 mg/l for small catfish to 0.4 mg/l for bigger ones.

The signs of ammonia intoxication are:

150

Loss of appetite; usually the first unspecific sign when a problem with the fish

occurs

Lethargy and changing colour

Inflammation of gills Red barbels, red fins and inflamed eyes

If the incoming water is lower in ammonia concentration than the water in the tank, you will see the fish swimming towards the fresh water flow. The remedy is relatively simple: drain as much bad water out of the tank as quickly as possible and replace it with clean water without ammonia-nitrogen.

Test kits are available in the market to test the water for the ammonia-nitrogen concentration

and the pH. You cannot see or smell the ammonia-nitrogen easily, so using your senses is not a reliable option!

For small fry and fingerlings an ammonia-nitrogen concentration below 5 mg/l, and for juveniles below 10 mg/l are recommended. For grow-out fish, the ammonia-nitrogen

concentration should be below 25 mg/l at a pH of below 7.5

Catfish diseases

## Suspended solids

Suspended solids are particles in the water which make the water cloudy. This turbidity can not only originate from waste materials, such as sand, laterite and clay, but also from the

faeces produced by the fish or from an algal bloom. Catfish are not very sensitive to turbid

water and thrive well in it. During the rainy season especially, the water can be very turbid because of soil erosion, but the fish will not face many problems. However, in the rainy season I have noticed greater mortality when using river water than during the dry season. I believe it isn't the solids suspended in the water that cause this problem, but the runoff

from farms, containing pesticides and herbicides. Of course, in the hatchery you want to

have clear water and when you use borehole water this will be usually the case. In general, high levels of suspended solids in the water will cause the oxygen level of the water to be low, because of a high biological oxygen demand (BOD). If the catfish have developed their extra breathing organ, they just compensate for this by taking oxygen from the air.

## High levels of carbon dioxide

Carbon dioxide $ \left( \mathrm{C O}_{2} \right) $ is not usually a big problem in African catfish farming, especially for all the growth stages of catfish bigger than fingerling size. In high density fish farming, the free carbon dioxide level increases in the water due to the metabolism of the fish. Normally,

fish remove oxygen from the water and release carbon dioxide. African catfish however,

release the carbon dioxide above the surface of the water so the carbon dioxide level of

the water is not easily elevated. I want to draw your attention to this just for hatcheries,

to this, just for hatcheries, because they use borehole water which usually contains high levels of carbon dioxide (50 mg/l or more). This can easily be tested with a simple pH-test kit. Test the borehole water

directly at the source without any contact with air. In most cases the pH will be slightly

acidic, which means below 7. Take some of this water and fill a 1-l bottle with 100 ml

(10%). Agitate the water by shaking the bottle for at least two minutes and measure the pH of the water again. Normally you will see an increase in pH to above 7. What happened is that the carbon dioxide, which is an acid, was released into the air and due to this

process, the pH of the water rose (Figure 25).

Equation: $ \mathrm{C O_{2}+H_{2}O} $

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_099.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

$ \mathrm{H C O}_{-}+\mathrm{H}_{+} \left(\mathrm{H}_{+}\right. $ is acid $ )_{3} $

Carbon dioxide has a negative impact on the metabolism of young fish. They will behave

sluggishly and refuse to eat. You can compare this to a church full of people with no

ventilation; you start to feel sleepy. The concentration of free carbon

dioxide should not be

higher than 20 mg/l.

So, anyone who sets up a hatchery, has to degas the water from the borehole before it

enters the fish tank. This can easily be done by a trickling tower above the water storage

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_100.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Chapter 9

tank, which does not require extra energy, or by flowing the water into the tank through

a showerhead.

Dissolved oxygen

In 1984 I started my farm in the Netherlands. Not only did I grow catfish but I also

tried a lot of other fish species. I was trading ornamental fish for outdoor ponds,

including sturgeon (Acipenser gueldenstaedtii). I used to buy them from a farm in Eastern Europe and at the end of the summer, when the selling season was over, I just let the leftover sturgeon grow bigger for the next season at my indoor farm; by which time they would fetch a very good price! On Christmas day after feeding and

checking the fish farm, I went to church and visited my family in the village. Coming

back home in the afternoon, I experienced a disaster; the pump of the tanks where the sturgeon were stocked, had stopped and the water was not fowing through the tanks anymore. Most of my sturgeon had died because of oxygen depletion. I forgot to equip the system with backup aeration and the alarm system didn't work.

mortality of fish. It is a very common cause of death at fish farms which farm non-air breathing fish, and also in rivers where factories dump chemicals into the water which consume all the oxygen.

African catfish however, are hardy fish when it comes to oxygen concentrations in the

Catfish diseases

water; they survive and even do well when the oxygen level is below 1 mg/l. Their organ to breath air is not immediately developed when they are born though. It takes about three to four weeks for the catfish to get to this growth stage. So, before this stage, oxygen levels

have to be at least 4 mg/l. Therefore, hatcheries need running water in the tanks and/or

aeration 24/7, and the tanks should not be overcrowded.

Oxygen levels in the water vary with the water temperature

Figure 26 shows that maximum oxygen levels reduce significantly when water temperature

temperature rises. In addition, the metabolism of fish increases with increasing temperatures. As already

Low oxygen levels, also called environmental hypoxia, can cause mass

As already stated, in a farm situation when a catfish has developed its air breathing organ, a low oxygen level is not a serious problem. However, it is good to realise that transporting fish in a car without air-conditioning, might lead to problems with maintaining an optimum water temperature, inducing mortality. So, for fish transportation ideally the water should

not be more than 25 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $

## Herbicides and insecticides

Herbicides and insecticides are usually highly toxic for aquatic animals, including fish. Therefore, don't use insecticides at your fish farm to kill insects such as mosquitoes, flies

or cockroaches. If they drop dead and fall into the water of your ponds or tanks, they can

even be eaten by the fish! When spraying with herbicides on your premises to kill the grass, make sure that there is little

wind so that none of the chemicals blow into the water make sure that there is little

Another source of chemicals entering the water arises during the rainy season, when

farmers use a lot of chemicals at their farm. Runoff flowing into the river might be contaminated with herbicides and insecticides. The dilution factor is high, but I believe even low concentrations of these chemicals can cause problems for your fish, if you use the river water directly. I believe the immune system of the fish is challenged and they will not

be able to resist diseases as strongly as they can normally. The best way to use river water

is to allow it to settle in a big reservoir with a retention time of at least two days.

During the dry season another threat occurs when fishermen use gammalin 20 (Lindane) to kill and catch the fish in the river. The flow of the river is slow and just a few litres of

gammalin can kill a lot of fish. When you use this water to flush your ponds, you will

certainly get problems with your fish. My advice is to always check the river and the water intake for floating dead fish; if so, delay pumping the water till you don't see dead fish anymore. The chemical will pass by if the river is still flowing. anymore.

Figure 26. The relationship between the water temperature and the oxygen level at saturation (source: Fondriest Environmental Products).

Catfish diseases

Chlorine

Chlorine is a highly toxic chemical which is used for disinfecting materials and systems at the farm. It kills all the germs. But it is also used to disinfect the drinking water by

chlorination. Fry are more susceptible to chlorine than adult fish. Lethal concentrations

vary from 0.01 mg/l for fry to 0.25 mg/l for bigger catfish. Test kits for chlorine are rarely

available in Nigeria, but they do exist.

What does chlorine do to the fish?

Chlorine is an oxidizer and kills every living tissue by causing necrosis. In catfish lethal levels

of chlorine will cause the slime on the skin of the fish to disappear within 24 hours. The fish will certainly die. Also, chlorine attacks the respiratory system. So, the gills and the labyrinth organ will be affected too, causing breathing difficulties.

Fortunately, removing chlorine is not that difficult. Chlorine is relatively unstable in water

and will vaporise from the water by itself within 24 hours, especially if you aerate it. A quick neutralisation of chlorine can be carried out with sodium thiosulfate at doses of 2 to 7 parts of sodium thiosulfate for 1 part of chlorine. If you have 2 m $ ^{3} $ water with a concentration of 0.5 mg/l chlorine, you need to neutralize the chlorine with 2 to 7 g of

sodium thiosulfate.

pH and alkalinity of water

The pH of pure water is 7. In general, water with a pH lower than 7 is considered acidic,

and water with a pH higher than 7 is considered basic. The normal range

## of the pH in

surface water and ground water is between 6 and 8.5. This is also considered to be a

good pH for fish to thrive in. The complete pH-scale ranges from 0 to 14. A pH lower than 6 and higher than 8.5 is dangerous for the well-being of fish. In both cases the slime on the skin and the gills themselves are affected. The slime on the skin actually dissolves. In addition, when the pH is high the ammonia-ammonium ratio is shifted towards the very

toxic ammonia.

Alkalinity refers to the property of water to neutralize acid; it's an expression of the buffering capacity. For fish farming the alkalinity of the water should not be less than 25 mg/l equivalent calcium carbonate (CaCO3). Farming in extensive earthen ponds, creates an environment mg/l equivalent calcium carbonate $ \mathrm{(C a C O_{3})}

which enhances the natural production. When the water is acidic and the alkalinity is low an environment

(less than 25 mg/l), the buffer capacity of the water should be enhanced. In Nigeria this is pH-environment, when the soil is acidic (pH 6), the water will not have this buffer capacity and you will have to add limestone, which actually is calcium carbonate in order to increase usually carried out by adding lime to the water or onto the bottom of the pond. The dosage is 300 kg per 1000 mthe pH, the buffering of the water and the availability of nutrients from the soil. This way of the pond.

algae can grow and the natural cycle of phytoplankton to zooplankton is triggered.

Catfish thrive better in a pond with an algal bloom than in a clear water environment. When the

## Chapter 9

pH of the soil and the water is already above 7.5 at the end of the day, there is no need for additional liming! New ponds, which just have been constructed, need lime to make them fertile: 2000 kg for sandy soil and 4000 kg for clay soil per ha. This can be carried out in

an empty pond before filling it with water. The lime also disinfects the soil and enhances

mineralisation of the mud. One or two months after the ponds have been filled, you can test the total alkalinity with a test kit available in Nigeria. It should be more than 25 mg/l. If the alkalinity is less than 25 mg/l, you can add another 200 kg of limestone/ha, and repeat this as long as necessary (source: FAO, pond conditioning through liming).

Heavy metals such as copper, zinc, cadmium, leadHeavy metals such as copper, zinc, cadmium, lead

Some heavy metals, in small quantities though, are a necessity for growing fish. They are part of the essential micronutrients which are even added to the feed. But when they occur in the water, even at low concentrations, they will be toxic to the fish and should be avoided by all means.

Normally in groundwater you will not have problems with heavy metals, but when you are using copper or galvanised pipes, you certainly will elevate levels of copper, zinc the levels of copper, zinc and cadmium in the water. This will be devastating for the results of your hatchery. If you use river water, you will not usually have problems with these heavy metals, but when a river passes heavy industrial or urban areas, you have to be cautious. Fish can become chronically sick and get susceptible to diseases or die directly from this type of pollution. Most of these pollutants damage the internal organs and eventually this will lead to mortality. Fish eaten from polluted rivers are even dangerous for human health. The natural food for river fish is polluted as well, and the fish will deposit these heavy metals in their organs and fat.

## Concrete

Newly built concrete ponds filled with water, will elevate the pH (basic) of the water for some weeks, but after this period the pH will be

adjusted to the pH of the incoming water. some weeks, but after this period the pH will be it is advisable to leave a pond at least one or two weeks filled with water without fish in order to neutralize the effect of concrete. After two weeks it's usually safe to stock fish in it, but flush the water first and refill.

## Water temperature

Catfish are tropical fish which cannot survive in cold water. The water temperature should be between 25-30 $ ^{\circ} $ C for good growth and health. The optimum temperature is 28 $ ^{\circ} $ and health. A short period of one or two hours of 12 $ ^{\circ} $ C will not cause the catfish to die. If the water temperature increases gradually after the short cold period, they will just wake up again with little problem. However, longer periods of cold water might initiate fungal fungal growthon the skin, resulting in a quick death. Temperatures above 34 $ ^{\circ} $ C are also dangerous for catfish, because this temperature comes close to the level at which proteins in their

Catfish diseases

body start to denature. Crucial enzymes and metabolic processes especially are irreversibly

damaged leading to mortality as well.

Monitoring the water quality

In order to find out if the levels of ammonium-nitrogen, nitrite, pH, iron, hardness, temperature etcetera are within limits for growing fish, you need to have several test kits or all of them combined in one box (Photo 38).

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_102.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

These test kits are very simple to use and have a very good instruction manual. They have

been especially developed for fish farmers and owners of ornamental fishes.

Feed-related deficiency

If the fish at your farm are completely dependent on the feed you are providing, the feed

should provide all the requirements for the fish. So the levels of protein, fat, ash, minerals

and vitamins should be balanced in order to allow the fish to obtain optimal health and optimal growth. Depending on the growth stage, the requirements change and should be adjusted. If the feed contains too little of a certain requirement, this will immediately be shown by retarded growth and limited feed intake. It becomes even worse if some

requirements are completely missing, such as vitamin C. This will cause the fish to develop

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_103.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Chapter 9

a vitamin deficiency called 'broken head disease' and they will eventually die from it, if not

taken care of.

If you don't make your own feed, there is not much to worry about, as long as you are buying

the feed from a respected feed mill with a proven track record. As already mentioned earlier, are buying

I don't believe in making your own feed. That's why I will not go into this subject in detail. mentioned earlier,

## 9.4.1 BACTERIAL DISEASES

The majority of bacteria which cause diseases in catfish, are normally present on the surface or

in the gut of the fish, or in the water of their culture environment They cause diseases when

the catfish are stressed.

When you carry out a bacterial examination on a fish with a bacterial disease, in many cases you will find out that the disease is multi-bacterial and that the disease is caused by many different bacterial species. The signs of different bacterial diseases in fish are also non-specific.

So, to be sure about which bacterial species has caused the problem is almost impossible either

after a physical examination or after culturing the bacteria in a laboratory.

This is a Gram-negative aerobic bacterium which causes infections on the mouth, barbels and

## Flexibacter columnaris

back of the catfish. Therefore, it is also known as 'saddleback disease' or 'cottonmouth disease'.

The bacteria also produce toxins causing the fish to swim erratically. Strangely enough these bacteria thrive well in well oxygenated water with a very low organic load. You will always find the bacteria in the water, but when the situation is stressful for the catfish and/or when new

catfish are introduced into clean water, the bacteria might get a foothold and cause a disease

outbreak. Hard water also causes the bacteria to be more pathogenic.

In a green water system, as I discussed in chapter 8, it is not likely that catfish will get this disease.

The disease can be treated with industrial salt at a dosage of 6 kg/m $ ^{3} $ as a bath treatment. This

can also be combined with oxytetracycline (OTC) at a dosage of 30 g/mL The OTC and salt treatment should be repeated after the second day, if the concentration of salt has significantly been reduced by flushing.

It is important to start the treatments as soon as you notice the first signs of the disease. If you

don't, you will be dealing with a virulent strain of Flexibacter columnaris which can kill almost all your population in the tank within two days. Smaller catfish are more susceptible than bigger ones.

## Aeromonas hydrophila

Aeromonas hydrophila is a heterotrophic, Gram-negative bacterial species, mainly found climates. The disease is known as 'ulcer disease' or 'red sore disease'. It causes lesions on

the body, and can also cause septicaemia by invading the organs of the fish.

The bacteria primarily affect freshwater fish such as catfish, tilapia and many other tropical

fish. Other symptoms are lack of appetite, swimming abnormally, pale gills and a bloated

hydrophila, run a laboratory test by taking swabs from organs and lesions and grow them on a blood agar. A sensitivity blood agar. A sensitivity test for various available antibiotics to enable application of the most effective ones, can also be

Catfish diseases

included. Aeromonas hydrophila can thrive in low and high oxygen water and prefers organic included.

## polluted water. polluted water.

Catfish are not usually affected by this bacterial species, but at an increased stress level caused by poor handling, bad water quality, poor feeding, temperature fluctuations etcetera, it might

break out. In Nigerian catfish farming this disease is the most common one to affect farms.

Usually it doesn't lead to mass mortality, but it can reduce a population in a tank by 10 to 20%. It starts with a few fish dying in one day and increases to 1-2% of dead fish within the next 24 hours. Gradually the mortality reduces again till it totally stops. When the fish are in a good environment, the disease is usually over after 10 days.

When you have a disease outbreak in bigger fish, you will see a lot of slime and skin particles

making the water cloudy. You have to flush more in order to keep the water clean.

Treatment can be applied in the same way you treat a disease caused by Flexibacter columnaris: 6 kg/m $ ^{3} $ industrial salt and 30 g/m $ ^{3} $ OTC. Apart from this, you could also apply OTC in the feed at a rate of 50 g/ton of fish a day for a period of 10 days.

## Potential concern for human health

An Aeromonas hydrophila infection can be spread from fish to humans and vice versa. If youare healthy, it will not be likely to happen, but small children and people with an immunedeficient system can get infected. The symptoms, such as diarrhoea, are the same as in cholera.

I always recommend fish farmers to feed the fish with a spoon or a basket and not by hand,

because this disease can also be spread from human beings to fish. Sick fish should be handled

with gloves!

## Citrobacter freundii

As with the other bacterial diseases, Citrobacter freundii, which is a Gram-negative motile

bacterial species, is triggered by bad environmental factors, such as poor water quality, high water temperature and other stress factors. A typical symptom for infected African catfish, is a swollen head kidney. This can be seen just after the pectoral fins. It can even burst through the skin leaving an ulcer behind. The fish are sluggish and will certainly die from it. The head kidney

is a blood forming organ and if it is affected, it will affect the whole body causing septicaemia.

This occurs when a bacterial infection elsewhere in the body, for example in the kidneys, enters the bloodstream. This is fatal in most cases because the bacteria and their toxins can be carried

through the bloodstream to all the other organs of the fish.

Once when I had a problem at the farm with this disease at the growth stage of juveniles, we

ran a sensitivity test which indicated that Trimethoprim as a bath treatment at a dosage of 10

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_104.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

## Chapter 9

g/m $ ^{3} $ performed well. It can also be used in the feed at a dosage of 30 g/ton of fish in a period

of 7 days. Trimethoprim is also considered a broad-spectrum antibiotic

Gram-negative bacteria: what does it mean?

In microbiology, laboratory tests are run to find out which type of bacteria is causing the fish to

get sick. Gram staining is a method for bacterial differentiation: if the cell retains crystal violet,

it is called Gram positive-purple coloration, if it doesn't,

coloration). Hans Christian Gram invented the Gram staining method as early as 1882.

Unfortunately, the use of antibiotics is more an exercise of trial and error. While your fish

The effectiveness of antibiotics in treating bacterial diseases

are dying, you don't have the time to go to a laboratory to find out which bacterial

species is responsible for the disease and which antibiotic will be effective. Also, in Nigeria you rarely find laboratories which specialise in fish diseases and are able to run a sensitivity test. goes as follows:

## 1.

## 2.

Spread and grow the isolated bacteria on an agar plate (a bacterial growth medium

solidified with agar in a Petri dish).

3. Take the dominant growing bacteria colony to another agar plate which contains

several types of antibiotics in little circles. The bacteria will grow within the antibiotic

circles, but when the outside of one of the circles shows no bacterial growth, it means

that the bacteria are inhibited or killed by that type of antibiotic.

When you have found the right antibiotic by a sensitivity test, the veterinarian can prescribe the one you should use to treat your fish effectively.

## The silver bullet

As already mentioned, treating bacterial fish diseases with antibiotics is in many cases a matter of trial and error. However, there is this broadspectrum antibiotic Enrofloxacin, which is considered to be very effective for bacterial diseases in fish. The brand name in Nigeria is Kenflox 20% Oral. When nothing works, this medicine will be your last hope. That's why it

is also called 'the silver bullet': a magical solution to a confusing problem! This antibiotic can

be applied in the water or in the feed. the recommended dosage used is 10 mg Enrofloxacin/kg fish a day for 5 days. Added to the water, farmers use a dosage of 5 ml for 1

m $ _{3} $ of water which effectively is not more than 1 ml of 100% Enrofloxacin per

they repeat the dosage for 3 days.
