9.4.2 PARASITES

Introduction

Parasites are easily spotted on fish either by eye or microscope depending on the species. In

order to multiply, some parasites need a secondary host, such as a snail or a bird. These kinds of parasites you will rarely find at indoor farms, but only at outdoor farms with ponds in a farms with ponds in a natural environment, filled and flushed with river water. Other parasites

don't need a second host. environment, filled and flushed with river water. Other parasites don't need a host. They can be found indoors as well as outdoors. Parasites in catfish are not common and they have are not common and they

have little effect on catfish bigger than 50 g. However, in hatcheries parasites can cause severe damage

and if not treated in time, you will lose the majority of the young fish within a week.

The parasites spotted on catfish are ecto-parasites, and are based on the skin or gills. They areeasy to scrape off with a swab or surgical blade and put on a glass slide for identification under

a microscope. The list of parasites is long. Therefore, I will only mention the parasites I have

actually seen and experienced in catfish myself.

Dactylogyrus - Gill fluke or gill wormDactylogyrus - The gill fluke or gill worm

In 1994 I wanted to refresh my brood stock at my farm in the Netherlands, to avoid

## which had formerly been used for eel

inbreeding. I bought matured catfish from a farm

production; a massive farm with an enormous filtration system. The brood stock I bought was infected with gill worms, also called gill fuke or Dactylogyrus. The transmission of the gill worms to the catfish was caused by the eels which had previously been grown. Although there were no eels at that farm anymore, eggs must have stayed behind in the

filtration system and they were able to find the catfish. Big catfish don't mind gill worms

and I didn't put my new brood stock in quarantine and neither didn't check if they had any ectoparasites. So, when I started to use these brood stocks, I transferred the gill worms to my freshly hatched fries. The signs were clear because the young fish behaved sluggishly, by hanging in the upper layers of the water column. This was was confrmed

when I used my microscope and saw them hooked to the gills of my little fry. Next, I

used a medicine called Masoten (organophosphate insecticide) to kill those worms. This medicine is widely used in eel farming, but also on

animals, such as cows and goats and even human beings. The veterinarian guaranteed it was a very safe and effective medicine to use. So, I treated all my fry stocked in more than 10 tanks at once. After two

days, all the fry were dying and I discovered that catfish cannot handle this medicine; it's

toxic to them. With the next batches of fry, I disinfected the systems thoroughly before hatching, and if they got sick from gill worms, I just allowed it to happen because they didn't die from it and finally grew over it. As a young fish farmer, I was crying over my fish and over my mistakes but it didn't kill me, and what doesn't kill you makes you stronger!

Gyrodactylus - Skin fluke

The catfish parasite Gyrodactylus (Figure 28) belongs to the same family as the Dactylogyrus. Gyrodactylus parasites attach themselves to the skin of the catfish and bear live young. Inan adult Gyrodactylus you can already discover the babies in the body, if you put a swab if you put a swab of it under the microscope. So, they multiply very quickly and can turn into a big problem turn into a big problem forcatfish smaller than 20 g, if the conditions for the Gyrodactylus are favourable. In addition, favourable. In addition,

the consumption of the skin of the catfish by this parasite favours the introduction of bacterial infections on top of it. The catfish can die in large numbers when not taken care of.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_107.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 28. Drawing of the catfish parasite Gyrodactylus.

Fortunately, formalin is an effective medicine to stop the invasion. The dosage is 28 ml/m $ ^{3} $ at the concentration of 38% formalin. Use the formalin in combination with salt at a dosage of 1 kg/m $ ^{3} $. The water should not be flushed for 12 hours and afterwards start flushing

gradually. Checking with the microscope, you will notice a close to 100% reduction of the

parasites. If needed, repeat the treatment the second day.

Note. Formalin is also very toxic for catfish and the dosage used for treatment is not far away from their lethal doses as well! Calculation of the exact volume of water should

therefore be taken seriously. If you are not sure whether the fish can take the dosage, test

it on a small number of fish!

For example:

The fish pond has the dimension of 5.5 x 2.4 x 0.8 m (length x width x depth). The

volume is 5.5 x 2.4 x 0.8 m=10.56 m $ ^{3} $. The dosage is 10.56 x 28 ml/m $ ^{3} $ =295.68 ml

- Buy the formalin from a trustworthy supplier so that the % of formalin is according to the label on the bottle and not diluted. 38% formalin has a very penetrating smell, so use it with care. Wear gloves and a face mask.

Chapter 9

## Protozoan parasites

Protozoan single-celled parasites are troublesome and can multiply even more quickly than the parasites I have mentioned above. They multiply by binary fission: one parasite becomes

two, two parasites become four, and so on.

The ones I have seen on African catfish are:

Chilodonella, Trichodina, and the white spot disease-causing Ichthyophthirius multifiliis. All of the single-celled protozoa, such as Chilodonella, Trichodina, and Ichthyophthirius

multifiliis (Figure 29) are categorised as ciliates and cause grey thick slime on the skin or white spot

disease. Ciliates belong to a group of protozoans which have hair-like organelles around the cell, called 'cilia'. By taking some slime from the skin, all of these parasites are easily identified under a microscope at a magnification of just 100 times. You can even see them moving. They stick to the skin, fins, or gills of a catfish, causing either grey thick slime

on the skin, or, in the case of white spot disease, hundreds of spots of circa 0.5 mm to 1 mm on

on the entire body of the fish. Always use live fish for examination, since many parasites leave the host very quickly after the fish dies. By feeding on the gills, skin and slime of the fish, these parasites cause a lot of damage.

White spot disease has a life cycle: the larval stage is found on the fish, but after feeding

and growing to a spot of approximately 1 mm, the parasites will leave the fish and mature.

They multiply at the bottom of the tank and produce hundreds of new small larvae (cysts or new small larvae (cysts or spores) which in their turn look for a weak fish to infect. The life cycle takes six to eight days and is highly dependent on the water temperature.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_108.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_109.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_110.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 29. Left to right: single-cell catfish parasites Chilodonella, Trichodina and Ichtyophthirius multifilis.

Treatment against protozoan parasites

One treatment usually doesn't solve the problem with protozoan parasites. White spot disease especially needs multiple treatments to eventually stop the disease completely. Only the free-swimming spores of Ichtyophthirius multifilis are sensitive to chemicals, the other stages are

not. Dead fish should be removed swiftly in order to reduce the spread of the disease.

Catfish diseases

Many chemicals can be used to kill the parasites:

- Salt (NaCl)

Chloramine T

## 9.4.3 VIRAL DISEASES

## Definition of a virus

A virus is a small particle that is capable of infecting a cell and has the potential to cause

a disease. The cell that is infected by the virus is called a 'host cell'. Most viruses are too

small to be seen with a normal microscope. A virus is unable to reproduce without the help

## of the host cell.

There are a few viral fish diseases, but till today researchers have not yet isolated any virus in African catfish which causes serious damage. In general, viral fish diseases are not

treatable and can cause a high mortality especially among young fish. Fish which survive

the disease, become carriers and infect other fish which have not yet been exposed.

New fish viruses are still being diagnosed, which is a serious threat to aquaculture in general. Movements of fish from one continent to the other, make it even easier for viruses to spread

over the world very quickly. One of the latest examples is the Tilapia lake virus (TilV) which

was reported in 2014 in Ecuador and Israel. At present it has been reported in Asia and also in Lake Victoria among wild populations. It was suspected of causing the mass mortality at some of the cage farms in Volta Lake, but that did not appear to be the case.

Ghana authorities have strict regulations when it comes to importation of improved tilapia

strains into the country; actually, farmers can only use the local indigenous strains.

## Chapter 9

However, this holds back the introduction to Ghana of good growing strains of tilapia, produced in other parts of the world. But at the same time these regulations at least help the biosecurity and avoid the introduction of diseases which can cause severe damage to

both wild and farmed tilapia populations.

## 9.5 MEDICATION

A good farmer should have the most important medicines in stock, well stored in a cool,

dark and dry environment. Fish diseases spread very quickly and once detected, the fish should be treated immediately. It will save you a lot of fish and money if you don't waste time!

There are 3 ways to apply medication:

- Apply in the feed

Applying drugs in the feed can only work if the fish are still eating. Usually the dosage is

given as x mg/kg of fish a day. The feed is given in % of bodyweight and should be reduced

to less than 1% of the bodyweight in a day. So, you need to know the number and the

approximate size of the fish in the pond you want to treat with medication.

Example 14. How to calculate the daily dosage of medication applied in feed? Suppose that you have stocked 5000 catfish and after 2 weeks mortality starts and you

suspect a bacterial infection. The fish are stocked at an average of 10 g a piece and in 2

weeks they were fed 40 kg.

The estimated biomass of the fish will be:

5000 x 0.01 kg + 40 kg x 1.0 (FCR=1) = 90 kg

The dosage of applying Oxytetracycline (OTC) in the feed is 75 mg/kg of fish.

So, the dosage on a daily basis for a period of 7 days is:

90 kg x 75 mg/kg = 6750 mg or approximately 7 g.

You feed the fish 1% of the bodyweight on a daily basis which is 90 kg x 1/100=0.9 kg

In summary you apply 7 g of OTC per day in 0.9 kg of starter feed for 7 days.

Note. Mixing the antibiotic in the feed should be carried out with gloves Normally the antibiotic will stick to the oil-coated starter feed. If the feed is too dry, you can add a little vegetable oil to make the feed sticky for the antibiotic.

168

- Apply to the water

Catfish diseases

Applying medication to the water is not always feasible. When fish are stocked in a pond

with a very large volume of water, it will simply cost too much. In some cases, you can

reduce (lower) the volume of water in order to save on the amount of medication. You

can give the fish a permanent bath by applying a dose of medicine in the water and let the fish remain in it for hours, or you

and salt treatments can be carried out as a permanent bath at low concentrations or a dip

treatment when high concentrations are applied. I personally don't like the dip treatment except for cleaning the brood stock before using them for spawning or before introducing them to other fish.

Example 15. How to calculate the daily dosage of medication applied in water?

A concrete tank has the dimension of 5 x 2 x 0.8 m and you want to treat the fish with OTC 40 g/m $ ^{3} $. You reduce the water level to 0.4 m. How much OTC should you

use?

5 x 2 x 0.4 m = 4 m $ _{3} $ volume of the pond. Dosage: 4 m $ _{3} $ x 40 g/m $ _{3} $ = 160 g.

Solution:

The OTC should remain in tank for at least 4 hours, followed by adding fresh water.

Note. OTC is yellow, but when it starts to decompose after some time it becomes brown.

So, the water colours brown too, but that is not a problem. There is no need to flush it.

OTC can be bought in different grades of purity; all the dosages given are for the active ingredient in the medicine.

Example 16. How to calculate the dosage of medication based on the percentage of active ingredient?

The OTC you are buying has an active ingredient of 100 g OTC/kg, which means that the medicine has 10% active ingredient.

The dosage of 40 g/m $ ^{3} $ has to be multiplied by $ 1 0=4 0 0 \mathrm{~ g / m^{3}}.

Always try to buy medicine with 100% active ingredient. The inactive ingredient will pollute the water.

- Apply by injection

Applying medicine by injection is not used in catfish farming, but it is normal with.

Chapter 9

ornamental fish which are very expensive or which have emotional value. For catfish It Apply by injection

would be just too much hassle and expense to inject each fish separately! Applying medicine by injection is not used in catfish farming, but it is normal with ornamental

fish which are very expensive or which have emotional value. For catfish It

9.6 BIOSECURITY

9.6 BIOSECURITY in fish farming consists of practices that minimize the risk of introducing an

infectious disease and spreading it to other fish, either at the farm or outside the farm.

## 10.1 INTRODUCTION

Fish farm management starts with making a production plan and following it so that

the production estimated will be achieved. For farm management records are very

important; they show the progress of the farm and whether you are on track to reach

your targets.

10.2 HOW TO MAKE A PRODUCTION

PLAN: CASE STUDY

Let us start with an example of a catfish farm with a flow-through system. I'll take you through the necessary calculations to estimate the production and the inputs needed.

Quantify the facility:

- 50 concrete tanks of 50 m each

Growth cycle and production figures:

- Hatchery producing juveniles: 2 months

Pre on-growing producing post-juveniles: 45 days On-growing producing table-sized fish: 150 days Density in pre on-growing: 500 pieces/m $ _{3} $

Density in on-growing: 100 pieces/m $ _{3} $

Water usage: 1.4 m $ ^{3} $ /kg of feed

FCR (feed conversion rate) for pre on-growing: 0.7

FCR for on-growing: 1.25

Target: table-sized catfish in the range of 1.5 to 2.0 kg

Calculation

We will start with calculating the maximum production for the ongrowing stage. Then we will calculate if the facilities for the pre on-growing

stage and the hatchery stage are sufficient to provide the fish needed for the on-growing stage.

Fish farm management

Each tank in the on-growing system can provide a minimum of 2 cycles/ year: 365/150=2.4 cycles, but we reduce it to 2, since the tanks will be empty for some time before restocking and in case the sales of the table sized fish are delayed a bit. It is always good

to allow yourself some space to manoeuvre. Be realistic.

Production capacity in the on-growing system

50 $ m_{3} $ (volume of pond) x 100 fish/$ m_{3} $ (density) x 1.75 kg (average weight) x 2 (number of cycles/annum) x 50 (number of ponds) = 875, 000 kg of table-sized catfish per annum.

In practice, you will sell 2 ponds every week with only a 2 week's break! The production

of each pond is 8, 750 kg.

Post-juveniles needed per annum: 100 x 5000 x 1.1 (+/- 10% mortality during 150 days)

Water needed per annum:

stocking density at the end of the growth stage is 500 pieces/m $ _{2} $ and the tank is 11 m $ _{2} $; so, we can harvest 5, 500

Advice

The intake pump provides 200 m/hour. In order to supply 4, 200 m/day, it has to pumpfor 21 hours. However, if the pump fails, you actually do not have any back-up in thereservoir. If you want to have a back-up water supply for 1 day, the reservoir should

have a volume of at least 4, 200 m $ ^{3} $ and the pump should have a capacity of 400 m $ ^{3} $ /

hour. After one full day of pumping, you will have served the need for one day and have obtained circa 4, 200 m $ ^{3} $ extra for the following day. If your reservoir is already full, you only need to pump approximately 11 hours a day to keep it that way.

Production capacity in the pre on-growing system

We have 15 tanks for the pre on-growing which takes 45 days. We can do 365/45 cycles a year = 8 cycles a year but practically we would count on having 7 cycles a year, because of delay by stocking, cleaning etcetera. The

pieces per cycle. The production capacity of 1 pre on-growing tank is 7 x 5, 500 pieces

= 37, 500 pieces.

The total capacity of the pre on-growing to serve the on-growing is 15 x 37, 500 pieces = 577, 500 post-juveniles. We need 550, 000 post-juveniles, so the capacity should be

enough.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_111.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

10

The mortality rate in the pre on-growing is estimated at approximately 20%. It is important to stock well graded juveniles of 5 g and make sure all the shooters are removed. So, the hatchery should supply 550, 000 x 1.2 = 660, 000 pieces a year. Each

tank in the pre on-growing system is stocked with 6, 600 pieces.

What is the reason for having a pre on-growing system?

Some readers might wonder why you need a pre on-growing stage. Why not stock the juveniles from the hatchery directly in the on-growing system?

By stocking small fish in a big pond, the pond is not utilized efficiently. This way of stocking increases the growth cycle from 150 days to 195 days which reduces the production capacity by almost 25%. The big tanks are an expensive investment and therefore it's important to use them intensively.

Stocked juveniles of 5 g need grading after 45 days, because there will still be

shooters and runts around. If you don't take them out, you will end up with a varied batch of fish, more cannibalism and a few catfish which don't grow but still consume feed. The feed conversion rate will be negatively affected by it. In the stage of growing juveniles to post-juveniles from 5 g to 80 g, the g to 80 g, the fish

are still sensitive and can fall sick. Treatment in a small tank, especially a bath

treatment, is easier and cheaper compared to a large tank.

The juveniles from the hatchery have been raised in borehole water and have to be weaned to river water, especially during the rainy season when the river water is muddy. So, the supply of pre on-growing has two sources of water:

river water and borehole water.

The hatchery

The capacity of the hatchery has been estimated at 1, 000, 000 juveniles. For growing table-sized fish, you need to take out only 660, 000 juveniles of 5 g. So, the capacity of

the hatchery is enough and even allows you to sell some young fish to other farmers.

10.3 CHECK POINTS FOR THE MANAGER

8 points for the manager to check:

1. The stocks of fish in number, age and weight on a weekly basis.

2. The feed given per tank on a daily basis with a weekly summary.

3. The feed stocks on a weekly basis.

4. Your staff clocking in and out.

5. The budget for petty cash made and controlled on a weekly basis.

Fish farm management

6. The stocks of diesel for the generator and its service programme on a weekly

basis.

7. The harvest and sales and outstanding customer funds.

8. The safety of the environment for staff and customers, which also needs

continuous maintenance.

To check all these points, you need to keep records. Below you 'll see the formats for each of them. The formats are filled in for easy understanding. They don't

correspond with each other, and are not based on the examples given before

in this chapter.

## 1. Check the stocks of fish in number and in weight on a weekly

basis

Every week you should have the following information available for each tank, and also

have a summary for all the tanks together.

For each tank:

You should make the calculations of example 17 for each tank every week. As a manager you can derive a lot of information from them:

You will know the total number of fish on the farm.

## 178

You will know the average fish size of each pond and when they will

You will know the total standing stock in kg of the farm.

be ready for selling.

These figures shouldn't fluctuate much. If they get lower, it means you are selling more

than you are stocking. They also give you the size of the fish by calculation and not by

test cropping. This is possible, because the FCR is derived from earlier harvesting results, and the FCR fluctuations are low if the farm is operating constantly and doing well. Test cropping of fish, in my opinion disturbs the fish a lot. It slows down their growth and it does not even yield a clear record of the size of the fish. Also, you are able to predict the

number of fish to sell during the coming months because your target is age 180 days. Any

fish that is 150 days old or older can be sold the next month. Never base your sales on the size of the fish but always on age, whether they are big or small. By doing so, you have a clear and stable growth cycle which makes it possible to predict and forecast results.

2. Check the feed gift per tank on a daily basis with a weekly summary For every tank make a feeding list which should be filled in during the week. It shows the weight in kg and the particle size in mm of the feed used. The progress of feeding already provides an indication of the performance of the fish. Every day there should be an increase of feed (0.5 kg or 1 kg). Since the fish are growing on a daily basis, they should get more

feed every day. A reduction of the feed given each day during the week, is a result of

problems in the tank, cold weather, disturbance, no feed available or other problems. This

Many farmers love to keep the feed gift per day constant for one week and after one or

should be noticed and checked.

two weeks they suddenly increase it. They also like to feed a full bag of feed and jump

Fish farm management

to two bags after some time. It's pure laziness. It does not work like this. These farmers simply don't want to weigh out the feed. Erratic feeding patterns can never give you good growth and good feed conversion rates. I believe that underfeeding the fish is the biggest

problem in Nigeria. Farmers are afraid to spend money on feed for their fish, but they lack

the understanding that the profit comes from the feed; the more you feed the more profit

you make!

The empty feed bags yield valuable information and should be collected and stored. For

example, if the farm uses 15, 000 kg of feed during the week, you should have 1000 empty

feed bags, which comes down to 83 dozen. If bags are missing, it could be 2

a result of bad 3

recording, incorrect weighing out the feed or theft. 4

3. Check the feed stocks on a weekly basis

Checking the feed stocks can be carried out by taking physical stock every week. In order

to do this, each feed size has to be stocked properly and in such a way, that

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_114.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

During the week there will be changes; stocks will reduce when feed is given to the workers to feed the fish and they will increase when feed is purchased. The feed that comes in, should also be added to the stock. The changes should reflect the consumption of feed

during the week. Afterwards, the storekeeper should provide the farm manager with the

records.

The records of the feed stocks are important, because they will inform you when you will be out of stock. For example, a farm which feeds around 3, 000 kg on a daily basis,

should determine the minimum stock level which depend solely on the lead time between

ordering and getting the feed and the reliability of the feed company. To be on the safe side for not running out of feed, the minimum stock level before ordering should be the daily consumption x 2 times the lead time.

Example 19. How to calculate minimum stock level of feed?

Suppose the daily feed gift is 3, 000 kg

4. Check your staff clock in and out

If you want to create discipline with your staff, you have to start an attendance list where

they can sign in and out and note the time of day when they come in and go out of the

farm.

During the day, the staff should remain on the farm or have written permission to go out, given by the farm manager. At big companies they have a time keeper to monitor these things. Normally, he is assisted in doing this by the gate man.

If the farm is small, it is the personal responsibility of the staff to remain at the farm and carry out the work which has to be done. But the moment a farm becomes big, many workers believe that if they are not doing their job, somebody else will do it.

Workers who are at the farm during the night should by no means go out. Because, if

anything happens at the farm, such as robbery, theft or any other criminal offence, the

people who have left the farm illegally, are the first suspects!

## the list clearly shows the days worked by

The attendance list shows the manager the loyalty of each staff member which can be used

each worker and their corresponding salaries. As a manager you should keep a clear-cut distinction between you and your staff. You can be friendly to them and interested in their well-being, but you should not become emotionally attached to them, in order to keep a clear unbiased eye on each of them.

for decisions about future bonuses. But primarily

## 5. Check and budget for petty cash on a weekly basis

Every week the manager should budget for petty cash needed for the coming week. This

money will come in on Monday morning, and by the end of the working day, the money

should be counted and balanced. All the money going out should be accounted for! If you

take the budget from the sales activities, it will become very blurry and difficult to get clear

records of expenses and turnover.

to pay by bank transfer. The fewer cash transactions the better; if the sausage is close to

It is best to have a limited number of suppliers which provide you with credit or allow you

the dog, the dog will get tempted and eventually eat it, regardless the level of training! A large income of cash attracts criminals and it is very difficult to handle these kinds of situations.

Fish farm management

6. Check the diesel stocks for the generator and the service

programme on a daily basis

In some farms the cost of diesel exceeds the cost of labour! So, it's obvious that the diesel

consumption has to be checked and controlled by the management. Diesel is widely used

and, once stolen, easy to trade and convert into money.

Depending on the size of the generator and farm, you should have a calibrated tank, so that you can dip on a daily basis to find out how much diesel is in the tank and how much

has been consumed by the various machines per day. If the generator is small, you can

work with 50-1 jerry cans. The moment you fuel the generator tank, you note the volume and check its running hours. What you want to find out is the consumption per hour of the generator. If you know this, you can be aware of changes in the consumption of the generator per hour, and you are also able to predict the consumption for a period of time.

Always refill the generator till the brim. Running a generator on a low level of diesel in the

tank, is not good for the engine and you also lose control over the consumption of diesel

per hour.

When you combine a generator with electricity from the PHCN, you should have an alarm

system for when the PHCN-electricity goes off or comes back, in order not to overuse the

## generator or have unnoticed power outages.

Some farmers keep very low stocks of diesel or petrol and fail to have constant power for pumping water or for running their hatchery; don't be surprised that you don't get

good results at your farm. Minimising the cost of energy is actually penny wise and pound

## foolish!

Servicing the generator, either a petrol or diesel one, is of utmost importance if you don't want any nasty surprises; make a servicing programme and follow it. Servicing is different

from fixing the generator when it gets faulty.

The consumption of a generator depends on the load. The table in Figure 30 below in Figure 30 shows the consumption of diesel per hour in relation to the load and the size of the generator.

authorized

7. Check the harvest and sales and outstanding customer funds Cropping and sales are actually two different things. When customers visit the farm, the best way to sell them the fish is at a point of sales. When you sell the fish directly from the pond, all your customers are at your farm at once and become a threat for biosecurity. Your customers carry baskets from one farm to the other and they don't have

any idea of biosecurity. The fish in the ponds close to the pond you are selling the fish

from, will also be disturbed by all the activity. It is advisable to harvest the fish and carry

them to a point of sales close to the gate.

When you harvest the fish, you should weigh them too. Then you can sell them at

the point of sales per basket of 25 kg. The people who harvest the fish should not be

the same ones who sell them. At the end of the sales day, you compare the harvest results to the sales results. The difference between them should not be more than 3%.

The difference arises from not being able to sell exactly 25 kg but 25.3 kg or 25.5 kg. Your customers are very keen to get a little bit more, since the fish lose weight during

transportation but they will have to sell the basket for 25 kg to their customers. It is best.

to use a digital scale and a calibrated weight of 10 or 25 kg to convince your customers that your scale is accurate. See below example 25 showing harvesting and sales results in a month's period.

Chapter 10

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_117.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

<table class="table table-bordered"><thead><tr><th>Date</th><th>Harvested (kg)</th><th>Sales (N)</th><th>Sales (kg)</th><th>Difference (kg)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>03/01/2019</td><td>5,430</td><td>3,909,600</td><td>5,270</td><td>160</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>24/01/2019</td><td>6,320</td><td>4,518,800</td><td>6,190</td><td>130</td></tr></tbody></table>

It is an obligation to keep the working environment safe for your staff.

Operating machinery should be carried out with hand gloves, helmets, ear protection, glasses etcetera.

Working with chemicals, such as fish medication, should be executed with

personal protection.

Harvesting fish should be carried out with a wet suit, rain boots etcetera.

Fire extinguishers and the first aid kit should be available and up to date.

Rats and mice should be eradicated by avoiding spillage of fish feed, and to

the environment clean. Use rat poison in order to avoid diseases such as Lassa

fever.

Waste removal has to be done regularly.

The staff should be educated that working safely and keeping the environment clean is every body's responsibility.

## 11

CATFISH MARKETING

11.1 INTRODUCTION

11.2 PRODUCT FORMS

11.3 PRICING

## 11.1 INTRODUCTION

Most farmers have no idea how to sell fish when they start farming. They believe that

that catfish will sell anyway and that there are never enough of them in the market. Yes,

globally this is correct; Nigeria still imports a lot of fish, but that doesn't mean that all imported fish can be replaced by farmed Nigerian catfish. Many Nigerians also like to eat sea fish such as shrimps and tilapia, fish products such as Titus, and other canned also like to eat seafish, products. So, to be successful in fish farming requires a plan and an innovative

approach to the marketapproach to the market.

Wholesalers

The easiest way to sell fish is by contacting the wholesalers or highvolume buyers who buy all your fish at once. If you are producing large quantities of fish, in principle you

have to work with buyers who are able to distribute the fish to the markets in Nigeria.

These kinds of customers are able to buy all your table-sized fish and transport them as far as a full day's journey. They take responsibility for transport and take care of collecting the money for the fish from the customers, mostly retailers, who sell fish too. The major disadvantage of wholesalers as customers is that the price you get for

your catfish is controlled by them. When you are a small-scale farmer, it could be less

profitable for you to venture into selling to them, since your cost price is relatively high

because you don't farm at the ideal economic scale.

Niche markets

As a small-scale farmer, you should look at markets which are smaller and closer to

your farm: these are called niche markets. This way, you 'll become a marketer and in some cases even a retailer, alongside being a fish farmer. It takes time to analyse and develop these niche markets but you have more control over the sales price and it will be higher.

## Plan and planning

Marketing requires a plan and planning. How much fish must I sell within a certain time to have a balanced standing stock? The standing stock is the quantity of fish at the farm and it can be derived from the production records. If the standing stock increases,

the number of fish you sell, is lower than you produce, which means that your fish

will grow bigger and are at the farm longer than necessary. This way more farm space will be occupied and the production will go down. On the other hand, if you sell more than you produce, you will soon be out of production and the fish available for sale, become smaller in size. You will soon have empty ponds and the production will reduce

drastically.

190

## Target size

Catfish marketing

Another inadvisable way of selling is by top cropping. Top cropping means grading the big

fish out and leaving the smaller fish in the pond. The advantage of this approach is that you

start to sell earlier and initially your cash flow will increase. However, at a later stage, it will

be detrimental, because the smaller fish that are left in the pond, will not grow anymore because of the disturbance of the top cropping activity in their pond. Neither do you make optimal use of the pond space. Always sell according to your planning and let the target size be the average size of the fish in the pond.

If the market is strong, you will be tempted to over sell, but you will certainly regret this. Stick to your growth cycle and the size of fish you want to sell. On the other hand, keeping the fish in the pond because the price is not favourable to you, can become very expensive, since the fish have to be maintained in the pond and consume feed, while they don't grow

rapidly anymore. Sometimes you have to reduce the price in order to keep the standing stock

constant and the production going.

Good and bad prices

In general, the price you get for your catfish, should not be calculated based on one month,

but on a production cycle of one year. You will have good and bad prices, but it will balance

out. Many farmers are discouraged to buy juveniles when the table-sized fish price is low, which is a big mistake. The time of excess fish is actually

## Competition

As already said, catfish are not the only fish eaten in Nigeria. There is a lot of competition from river fish and sea fish. Frozen fish imported from Europe, has been very popular, but it has become expensive since the government introduced import regulations to protect the

the best time to buy juveniles because the market will be strong in six months' time. However, the best approach to marketing is to produce as efficiently as possible and have a constant production at the lowest cost price.

Most fish are caught during the dry season from January to April and these supplies certainly compete with the farmed fish.

The number of catfish that are produced varies too; the supply is highest at the beginning of the dry season and lowest when the rains start. Catfish normally sell easily from March to

Nigerian fishing and aquaculture industry. Also, the fishermen's supply varies during the year.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_119.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

April. The variable supply of catfish is due to the rainfall. Many farmers are able to produce

more fish during the rainy season but have problems keeping the fish in the ponds during the dry season and therefore want to sell by any possible means during this period. The middle men take advantage of this situation. The 'rainwater-farmers', who must plan their production in relation to the rainwater availability, have a big disadvantage in comparison to

farmers who do not have to rely on this water source.

## Chapter 11

## 11.2 PRODUCT FORMS

The catfish industry is dominated by only two products: live catfish and smoked catfish.

You rarely see any other product around. This is a logical development since catfish can be

easily kept alive with a little water and customers love to buy live fish especially in Nigeria

where the so-called cold chain is not well developed.

The optimum proof of freshness is a fish that is still alive and moving. Roadside catfish

Live catfish

sellers know this very well and shake the catfish in order to draw attention to the traffic passing by and to show the fish are still alive!

The popular beer joints have their slogan "Point and kill". The most popular way to eat catfish is in a pepper soup, which definitely also helps to increase the beer consumption.

They offer either a complete small catfish or a part of a bigger catfish in the soup. You can

choose either head, middle or tail. When the fish is cut in pieces, the retailer can make good money out of one fish. Therefore, the demand for big fish is high, which results in a higher price per kg. The catfish can also be grilled with spices and vegetables wrapped in aluminium foil. This dish comes with chips or any other type of high carb food. Big fish are

popular in this type of dish, because people like to share the fish with two or three others.

As a farmer you are unlikely to stand out with live catfish; there is no brand for it and the fish cannot advertise for you. The moment the seller

has them in his basket, the fish have become anonymous. This doesn't mean that bad fish sell as well as good fish. If a farmer

wants customers to come back and pay a good price, he needs to be aware of this.

With product forms which have a package, the package reveals the source of the product and can advertise for itself.

The following quality aspects should be taken into consideration when selling live

The gut of the fish must be completely empty, so no feeding 36 hours before selling. If not, the fish will vomit and deposit their waste in the water which will make the water and fish start to smell bad in no time.

The fish should be healthy, having no wounds on the body or any other abnormalities.

The fish should look well fed. Lean fish have more bone than meat, which is not

desirable for the end-user!

The female fish should not be full of eggs with a bloated belly. Some people like

the eggs, but most people don't.

Catfish marketing

The catfish should not have a lot of belly fat, because it is not eaten and

feed is very high. The energy will be stored as mesenteric fat and will not be used for growth.

Fish which are ready to be sold, should be graded by size.

Catfish transport

Marketers buy fish and load their vans and cars with plastic bowls covered with sacks.

Each bowl contains 25 kg of catfish and 10 to 15 l of water. The sack is made of a woven

material which allows air to pass through. In order to avoid foaming, they put a bit of

palm oil in the water by using a 5-ml cap of an ordinary plastic bottle. Planks between the bowls are used to support them. In this way a van can carry over 40 bowls filled with 1000 kg of fish. If the car is being driving, open windows will provide enough ventilation. But, if the car is stationary, the bowls with fish become overheated and the accumulation of

carbon dioxide in the water can easily weaken the fish or even kill them. Carbon dioxide

gas is heavier than air, so the accumulated gas will remain right above the surface of the water in the bowl. As a result, the fish will suffocate. Retailers will know that the fish have

been struggling to stay alive, because when you cook these catfish, their meat is not firm anymore. Also, the end-users, who eat them will not enjoy the meat, because its texture

has become mushy. That is why the retailers should also consider how to store the catfish

in order to maintain good quality. Almost all retailers use bathtubs, but they should but they should cover them in order to allow ventilation. Change the water once or twice a day, but never use city council water because of the added chlorine.

Smoked catfish

## 1.

Smoked for a short period of time, provides the catfish with its particular smoke taste

## 2.

and preparation, but the fish have not yet been dried. They should preferably be eaten

the same day they are bought or they should be kept in the fridge.

Smoked for a longer period of time provides the catfish not only with its particular taste and preparation but also with the drying necessary to keep them in good condition

without refrigeration. The moisture content of the fish can be as low as 10-15% and

the fish will have lost a lot of weight. Therefore, most of the smoked fish in the market

are sold without knowing the weight but by eye!

Smoking fish can be carried out in an oven or kiln with charcoal, wood, electricity or gas

## Chapter 11

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_120.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

a farmer smoke the fish yourself, you can develop a brand if the fish are properly packaged. Some fishmongers smoke sick or dead catfish, because the smoking process camouflages the freshness of the fish. This is a bad development. Therefore, I advise you to package and

brand your catfish, when you smoke them yourself.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_121.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Photo 39. An oven or kiln for smoking catfish.

Catfish fillets

Another catfish product which is not yet very popular in Nigeria, is catfish fillets. The catfish industry in the USA, Vietnam and Europe, relies on

them either fresh on ice in insulated Styrofoam boxes or frozen in sealed plastic bags.

Value can be added by marinating the fillets with different flavours. Catfish fillets are quite neutral in taste which can be adjusted with herbs to the consumer's preference. By filleting the fish, the product has become consumer-friendly; they just have to fry the fish fillets to eat them. African consumers spend less and less time cooking and

are more willing to buy convenience products. With regard to the increasing middle-

## filleting the fish and packaging

class population in Nigeria, I believe that boneless fillets could also be distributed and marketed via supermarkets all over the country. Be aware that by filleting the catfish you will lose 55% of the initial weight. The waste from filleting, such as the catfish heads, can be sold to local markets.

## 11.3 PRICING

Catfish prices vary from selling at cost price to high prices which only a few people are

willing to pay. The real price you will get for your fish will be something in between.

Factors influencing the price of your fish:

Where in the market do you position your product?

Who are your customers? Are they consumers pepper soup joints, supermarkets,

## What are your competitors offering?

Do you have something unique to sell? Or can you differentiate your product or service from other farmers?

## Competitive pricing

The easiest way of pricing is to calculate your cost price and add your percentage on top of it. This system works fine when there is not much competition, because you don't have to consider the pricing of your competitors. The most regular way of pricing your product is

competitive pricing, which strongly relates to prices offered by your competitors.

## Discount pricing

Discount pricing can be useful when you start your business and you want to have a share in the market more quickly. Discount pricing however, is suitable for a period of time but

is not limitless. You can also see it as an introductory price. When you are already in the

business, a discounted price can be given as an incentive for buying large quantities at once or to very loyal customers. Discounts can also be given if customers pay in advance which can be useful if you have cash flow problems.

In general, different prices for individual buyers will give you a lot of problems. Your

customers will not be able to keep their prices secret and you will soon have big arguments. Some farmers think they are smart by keeping the prices the same for everyone, except for a selected group of customers to whom they give away, for example 1 bowl of 25 kg for every 500 kg they buy. Even this cannot work, because the buyers are clever enough to find

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_122.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

11

out the real prices! My advice is to keep the prices the same for everybody except when

you have a good reason, such as higher volumes, advanced payments etcetera.

Non-price factors

Pricing the fish differently or pricing them higher because you want to promote your fish

on non-price factors, such as healthy fish, grown in clean water, good quality fish feed,

## Chapter 11

does not work in the Nigerian market because, as already stated before, the moment the fish are put in a basket, they become anonymous. People don't believe much in these factors, although a significant group of Nigerian consumers believe that catfish from the

wild taste even sweeter than farmed catfish.

## Knowledge of the market

Fish farmers generally do not collaborate. They will never tell their colleague farmer the real sales prices. If they do, they will most likely tell you a higher price than the one they sell at. You start wondering why you

cannot sell at these prices your competitor can! It's obvious, it is because he is selling for a lower price than the price he tells you.

Most farmers have limited knowledge of the market situation. Is the market flooded with fish or is there a shortage? They don't know. The wholesalers take advantage of this situation and quickly buy from farmers who are isolated from the real market situation, telling them the market is dull and fish is barely moving, while in fact the opposite is true! By the time these farmers find out the truth, they have already sold most of their sold most of their tablesized stocks. Figure 31 shows the prices for catfish in 2018 from a farm in Abuja. sized stocks.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_123.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Figure 31. Prices for catfish from a farm in Abuja in 2018.

## Price trend

As you can see in Figure 31, catfish prices fluctuate during the year depending on availability

and demand. Apart from this, inflation also plays apart; normally the price should increase

because of inflation. During the rainy season, the price of fish tends to rise. You will also see this trend in other years. In addition, you can see that fish smaller than 1 kg are always lower priced than bigger fish. That is partly caused by the fact that many farmers sell small

fish because they are not able to produce bigger ones. The most interesting part of this

chart is the price trend shown, not the absolute figures. In Oyo State for instance, the prices shown in the chart will not be possible for farmers, but in the North of Nigeria and in Port Harcourt, they are not only possible but can be even higher.

## 11.4 PROMOTION

The moment you have a product and a price, you start your promotion. Promotion is usually personal and for your product only, but I want to emphasize that promotion of fish

products should also be carried out generally. What does this imply?

Fish products should be positioned in the market as healthy and tasty. The health aspect of fish for older people and also for children should be emphasized via magazines, articles, brochures etcetera. This can be done by umbrella organisations, such as CAFAN and

organisations in the fishing industry. The consumer makes a choice to eat fish or any other

meat product, but will be more likely to decide to buy fish if it is widely promoted. When the demand for fish generally increases as a result of this, it will also increase the demand for catfish. The problem with this kind of promotion however is that everybody involved in the fishing sector should contribute, which is almost impossible to do in the Nigerian

society. Most Nigerians want a free ride. That's why general promotion happens only by

the grace of reporters, books, medical staff, teachers etcetera. It is not coordinated at all.

## Advertise channels

The most common way to promote your own product is by personal communication. This

can be highly effective, but word of mouth promotion is slow going. Also be aware that

positive word of mouth promotion comes by feet, but negative word of mouth promotion

leaves on horseback!

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_124.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

magazines, handbills, flyers and Other advertising channels include radio, newspapers, TV,

posters. The promotional message must be clear, to the point and focused.

When you visit the bigger fish markets in town, you will recognize your potential customers straight away. In some areas, they specialise in smoked fish, and you will notice your potential customers there as well. You can hand out flyers to them or try to convince them to visit your farm to show them your fish.

to big offices Other places to sell fish, are retail shops, road side markets, locations close to big offices and fairs and festivals. It just depends on how inventive you are and how much time you want to spend marketing your fish.

## Delivery of fish

Sales which include delivery can be very tricky, because the moment you arrive at the customer's place, he is the one who is in charge; you want to sell your perishable product, but if he does not mean well, he can take advantage of this. Delivery of fish can only be

done in mutual understanding with the buyer and when you are sure he is a fair business

Chapter 11

man.

Also, be aware that a sale has only been carried out successfully after payment has been fulfilled!



## 12

ECONOMICS OF CATFISH FARMING

12.1 DIRECT COSTS

12.2 INDIRECT COSTS

12.4 FARM SIZE VERSUS PROFITABILITY

<div align="center">

12.1 DIRECT COSTS

</div>

Expenses for fish feed and juveniles are direct costs because they are directly related to

the fish production.

As already stated in chapter 7, fish feed represents the biggest part of the costs to produce catfish. Depending on the system and efficiency of the farm, it can increase to 75% of the cost price. The higher the percentage, the better it is, taken in consideration that the

feeding and the feed quality are okay. At large farms with a high production the percentage

is high, while at small farms the percentage is low. The overheads, which are indirect costs, are relatively higher for smaller farms than for larger farms. That is the advantage of scaling up production. For example, a farm producing 20 tons of fish a year is able to increase the production to 50 tons a year, while the costs for manpower, security, light etcetera will not

increase 2.5 times. These costs will increase less than that.

20/piece. Mortality rate from juvenile to table size: 20% due to cannibalism, diseases, birds etcetera.

When you buy good quality juveniles and grow them to table size, you will still lose 20% due to mortality, mainly at the beginning of the growth cycle. So, if you sell them at 1 kg average, you 'll need to purchase 1.25 juvenile for each kg. If the cost price for juveniles

is 20/piece, your cost for juveniles to produce 1 kg fish, will be $ 20 \times 1.25 = \mathbb{N} \ 25/\mathrm{kg}.

When you produce fish for smoking and selling them at 500 g, you will need 2.5 juvenile

for each kg of smoked fish produced. The cost will be $ 2.5 \times \mathbb{N} \ 20 = \mathbb{N} \ 50/\mathrm{kg}.

As you can see, the size you sell your fish at, matters a lot when it comes to the number of juveniles you need and the cost of juveniles per kg of table-sized fish. To make it even

more complicated, the feed conversion rate also changes with the selling size. Big fish

Economics of catfish farming

have a higher FCR than smaller fish. Another factor which varies, is the selling price for the different sizes of fish. Normally bigger fish will fetch a

<div align="center">

higher price per kg. The FCR varies from 1 for 500 g fish, to 1.38 for 2000 g fish (Figure 33).

From the figures of a farm in Abuja, shown in Figure 33, you can conclude form the gross margin that the selling size of 1.5 kg is most profitable. However, there are other factors which have to be taken into consideration; for instance, the market demand for this fish

size. Actually, the farm in Abuja is targeting at 1.5 kg fish because the competition with

local small farmers is less for bigger fish sizes than for sizes of 1 kg or less. Many farmers

don't have the financial capacity to grow bigger sized fish.

## 12.2 INDIRECT COSTS

Indirect costs are costs that are not directly accountable for the production of fish. These costs are less variable and can even be fixed. Such costs are:

Administration

Security

In principle, the direct costs for all the farms are the same, while the indirect costs vary a

lot from farm to farm. The location, the facilities and the capacity of the farm matter a lot.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_125.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

Energy Marketing Labour

## Chapter 12

For instance, do you have a steady access to the supply of PHCN or does your farm run on a generator most of the time? Is the accessibility of your farm good enough when it comes to marketing, transport and even the sales price of the fish? Has the farm been built with

good materials or has it been constructed in an inferior way which results in the need for a

lot of maintenance? Do you have good staff and a high level of integrity on the farm? Do

you fund your farm with a bank loan or with your own money?

## 12.3 CALCULATION OF BREAK-EVEN POINT

Each farmer should know the minimum production capacity of his farm needed to pay back its running costs. The remaining profit is for refunding the investment and paying the interest if applicable. It is very important to know the break-even point. The following

example and Figure 34 show how this is calculated.

Example 26. How to calculate the break-even point?

The farm has a capacity of 100 tons per annum and the fish are sold at the average

price of N 720/kg. The direct costs (see Figure 33) are N 480/kg. Gross margin = 720

-480=N240/kg.

The following indirect costs per annum are applicable per annum and estimated in

Energy-2, 600, 000

Marketing-1, 000, 000

Interest (financed through own resources)

Maintenance-500, 000

Miscellaneous-500, 000

10 ton/annum

31.7 ton/annum

Total: N7, 600, 000.

The break-even point represents the amount of production that is necessary to pay for the running cost of 7, 600, 000: 7, 600, 000/240 $ /kg = 31, 666 kg.

## Economics of catfish farming

## Prices for catfish during the year

The prices for catfish fluctuate during the year depending on availability and demand. Apart from this, inflation plays a part. Normally the price should increase because of it. During the rainy season, the price of fish tends to increase. This is an annual trend.

You can derive from Figure 31 in chapter 11, that fish smaller than 1 kg are always sold

at a lower price. This is partly due to the fact that many farmers sell small fish and few

7600, 000 Figure 34. Calculation of profits in relationship to the amount of production.

When you put the figures in an Excel sheet you can play with them by changing the, 7600, 000 selling price, the FCR, the feed price or the labour cost. You will immediately see the changes in gross profit and net profit of the farm. Also, the break-even point will change.

The example shown in Figure 34 comes from a financially healthy farm; even when the

farm produces only 31% of its production capacity, it will not yield a negative cash flow which means that the farm can be maintained. The problems start when a farm has to produce close to the maximum capacity to break-even, because then the net margin will be very low.

For several reasons the profitability of farms varies not only a lot between farms of the same size but also between small, medium and large farms. First let us categorise the sizes of farms.

Small farms: less than 10, 000 kg per annum

Small farms are usually farms producing less than 10, 000 kg per annum and are mostly backyard farms or cluster farms. The definition of backyard farms has already been given in

chapter 4, but in short it's a farm which combines a household with a little fish farm in the

backyard. A cluster farm is a group of farms situated in a water logged area run by many

individuals who share the responsibility for security, roads, market etcetera.

Medium sized farms: less than 100, 000 kg per annum

Medium sized farms are usually situated on the outskirts of a big town where the owner

lives.

Large farms: over 100, 000 kg per annum

Large farms are usually located in areas where there is enough space and water to facilitate

a massive production of fish. The owner can live anywhere in Nigeria or even outside

## Nigeria.

Statistics about the number of farms in Nigeria and their productions are either not available or not reliable, but I believe that Nigeria has over 100, 000 small-scale farms while there are

up to 20, 000 medium sized and up to 300 large farms.

Differences in profitability

The capacity of the farm and its actual production are in most cases not in line with each other.

The medium sized farms especially claim large production capacities but some of them produce

even less than 10% of their capacity and they should in fact be categorised as small-scale

farms, but without the benefits of a small farm.

The small sized and the medium sized farms especially show very big differences in profitability within their categories. At large farms the way of farming has been harmonised to the best

farming practice and therefore the range in profitability between these farms is not as much as

in the other categories. Large farms are large for a reason: they do well and have the correct

Medium sized farms face the biggest problems in my opinion. The ambition of medium sized

infrastructure and a good market.

farms is bigger than what they can handle. Most of the time they face lack of good management

and security, lack of finance and lack of good infrastructure, such as the availability of water. They are too small to hire good staff and are not able to build good infrastructure. Finally, the set-up of a medium sized farm is too big for the farmer to handle. Most of the time the locations where the farms are situated, are too far away for proper supervision and therefore

206

the farms are only checked at the weekend, in the evening or by phone.

Economics of catfish farming

The smaller farm's set up is not ambitious but smart; they don't pretend to make a lot of money but at least the majority of them make a profit. The quantities of fish produced can even be sold to retailers and these farms will get a better average price than the medium

sized farmers. Drop outs are usually found in the category of the medium sized farms.

The fact that Nigeria is the biggest fish farming nation on the continent, apart from Egypt, is not because we farm any better, it is because of the mentality of Nigerians; Nigerians don't shy away from risks, have entrepreneurial skills and don't give up easily. Soldier go,

soldier come, barrack remains the same!

## 13

INTEGRATED FISH FARMING

13.1 INTRODUCTION

13.2 3 METHODS OF INTEGRATED FISH FARMING

13.3 CATFISH AND CHICKEN SLAUGHTER WASTE

13.4 USING FISH EFFLUENT FOR IRRIGATION PURPOSES

13.6 COMBINING RICE AND CATFISH FARMING

## 13.1 INTRODUCTION

A farm in the middle of Ibadan, used recirculation systems and had a big settling

tank for the waste water in order to keep the gutters and the public drainage

system free from its solids. Each year the sludge from this tank was used for the polo felds as a preparation for the polo tournament in January. A big tanker was used to transport the sludge and distribute it over the polo feld. However, the horses were so happy with the abundance of grass on the feld that they refused to

run but instead enjoyed the grazing!!

Integrated fish farming is a system of fish production in combination with other agricultural/livestock farming operations close to the fish pond. The farming sub-systems, for instance fish, crop and livestock, are linked to each other in such a way that the byproducts and wastes from one sub-system become valuable inputs for another sub-

system and thus ensures total utilization of the land and water resources

of the farm, resulting in a maximum and diversified farm output on minimum overheads and labour

costs.

13.2 3 METHODS OF INTEGRATED FISH FARMING

1. The waste (water and nutrients) of the fish are collected and become a source of

nutrients and water for rearing crops.

2. The waste from live stocks or crops is given to the fish pond where it becomes

a direct feed source, for instance chicken intestines and faeces, or it becomes a

fertiliser to enhance the growth of algae and zooplankton which will also be a

source of fish feed.

3. A combination of the first 2 options.

In Nigeria integrated fish farming is rare, but in Asia, for the small-scale farmer especially, it's a beneficial way of farming and therefore popular. Farmers use the manure of live-it's a beneficial way of

farming and therefore popular. Farmers use the manure of live- stock, such as cattle, chickens or pigs, to fertilise the water; in some cases, the pen of the animals is situated above the fish ponds and the droppings fall directly into the pond. The

ponds are also relatively big: 0.5 to 1.0 ha. The fish species used in this type of farming

are tilapia and several species of carp, either in monoculture or in polyculture. These fish directly consume a little part of the manure but in general the natural production of the fish pond is increased because the manure fertilises the water. The natural food for the fish is algae, zooplankton and benthos.

natural production as other fish species do, because they are carnivorous and not omnivorous or herbivorous, such as

Integrated fish farming

carp and tilapia. Fish production with integrated farming is rather extensive and, in most

cases, not more than 5000 kg per hectare per year. In Nigeria land is too expensive to use it extensively. All farms use complete feed or at least additional feed to grow catfish in densities which allow a production of at least 50, 000 to 100, 000 kg per ha per year.

In Nigeria this type of integrated farming is not popular, because of the fish species we grow. Catfish do not benefit directly from the enhanced

## 13.3 CATFISH AND CHICKEN SLAUGHTER WASTE

Catfish do well on chicken slaughter waste, such as fat, blood, intestines and organs that are not eaten by humans, and aborted eggs. This waste can be put into the pond directly

or it can be processed into a moist pellet with other ingredients and then fed to the catfish.

A farm in Ibadan has been very successful in using chicken slaughter waste directly for the catfish. Their brand is known for extremely big fish! Another farm together with a slaughter house in Lagos, has been very successful with converting chicken waste into a moist pellet for catfish, and using a recirculation system to grow their catfish. They already started this

collaboration by the year 2000. These companies have their own chicken farms, slaughter

houses, freezers and machines and in both cases the slaughter waste is processed close to the fish farm. Chicken waste appears to be a very good feed for catfish. This feed can also be given in combination with ordinary pellets. However, for catfish below 500 g it is not advisable to feed raw chicken slaughter waste.

It is obvious that the water pollution at the farm will be higher with this kind of feed than with a good quality pellet, so chicken waste can only be used if enough water is available to flush the ponds.

If you are a farmer without a slaughter house and you still intend to use slaughter waste,

this could be difficult. Logistics, availability and competition for the raw materials can make it unprofitable to use these products, apart from the effort needed to keep them fresh till feeding time!

13.4 USING FISH EFFLUENT FOR IRRIGATION PURPOSES

In principle the waste water of fish ponds is good for fertilising and watering crops, but it has its restrictions. First of all, the nutrients in the water are available in very low

Chapter 13

Researchers in Sagana Institute in Kenya found out that fish water effluent can contribute at most 20% of the nutrients required. After all, you cannot flood the crops in order to push the nutrients out.

To supply the water to the crops or the orchard is another hassle Normally, a good method is drip irrigation. A small polyethylene hose with small holes 50 cm apart is supplied with effluent under a pressure of only 0.5 bar and dispenses the water in small quantities to the crops efficiently. Also, there will not be much evaporation. The problem

with fish farm effluent though, is that the water has been contaminated with a lot of

bacteria, so called 'living water'. They cause the holes of the drip hose to clog very easily, quickly resulting in a bad water distribution. Therefore,

effluents from fish farms can be used only in an open irrigation system with canals or water sprayers with big holes and lots of pressure.

Another restriction of fish farm effluent is the fact that there is no need for this water

during the rainy season.

## 13.5 HOW FISH EFFLUENT CAN BE USED IN NIGERIA

The fish effluent contains suspended solids, such as faeces, clusters of bacteria and dead algae, which settle rather easily. So, it is advisable to have a settling pond for all the drainage water of the farm. Let the overflow eventually return to the drainage or river,

because it will be much less contaminated. The sludge can be pumped out of the settling

tank and used to improve the amount of organic matter in the soil and increase its nutrient levels. In many parts of Nigeria, the level is low, because it contains mostly sand. When the sludge is added to the soil, it will become more fertile.

13.6 COMBINING RICE AND CATFISH FARMING

Rice farming has become increasingly popular in Nigeria since the government has

promoted rice culture and banned the import of rice. This offers the opportunity to

combine rice and fish culture; this way not only carbohydrates are produced, but also the so much needed proteins. This type of farming is very popular in Asia and we can learn from them. Already many trials are conducted in Nigeria. In most cases the combination of rice and fish is more profitable than rice or fish separately.

212

Fish culture in rice fields can be done in 2 ways:

Integrated fish farming

1. Simultaneous culture: both at the same time

## Simultaneous culture

2. Rotation culture: one after the other

Simultaneous culture of rice and fish can best be carried out in rice fields of 0.1 ha divided into 4

subplots of 10 x 25 m. Between each plot there is a ditch 0.75 m wide and 0.5 m deep. Around the plots there are dykes 0.3 m wide and 0.3 m high. Each field has an inlet and outlet both with

screens, in order to keep the water at the right level and avoid fish coming in or going out. The

ditches are shelters for the fish where they can hide when they are not foraging between the rice plants. When it is time to harvest, the water level is reduced so that the fish can only remain in the ditches and are relatively easy to catch.

Many fish species can be cultured in rice fields. They should be specifically tolerant to high water

temperatures (35 $ ^{\circ} \mathrm{C} $), low oxygen levels and high turbidity. In Asia the most common species to be cultured in combination with rice are Asian carp, rohu, common carp, milkfish and catfish species. The African catfish can also be cultured in rice fields, since it tolerates these conditions. species.

## Procedure

Five days after the rice seedlings have been transplanted from the nursery site to the pond, catfish juveniles are stocked at a ratio of 4000 per ha and are given supplemental feeding. The fish can grow during the entire period the rice is growing. Approximately 120 days are needed to grow rice from seedling to harvest. In this period the fish can grow up to 500 g (smoking

size); depending on the quantity and quality of the

## supplements fed, the fish might be smaller

or bigger.

Advantages of simultaneous culture:

The fish increase the rice yield by 5 to 15%, mainly due to indirect organic

fertilisation through the fish excrements. If stocked with tilapia, the tilapia will eat algae which otherwise would compete with the rice for nutrients.

Insect pests of rice, like stem borers, are controlled by fish that feed on them, which are in particular catfish.

Fish also feed on the mosquito larvae which are intermediate hosts for malaria

and other waterborne diseases. This way they reduce the risk for human beings

becoming infected by one of these diseases.

<div style='text-align: center;'><img src='images/img_128.png' alt='OCR图片'/></div>

The major limitations when cultivating rice and fish simultaneously, are the use of

agrochemicals to control weeds and insects. Most of those agrochemicals are toxic for fish.

can use the herbicides and pesticides needed to control weeds and pests. And, during the culture of fish, you can have a higher water level which is more favourable for the catfish. The sludge at the bottom of the pond is an excellent fertilizer for rice.

## APPENDIX 1

Fish farm growth stages of catfish from fertilization to selling

Fertilised egg: the egg after successful fertilization.

Yolk sac fry: the larval stage of fish which has just hatched and feeds on and feeds on its yolk sac for approximately 2 days.

Free swimming fry: fry that swim up in search of food. This a one day's growth stage,

also called 'swim up-fry'.

Advanced fry: the period after the free-swimming fry up to 21 days.

Fingerling: a fry that starts to use its organ to breath oxygen from the air. The moment fry are able to do this, they are called fingerlings. This growth stage lasts until they are 6 weeks old and weigh less than 1 g.

Juvenile: a catfish from 1 g to 10 gJuvenile: a catfish from 1 g to 10 g

Post-juvenile or jumbo: a catfish from 10 to 50 g.

Grow-out: a catfish from 50 g to selling size.

## APPENDIX 3

Cash flow forecast for a 100 tons per annum production capacity catfish farm selling 2 times a year

This appendix shows you in facts and figures that stocking all the fish at once is not desirable, since you have a very high demand before selling. Apart from this, there are many other reasons not to stock all the fish at the same time:

220

Selling all the fish in one month will be difficult and you cannot actually build a customer base this way.

When things go wrong at the farm; all your fish are at stake! Your standing stock at the point of selling is 2 times higher than when you sell the fish on a monthly

basis.

Your infrastructure should be able to accommodate all these fish at the same time.

The consumption of water and power is at least two times higher than when you are selling on a monthly basis at the point of delivery!

DON'T BE GREEDY; STOCK AT REGULAR INTERVALS AND CONSEQUENTLY ENJOY

REGULAR SALES!

## APPENDIX 7APPENDIX 6

Examples of ranges in feed sizes and their composition

Starter feeds are usually high in proteins with high levels of fish meal and fish oil. Feed conversion rates below 1 are obtainable and can even be as low as 0.6.

<table border="1"><tr><td>Sizes(mm)</td><td>Protein(%)</td><td>Fat(%)</td><td>Crude fibre(%)</td><td>Ash(%)</td><td>Crumbles</td></tr><tr><td>0.2-0.3</td><td>56</td><td>15</td><td>0.1</td><td>12</td><td>sinking</td></tr><tr><td>0.3-0.5</td><td>56</td><td>15</td><td>0.1</td><td>12</td><td>sinking</td></tr><tr><td>0.5-0.8</td><td>56</td><td>15</td><td>0.1</td><td>12</td><td>sinking</td></tr><tr><td>0.8-1.2</td><td>56</td><td>15</td><td>0.1</td><td>12</td><td>sinking</td></tr><tr><td>1.2-1.5</td><td>56</td><td>15</td><td>0.1</td><td>12</td><td>sinking</td></tr></table>

Starter feeds in particle sizes of 1 mm and 1.8 mm can also be produced as mini pellets. 8.8

This will result in feed with less dust.

Pre-grow feeds can be purchased as high performance feed with high levels of proteins and fats or as feed with a lower performance containing lower levels of proteins and fats,

which will result in less growth of the fish and lower feed cost.

<table border="1"><tr><td>Sizes(mm)</td><td>Protein(%)</td><td>Fat(%)</td><td>Crude fibre(%)</td><td>Ash(%)</td><td>Pellet</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>50</td><td>15</td><td>0.7</td><td>8.8</td><td>floating</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>42</td><td>13</td><td>2.3</td><td>6.4</td><td>floating</td></tr></table>

Out-grow feeds are produced in different ranges of quality. They have been given names, such as 'economy feeds', 'essential feeds', 'superior feeds' etcetera. Out-grow feeds are usually floating but you can still buy sinking feeds which are only pelletized, not extruded. Floating feeds are the most in demand on the market.

If you start with a different number of fish you divide the feed gift by 5000 and multiply by the number of fish you have stocked and repeat this calculation for all days. Feeding tables are always an advice and should be a guideline. If the fish cannot eat this amount reduce according to their appetite. be a guideline.
